Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Eight Conditions for Valid Tayammum
Lists and explains the eight conditions for valid dry ablution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the eight conditions for valid tayammum according to the Hanafi school and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding building upon prayer.

Core Idea
Tayammum requires a valid excuse, earth from its genus, complete wiping, two strikes, and removal of barriers.

Tayammum is a dry purification substitute for wudu when water is unavailable or harmful. This lesson unpacks the eight conditions that must be met for tayammum to be valid, as outlined in Nur al-Idah along with commentaries. We will also examine a key dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two companions about using tayammum to continue a prayer that was begun with wudu.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its nature
Recognize that tayammum is a substitute for wudu and is wajib when water is unavailable. Note the eight conditions for its validity.
Tayammum purifies for acts like salah and touching the Quran.
2
Work through each condition
Examine each condition: valid excuse, clean earth from the genus, covering face and hands, wiping with most of the hand, two strikes, cessation of menstruation/postpartum/hadath, removal of barriers.
Pay special attention to what counts as 'genus of earth' – not wood or metals.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on building
Contrast Abu Hanifa's view (tayammum valid for building even if one began with wudu) with the Sahibayn's view (only if one began with tayammum). Identify the practical consequence.
This dispute is about the scope of the 'building' excuse.
4
Distinguish conditions from pillars
The two pillars (rukn) are wiping the face and hands. Conditions are external prerequisites; missing a condition invalidates tayammum, while missing a pillar also invalidates it but is a different category.
Hanafis distinguish shart (external) from rukn (internal).
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a scenario, test each condition and determine if tayammum is valid. For example, a person wipes with two fingers repeatedly.
Use the provided ruling anatomy to check.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شروط صحة التيمم
كتاب الطهارة أو عيد ولو بناءً، وليس من العذر خوف فوت الجمعة والوقت. الثالث: أن يكون التيمم بطاهر من جنس الأرض، كالتراب والحجر والرمل، لا الحطب والفضة والذهب. الرابع: استيعاب المحل بالمسح. الخامس: أن يمسح بجميع اليد أو بأكثرها حتى لو مسح بإصبعين لا يجوز، ولو كرر حتى استوعب، بخلاف مسح الرأس.
وصلية: أي يجوز التيمم لخوف فوت صلاة عيد بتمامها فإن كان بحيث لو توضاً يدرك بعضها مع الإمام لا يتيمم. حاشية الطحطاوي: ۱۱۷] ولو بناء: أي ولو كان يبني بناء جاز له التيمم وصورته: أن يشرع مع الإمام في صلاة العيد، ثم يحدث المقتدي أو الإمام جاز له التيمم للبناء عند أبي حنيفة وقالا إن شرع بطهارة الوضوء لا يجوز له التيمم، وإن شرع بالتيمم جاز له البناء به تبيين الحقائق: ۱۳۲/۱] وليس من العذر إلخ: أي إذا خاف فوت الجمعة إلى أن يتوضأ لها، أو خاف خروج الوقت في سائر الأوقات إلى أن يشتغل بالطهارة لا يجوز له التيمم بل يتوضأ؛ لأنها تفوت إلى بدل والفوات إلى بدل كلا فوات [تبيين الحقائق: ١٣٢/١] بطاهر: أي طيب، وهو الذي لم تمسه نجاسة، ولو زالت بذهاب أثرها. [مراقي الفلاح: ۱۱۸] من جنس الأرض: اعلم أن الفاصل بين جنس الأرض وغيره: أن كل شيء يحترق بالنار ويصير رماداً ليس من جنس الأرض، وكذا كل شيء ينطبع ويذوب بالنار ، وكل شيء تأكله الأرض ليس من جنسها. (زيلعي بتصرف) لا الحطب إلخ أي لا يصح التيمم لنحو الحطب إلخ، وههنا لطيفة، وهي أن الله تعالى خلق درة ونظر إليها فصارت ماء، ثم تكاثف منه فصار تراباً، وتلطف منه فصار هواء، وتلطف منه فصار ناراً، فكان الماء أصلاً، ذكره المفسرون، وهو منقول عن التوراة، فإذا تعذر الطهارة بالأصل انتقل إلى التبع وأقيم مقامه، والنبات كالشجر ونحوه والمعدني كالحديد وشبهه ليس بتبع للماء وحده حتى يقوم مقامه، ولا للتراب كذلك، وإنما هو مركب من العناصر الأربعة، فليس له اختصاص بشيء منها حتى تقوم مقامه. (العناية) استيعاب المحل إلخ [وهو الوجه واليدان إلى المرفقين] اعلم أن الاستيعاب شرط في ظاهر الرواية حتى يحرك الرجل خاتمه، والمرأة سوارها، أو ينزعانهما، ويخلل الأصابع ويمسح جميع بشرة الوجه والشعر على الصحيح، وما بين العذار والأذن إلحاقا له بأصله، وقيل: يكفي مسح أكثر الوجه واليدين. [مراقي الفلاح: ١٢٠] أو بأكثرها أو بما يقوم مقامها كيد غيره. لا يجوز لفقد كون المسح بجميع اليد أو بأكثرها. ولو كرر إلخ أي لا يجوز التيمم ولو كرر المسح بإصبعين حتى استوعب الوجه واليدين؛ لفقد الشرط المذكور من كون المسح بجميع اليد أو بأكثرها. بخلاف مسح الرأس : أي حكم مسح الرأس مخالف للتيمم، فإنه لو مسح الرأس بإصبعين جاز مسحه، ولا كذلك التيمم.
كتاب الطهارة
السادس: أن يكون بضربتين بباطن الكفين ولو في مكان واحد، ويقوم مقام الضربتين إصابة التراب بجسده إذا مسحه بنية التيمم. السابع: انقطاع ما ينافيه من حيض أو نفاس، أو حدث. الثامن: زوال ما يمنع المسح كشمع وشحم. وسببه وشروط وجوبه كما ذكر في الوضوء وركناه مسح اليدين، والوجه.
Conditions for the validity of tayammum: first: that it be for an excuse, or for Eid prayer, and even if building upon prayer, and fear of missing Friday prayer and time is not an excuse. Third: that tayammum be with clean [earth] from the genus of earth, like dust, stone, and sand, not wood, silver, and gold. Fourth: covering the place with wiping. Fifth: that he wipe with all of the hand or most of it, so that if he wipes with two fingers, it is not permissible, even if he repeats until he covers, unlike wiping the head. Commentary: 'or Eid' means it is permissible to perform tayammum due to fear of missing the entire Eid prayer; if he would catch some of it with the imam by performing wudu, he does not perform tayammum. 'Even if building' means even if he is building upon prayer, it is permissible for him to perform tayammum; its form is that he begins with the imam in Eid prayer, then the follower or imam has an event, it is permissible for him to perform tayammum for building according to Abu Hanifa, and the two companions said if he began with wudu, tayammum is not permissible, but if he began with tayammum, building upon it is permissible. 'Fear of missing Friday prayer' etc.: if he fears missing Friday prayer while he would perform wudu, or fears the time leaving in other times while he would engage in purification, tayammum is not permissible; rather he performs wudu, because these [prayers] are missed for a substitute, and missing for a substitute is like not missing. 'With clean': i.e., pure, which is not touched by impurity, even if it is removed by its trace disappearing. 'From the genus of earth': know that the separator between the genus of earth and other things is that everything that burns with fire and turns to ash is not from the genus of earth, likewise everything that melts with fire, and everything that the earth consumes is not from its genus. 'Not wood' etc.: i.e., tayammum is not valid with wood etc. And here is a subtle point: that Allah created a pearl and looked at it, so it became water, then from it condensed so it became dust, and from it became delicate so it became air, and from it became delicate so it became fire; so water was the origin. The commentators mentioned this, and it is transmitted from the Torah. So when purification by the origin is prevented, one transfers to the dependent and it is placed in its place. Plants like trees etc. and minerals like iron etc. are not dependent on water alone to take its place, nor on dust alone; rather they are composed of the four elements, so they have no special relation to any of them to take its place. 'Covering the place' etc. [which is the face and hands to the elbows]: know that covering is a condition in the apparent transmission, so that a man moves his ring, and a woman her bracelet, or they remove them, and he passes his fingers through his fingers, and wipes all the skin of the face and hair according to the correct view, and what is between the ear and the cheek is attached to its origin; and it is said: wiping most of the face and hands suffices. 'Or most of it' or what stands in its place like the hand of another. It is not permissible due to the lack of the condition of wiping with all the hand or most of it. 'Even if he repeats' etc.: i.e., tayammum is not permissible even if he repeats wiping with two fingers until he covers the face and hands, due to the lack of the mentioned condition of wiping with all the hand or most of it. Unlike wiping the head: i.e., the ruling of wiping the head is contrary to tayammum, for if he wipes the head with two fingers, his wiping is permissible, but not so in tayammum. Sixth: that it be with two strikes with the inner part of the palms, even if in one place, and hitting dust with his body stands in place of the two strikes if he wipes it with the intention of tayammum. Seventh: cessation of what contradicts it, like menstruation, post-partum bleeding, or ritual impurity. Eighth: removal of what prevents wiping, like wax or fat. And its cause and conditions of obligation are as mentioned in wudu, and its two pillars are wiping the hands and the face.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage lists the eight conditions (shurut) for the validity of tayammum, along with detailed commentary from Hanafi works. The first condition concerns the excuse ('udhr); tayammum is permitted for fear of missing an entire Eid prayer, and also for building upon a prayer (e.g., if one's wudu breaks during Eid prayer, one may make tayammum to continue, according to Abu Hanifa, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad restrict this to those who began with tayammum). However, fear of missing Friday prayer or the time of a prayer is not an excuse; one must perform wudu even if it means missing the prayer, because the prayer is only missed for a substitute. The second condition (implied) is that the earth be clean (tahir), meaning not contaminated by impurity. The third condition requires that the medium be from the genus of earth (jins al-ard), such as dust, stone, or sand, but not wood, metals, or other materials that burn or melt. The commentary explains the distinction: anything that burns to ash or melts is not from earth. A subtle point is made about the creation of the elements, with water as the origin, and that plants and minerals are composite and not solely dependent on water or earth. The fourth condition is complete coverage of the area to be wiped (face and hands to elbows). The fifth condition requires wiping with the whole hand or most of it; wiping with only two fingers is insufficient even if repeated, unlike wiping the head in wudu where two fingers suffice. The sixth condition requires two strikes of the hands on the earth, even in one place, and if dust hits the body it can substitute. The seventh condition requires that menstruation, postpartum bleeding, or ritual impurity be absent at the time of performance. The eighth condition requires removing any barrier like wax or fat that prevents direct contact. The passage concludes with the cause (sabab) of tayammum being the intention to perform an act requiring purity, and its conditions of obligation are the same as for wudu (eight conditions: maturity, sanity, Islam, existence of hadath, absence of menstruation and postpartum, narrowness of time, and ability to perform tayammum). The two pillars (rukn) of tayammum are wiping the face and the hands.

Key Terms
الشرط (al-shart): A condition for validity; if missing, the act is invalid.
جنس الأرض (jins al-ard): The genus of earth, including dust, sand, stone, but not materials that burn or melt.
ضربتين (darbatayn): Two strikes of the hands on the earth, required for tayammum in the apparent transmission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling if a person wipes his face and hands in tayammum using two fingers repeatedly until coverage?
A) Valid, because coverage is achieved.
B) Invalid, because the condition requires wiping with the whole hand or most of it, not two fingers.
C) Valid, if he repeats it three times.
D) Invalid, because two fingers are never sufficient in tayammum.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum has eight specific conditions; the most nuanced are the definition of 'earth genus' and the dispute on building upon prayer.

The Seven Sunnahs of Tayammum
Lists and explains the seven sunnahs with commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the seven sunnahs of tayammum, explain the Hanafi position on the number of strikes, and identify when delaying tayammum is recommended.

Core Idea
Seven sunnahs complete tayammum; omission reduces reward but not validity.

Tayammum, the dry ablution substitute for wudu, has recommended acts that enhance its perfection. This lesson unpacks the seven sunnahs listed in the Hanafi text, along with key clarifications on the number of strikes, the intra-Hanafi dispute about the status of the strike, and the condition for delaying tayammum. Understanding these sunnahs helps distinguish between the obligatory pillars and the commendable practices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Seven Sunnahs
Read through the list: saying Bismillah, order (tartib), continuity (muwalah), bringing hands forward and back after placing in dust, shaking them off, spreading fingers, and delaying tayammum for one hoping for water before time expires.
These are sunnah muakkadah; omitting them does not invalidate tayammum.
2
Examine the Dispute on Strikes
The commentary addresses whether two strikes in the same place are valid. The soundest view (al-ashahh) permits it because the place does not become 'used'—tayammum is on the hands. Also note the dispute between al-Isbijabi and Shams al-A'imma on the ruling if hadath occurs after the strike but before wiping.
This highlights the question of whether the strike is a rukn or a means.
3
Understand the Delay of Tayammum
Delaying tayammum is recommended only for one who is legally without water (faqid shari'an) and hopes to find water before the time ends. If water is within a mile, tayammum is not permitted.
Restricted to those with realistic hope, not everyone without water.
4
Note the Pillars and Conditions
The commentary lists the pillars (wiping face and hands to elbows) and conditions of obligation (intellect, maturity, Islam, hadath, absence of menstruation/postpartum, narrow time, ability). These are the same as for wudu.
These are not sunnah but essential for validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسنن التيمم سبعة : التسمية في أوله ،والترتيب والموالاة وإقبال اليدين بعد وضعهما في التراب وإدبارهما، ونفضهما، وتفريج الأصابع، وندب تأخير التيمم لمن يرجو الماء قبل خروج الوقت. حالة الضرب: ولو في مكان إلخ أي ولو كان الضربتان في مكان واحد وهذا على الأصح من المذهب لعدم صيرورة المكان مستعملاً؛ لأن التيمم بما في اليد. ويقوم مقام الضربتين إلخ حتى لو أحدث بعد الضرب أو أصابه التراب، فمسحه يجوز على ما قاله الإسبيجابي كمن أحدث وفي كفيه ما يجوز به الطهارة، وعلى ما اختاره شمس الأئمة لا يجوز؛ لجعله الضرب ركناً كما لو أحدث بعد غسل عضو مراقي الفلاح: ۱۲۱] السابع: وهذا الشرط لصحة الوضوء أيضا. كشمع: لأنه يصير به المسح عليه لا على الجسد. [مراقي الفلاح: ۱۲۱] وسببه أي سبب التيمم إرادة ما لا يحل إلا بالطهارة. [مراقي الفلاح: ۱۲۱] كما ذكر في الوضوء وهي ثمانية: العقل والبلوغ، والإسلام، ووجود الحدث، وعدم الحيض، والنفاس، وضيق الوقت والقدرة على ما يجوز منه التيمم. حاشية الطحطاوي: ۱۲۱] وركناه [تثنية ركن سقط نونها للإضافة. وكيفيته أن يضرب بيديه على الأرض، يقبل بهما ويدبر ثم يرفعهما وينفضهما، ويمسح بهما بحيث لا يبقى منه شيء، ويمسح الوترة التي بين المنخرين ثم يضرب بيديه على الأرض كذلك، ذراعيه إلى المرفقين تبيين الحقائق: ۱۲۱/۱] ويمسح وجهه بهما مسح اليدين: لم يقل: ضربتان؛ لما علمته من من كون الضرب من مسمى التيمم. [مراقي الفلاح: ١٢١] ونفضهما: أي تحريكهما ليزول عنهما الغبار. تأخير التيمم أطلق التأخير وهو مقيد بمن هو فاقد الماء شرعاً في ظاهر الرواية، فإنه إذا كان يظن أن بعد الماء أقل من ميل لا يباح له التيمم؛ لأنه وإن كان عادم الماء بالفعل لكنه ليس بفاقد شرعاً. لمن يرجو أفاد بالتقييد أنه إذا لم يكن على طمع من وجود الماء في الوقت لا يستحب أن يؤخر، ويتيمم ويصلي في الوقت المستحب . [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٢٢]
And the sunnahs of tayammum are seven: saying the Basmalah at its beginning, order, continuity, bringing the hands forward after placing them in the dust and drawing them back, shaking them off, spreading the fingers, and it is recommended to delay tayammum for one who hopes for water before the time exits. Commentary: 'even if the two strikes are in one place' is the soundest view in the school, because the place does not become used; since tayammum is with what is in the hand. 'And hitting dust on his body stands in place of the two strikes' so that even if he has an event after the strike or the dust hits him, then wiping is permissible according to al-Isbijabi, like one who has an event while there is in his palms what suffices for purification; and according to what Shams al-A'imma chose, it is not permissible, because he considers the strike a pillar, like if he had an event after washing a limb. The seventh: and this condition is also for the validity of wudu. 'Like wax': because by it the wiping is on it, not on the body. And its cause: meaning the cause of tayammum is the intention of what is not permissible except with purification. As mentioned in wudu, and they are eight: intellect, maturity, Islam, existence of hadath, absence of menstruation, postpartum bleeding, narrowness of time, and ability to perform tayammum. And its two pillars (the dual of rukn, its nun dropped due to idafa). And its modality: that he strikes his hands on the earth, bringing them forward and back, then lifts them and shakes them, and wipes with them such that nothing remains, and wipes the bridge between the nostrils, then strikes his hands on the earth likewise, his arms to the elbows, and wipes his face with them. 'Wiping the hands': it was not said two strikes; because you know that striking is part of the meaning of tayammum. 'Shaking them': meaning moving them to remove the dust. 'Delaying tayammum' – the delay is unrestrictedly mentioned but is restricted to one who is legally without water in the apparent transmission; if he thinks that water is less than a mile away, tayammum is not permitted for him, because although he is actually without water, he is not legally without it. 'For one who hopes' – the qualification indicates that if he has no hope of finding water within the time, it is not recommended to delay; rather he should perform tayammum and pray in the preferred time.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage lists the seven sunnah acts of tayammum. These are: saying Bismillah at the start, performing the actions in order (first face then hands), performing them consecutively without a long gap, bringing the hands forward and backward after placing them in the dust, shaking off the dust, spreading the fingers, and it is recommended to delay tayammum if one hopes to find water before the end of the prayer time. However, this delay is only for those who are legally without water (faqid al-ma' shari'an); if one thinks water is within a mile, tayammum is not permitted. The commentary also clarifies that striking the hands twice is the relied-upon view, and if one strikes in the same spot both times, it is valid because the spot does not become 'used'—the tayammum is on the hands, not the ground. An intra-Hanafi dispute is noted: if one has an event (hadath) after striking but before wiping, al-Isbijabi rules that the tayammum is still valid because the hands have the dust, while Shams al-A'imma considers the strike a pillar, so the tayammum would be invalid. The cause (sabab) of tayammum is the intention to perform an act requiring purification, and the conditions of obligation (shurut al-wujub) are the same as for wudu: sanity, maturity, Islam, presence of hadath, absence of menstruation and postpartum bleeding, narrowness of time, and ability to perform tayammum. The two pillars (rukn) are wiping the face and the hands to the elbows. The commentary describes the actual method: strike the hands on the earth, bring them forward and back, shake them, wipe the face, then wipe the hands to the elbows, and also wipe the bridge of the nose. Finally, the text notes that wiping the hands is not called 'two strikes' because striking is part of the definition of tayammum.

Key Terms
السنة (al-sunnah): A recommended act in tayammum; omission does not invalidate but is rewarded if done.
الترتيب (al-tartib): Order: performing the wiping of the face before the hands.
الموالاة (al-muwalah): Continuity: performing the actions without a significant break between them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, when is it recommended to delay tayammum?
A) For everyone who is without water.
B) Only for one who hopes to find water before the time ends and is legally without water.
C) Only for travelers.
D) It is never recommended to delay.

Key Takeaway
The seven sunnahs of tayammum enhance the act; omitting them loses reward but not validity, and the delay is only for those with a realistic hope of finding water.

Taharah — Purification

Sunan and Conditions of Tayammum
List of conditions, pillars, and sunan of tayammum with internal Hanafi disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the eight conditions of obligation, the two pillars, and the seven sunan of tayammum, and explain the Hanafi position on the number of strikes and the ruling on delaying tayammum.

Core Idea
Tayammum has specific conditions, pillars, and sunan; the Hanafi school requires two strikes and recommends delay only for those legally without water.

This lesson examines the legal details of tayammum as presented in Nur al-Idah and its commentaries. Tayammum is a dry purification substitute for wudu and ghusl when water is unavailable or prohibited. Understanding its conditions, pillars, and sunan is essential for valid worship. The text also reveals internal Hanafi differences regarding the number of strikes and the recommendation to delay tayammum when hoping for water.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal classification
Determine that tayammum is wajib (obligatory) when conditions are met. It substitutes for both wudu and ghusl.
Hanafi: tayammum is wajib; Shafi'i considers it mubah.
2
Distinguish cause, conditions, pillars, and sunan
Understand the hierarchy: sabab (cause) → shurut wujub (conditions of obligation) → shurut sihha (conditions of validity) → arkan (pillars) → sunan (recommended acts).
The passage lists cause, conditions, pillars, and sunan in separate sections.
3
List the eight conditions of obligation
Memorize: sanity, puberty, Islam, existence of hadath, absence of hayd and nifas, lack of time, ability to perform tayammum, and legal inability to use water (faqid al-ma' shar'an).
These mirror the conditions for wudu, adjusted for tayammum.
4
Identify the two pillars
The pillars are wiping the face and wiping the hands (including forearms). These are essential; omitting one invalidates tayammum.
The passage mentions 'wiping the hands and the face' as pillars.
5
Enumerate the seven sunan
Recite: (1) saying Bismillah, (2) order (face before hands), (3) continuity, (4) bringing hands forward and backward in dust, (5) shaking hands to remove excess dust, (6) spreading fingers, (7) delaying tayammum for one who hopes for water before the recommended time expires.
The seventh sunnah is conditional on hoping for water.
6
Understand the internal Hanafi dispute
Two points of ikhtilaf: (a) number of strikes – al-Ispijabi accepts one strike if dust on body, Shams al-A'imma requires two; (b) delaying tayammum – Abu Hanifa says it is recommended, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it is obligatory if water is promised.
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is two strikes and recommended delay for the legally waterless.
7
Apply the condition of legal waterlessness
The delay of tayammum is only for one who is faqid al-ma' shar'an. If water is less than a mile away, tayammum is not permitted even if one is physically without water at the moment.
The passage restricts the absolute statement of delay to this category.

كتاب الطهارة ٤٤ سنن التيمم السادس: أن يكون بضربتين بباطن الكفين ولو في مكان واحد، ويقوم مقام الضربتين إصابة التراب بجسده إذا مسحه بنية التيمم. السابع: انقطاع ما ينافيه من حيض أو نفاس، أو حدث. الثامن: زوال ما يمنع المسح كشمع وشحم. وسببه وشروط وجوبه كما ذكر في الوضوء وركناه مسح اليدين، والوجه. ثمانية خير مبتدأ وسنن التيمم سبعة : التسمية في أوله ،والترتيب والموالاة وإقبال اليدين بعد وضعهما في التراب وإدبارهما، ونفضهما، وتفريج الأصابع، وندب تأخير التيمم لمن يرجو الماء قبل خروج الوقت. يعني ولو في مكان إلخ أي ولو كان الضربتان في مكان واحد وهذا على الأصح من المذهب لعدم صيرورة المكان مستعملاً؛ لأن التيمم بما في اليد. ويقوم مقام الضربتين إلخ حتى لو أحدث بعد الضرب أو أصابه التراب، فمسحه يجوز على ما قاله الإسبيجابي كمن أحدث وفي كفيه ما يجوز به الطهارة، وعلى ما اختاره شمس الأئمة لا يجوز؛ لجعله الضرب ركناً كما لو أحدث بعد غسل عضو مراقي الفلاح: ١٢١] السابع: وهذا الشرط لصحة الوضوء أيضا. كشمع: لأنه يصير به المسح عليه لا على الجسد. [مراقي الفلاح: ۱۲۱] وسببه أي سبب التيمم إرادة ما لا يحل إلا بالطهارة. [مراقي الفلاح: ١٢١] كما ذكر في الوضوء وهي ثمانية: العقل والبلوغ، والإسلام، ووجود الحدث، وعدم الحيض، والنفاس، وضيق الوقت والقدرة على ما يجوز منه التيمم. حاشية الطحطاوي: ۱۲۱] وركناه [تثنية ركن سقط نونها للإضافة. وكيفيته أن يضرب بيديه على الأرض، يقبل بهما ويدبر ثم يرفعهما وينفضهما، ويمسح بهما بحيث لا يبقى منه شيء، ويمسح الوترة التي بين المنخرين ثم يضرب بيديه على الأرض كذلك، ذراعيه إلى المرفقين تبيين الحقائق: ۱۲۱/۱] الخلاف ويمسح وجهه بهما مسح اليدين: لم يقل: ضربتان؛ لما علمته من من كون الضرب من مسمى التيمم. [مراقي الفلاح: ١٢١] ونفضهما: أي تحريكهما ليزول عنهما الغبار. تأخير التيمم أطلق التأخير وهو مقيد بمن هو فاقد الماء شرعاً في ظاهر الرواية، فإنه إذا كان يظن أن بعد الماء أقل من ميل لا يباح له التيمم؛ لأنه وإن كان عادم الماء بالفعل لكنه ليس بفاقد شرعاً. لمن يرجو أفاد بالتقييد أنه إذا لم يكن على طمع من وجود الماء في الوقت لا يستحب أن يؤخر، ويتيمم ويصلي في الوقت المستحب . [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٢٢]
The Book of Purification. 44. The Sunnas of Tayammum: Sixth: That it be with two strikes on the inner palms, even if in one place, and the hitting of dust on one's body when wiping with the intention of tayammum takes the place of the two strikes. Seventh: The cessation of what contradicts it, like menstruation, postpartum bleeding, or hadath (ritual impurity). Eighth: The removal of what prevents wiping, like wax or fat. Its cause and conditions of obligation are as mentioned in wudu, and its pillars are wiping the hands and the face. Eight... and the Sunnas of tayammum are seven: saying Bismillah at its start, order, continuity, bringing the hands forward after placing them in the dust and drawing them back, shaking them off, spreading the fingers, and it is recommended to delay tayammum for one who hopes for water before the time expires. He said: 'even if in one place' means even if the two strikes are in one place, and this is the most correct in the madhhab because the place does not become used (musta'mal); for tayammum is by what is on the hands. 'And takes the place of the two strikes' etc., so if one nullifies after the strike or dust hits him, then his wipe is permissible according to al-Ispijabi, like one who nullifies while on his palms is what allows purification, and according to the choice of Shams al-A'imma, it is not permissible because he considers the strike a pillar, like if he nullifies after washing a limb. [Marq al-Falah: 121] Seventh: And this condition is also for the validity of wudu. Like wax: because it makes the wipe on it, not on the body. [Marq al-Falah: 121] And its cause means the cause of tayammum is the intention of what is not permissible except with purification. [Marq al-Falah: 121] As mentioned in wudu, they are eight: sanity, puberty, Islam, existence of hadath, absence of menstruation and postpartum bleeding, lack of time, and ability for that which tayammum is permitted. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 121] And its two pillars (dual of rukn, its nun dropped for idafa). And its modality is that he strikes his hands on the earth, brings them forward and backward, then raises them and shakes them, and wipes with them so that nothing remains, and wipes the soft part between the nostrils, then strikes his hands on the earth similarly, his forearms to the elbows. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 121/1] The dispute: and he wipes his face with them, and wiping the hands: he did not say 'two strikes' because you know that the strike is part of the definition of tayammum. [Marq al-Falah: 121] And shaking them: meaning moving them to remove dust from them. Delaying tayammum: he mentioned delay absolutely, and it is restricted to one who is legally without water according to the apparent narration, for if he thinks that water is less than a mile away, tayammum is not permissible for him because although he is actually without water, he is not legally without water. For one who hopes: the restriction indicates that if he is not hopeful of finding water in that time, it is not recommended to delay, and he performs tayammum and prays at the recommended time. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 122]
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is a combination of matn and sharh from Nur al-Idah and its commentaries. It opens by detailing the conditions and sunnan of tayammum. The author lists three conditions that follow the sixth, seventh, and eighth sunnan: the need for two strikes (even in one place, with some internal disagreement about whether dust on the body suffices), the cessation of things that nullify tayammum (like menstruation or passing wind), and the removal of physical barriers like wax. Then it states the cause (sabab) of tayammum as the intention to do something that requires purification, and the conditions of obligation (shurut wujub) which are eight: sanity, puberty, Islam, presence of hadath, absence of hayd and nifas, lack of time, and ability to perform tayammum. The pillars (rukn) are wiping the hands and face. The seven sunnan are then enumerated: saying Bismillah, maintaining order and continuity, bringing hands forward and backward after placing them in dust, shaking them, spreading fingers, and the recommendation to delay tayammum for one who hopes for water before the end of the recommended time. The commentary clarifies that the delay is only for one who is legally without water (faqid al-ma' shar'an), and if water is less than a mile away, tayammum is not permitted. The internal differences within the Hanafi school are noted, particularly regarding the number of strikes and the effect of nullification after striking.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): A dry purification using dust in place of water when water is unavailable or prohibited.
فاقد الماء شرعاً (faqid al-ma' shar'an): One who is legally considered without water, even if water is physically present but inaccessible due to distance, danger, or inability to purchase at fair price.
الضربتان (al-darbatan): Two strikes of the hands on the earth for tayammum, as per the apparent ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many strikes are required for tayammum?
A) One strike
B) Two strikes
C) Three strikes
D) No strikes, just passing dust over hands

Key Takeaway
Tayammum's validity depends on meeting its eight conditions and performing its two pillars, with seven sunan enhancing completeness; the Hanafi school requires two strikes on the earth and restricts the recommended delay to those legally without water.

Delay Due to a Promise of Water: Obligation and Conditions
States the ruling on delaying prayer due to promise of water with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a person must delay prayer when promised water and identify when tayammum becomes permissible.

Core Idea
A promise of water obligates delay only if the promiser has water present or within a mile.

This lesson examines the ruling on delaying prayer due to a promise of water. The source text explains that while a promise creates an obligation to wait, it is conditional on the water being readily available. If the water is distant or absent, tayammum is permitted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Find the sentence that states the obligation to delay prayer due to a promise of water.
The text uses the verb "يجب" (obligatory).
2
Extract the Condition
Locate the restriction on the obligation: the water must be present with the promiser or within a mile.
The condition is introduced by "وهذا مقيد بما إذا". (and this is restricted to when).
3
Understand the Exception
When the water is absent or beyond a mile, the obligation drops and tayammum is allowed.
The proof: "لأن الشارع أباح له التيمم" (because the Lawgiver has permitted tayammum for him).
4
Apply the Ruling
Consider a scenario: a traveler is promised water from a friend 2 miles away. Does he wait?
No, because the distance exceeds one mile.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحكام التيمم الوقت، ويجب التأخير بالوعد بالماء ولو خاف القضاء، ويجب التأخير بالوعد بالثوب أو السقاء ما لم يخف القضاء، ويجب طلب الماء إلى مقدار أربعمائة خطوة إن ظن قربه مع الأمن، وإلا فلا، ويجب طلبه ممن هو معه إن كان في محل لا تشح به النفوس، وإن لم يعطه إلا بثمن مثله. الوقت أراد به الوقت المستحب وهو أول النصف الأخير من الوقت في صلاة يندب تأخيرها كما في 'النهر' بحيث يقع الأداء في وقت الاستحباب، وقيل: إلى آخر وقت الجواز والأول هو الصحيح كما في 'الجوهرة'، وعلى الأول فلا يؤخر العصر إلى تغير الشمس، وكذا لا يؤخر المغرب عن أول وقتها، وقيل: لا بأس إلى قبيل مغيب الشفق [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۱۲۳] ويجب التأخير أي يفترض تأخير الصلاة إذا وعد أحد بالماء وإن خاف فوات الصلاة، وهذا مقيد بما إذا كان الماء موجوداً عند الواعد أو قريباً منه دون ميل؛ فإنه إذا لم يوجد عنده أو كان بعيدا منه ميلاً فأكثر لا يجب عليه التأخير ; لأن الشارع أباح له التيمم. بالثوب: أي يجب على عادم الثوب إذا وعد له أحدٌ بالثوب أو بالسقاء كحبل ودلو أن يؤخر الصلاة كما في الماء، ولكن ما لم يخف القضاء، وهذا عند الإمام، فإن خاف القضاء تيمم وصلى وقالا يجب التأخير ولو خاف القضاء كالوعد بالماء. ومبنى الخلاف أن القدرة على ما سوى الماء هل تثبت بالبدل، والإباحة، قال الإمام: لا، وإنما تثبت بالملك أو بملك بدله إذا كان يباع، وقالا : تثبت بها كما تثبت بهما قياساً على الماء. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٢٣] طلب الماء: أطلقه فشمل ما إذا طلب بنفسه أو برسوله، والمقدار المذكور للطلب يعتبر من جانب ظنه، وإن ظنه في الجهات الأربع وجب الطلب منها وحد القرب أن يظن أن ما بينه وبين الماء دون ميل، والظن بقرب الماء يكون تارة برؤية طير، وتارة برؤية خضرة، وتارة بخبر مخبر. وإلا فلا أي وإن لم يظن قرب الماء، أو ظنه ولكن لا مع الأمن بأن خاف عدواً فلا يطلبه. [مراقي الفلاح: ١٢٤] إلا بثمن مثله هذه على ثلاثة أوجه إما إن أعطاه بمثل قيمته في أقرب موضع من المواضع التي يعز فيها الماء، أو بالغبن اليسير، أو بالغبن الفاحش، ففي الوجه الأول والثاني لا يجزئه التيمم؛ لتحقق القدرة على الماء؛ فإن القدرة على البذل قدرة على الماء، فيمتنع جواز التيمم كما أن القدرة على ثمن الرقبة تمنع التكفير بالصوم، وفي الوجه الثالث جاز له التيمم لوجود الضرر ; فإن حرمة مال المسلم كحرمة نفسه، والضرر في النفس مسقط، فكذا في المال. قيد لزوم الطلب بما إذا أمكن تحصيله بثمن المثل، فدخل ما إذا أمكن تحصيله بأقل. من ثمن مثله بالأولى، وألحق في لزوم الطلب ما إذا أمكن تحصيله بزيادة يسيرة واحترز به عما إذا أمكن تحصيله بغبن فاحش، وهو ما لا يدخل تحت تقويم المقومين قال في 'النوادر : وهو ضعف القيمة في ذلك المكان، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة: إذا قدر أن يشتري ماء يساوي دره هما بدرهم ونصف، لا يتيمم
Rulings of Tayammum: The time, and it is obligatory to delay (the prayer) due to a promise of water even if one fears missing the prayer, and it is obligatory to delay due to a promise of a garment or a water-skin as long as one does not fear missing the prayer, and it is obligatory to seek water up to four hundred steps if one thinks it is close with safety, otherwise not, and it is obligatory to seek it from one who is with him if he is in a place where souls are not stingy (i.e., water is usually shared), even if he does not give it except for its equivalent price. The time intended is the recommended time, which is the beginning of the last half of the time in a prayer whose delay is recommended, as in 'al-Nahr', such that the performance falls in the recommended time, and it is said: until the end of the permissible time, and the first is correct as in 'al-Jawhara'. According to the first, one should not delay Asr until the sun changes, nor delay Maghrib from its first time, and it is said: there is no harm until just before the disappearance of the twilight. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 123] 'And it is obligatory to delay': meaning it is obligatory to delay the prayer if someone promises him water, even if he fears missing the prayer, and this is restricted to when the water is present with the promiser or close to him within a mile; because if it is not present with him or is far more than a mile away, then he is not obligated to delay, because the Lawgiver has permitted tayammum for him. 'By a garment': meaning it is obligatory for one who lacks a garment, if someone promises him a garment or a water-skin like a rope and bucket, to delay the prayer as in the case of water, but as long as he does not fear missing the prayer, and this is according to Imam (Abu Hanifa). If he fears missing the prayer, he performs tayammum and prays. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: the delay is obligatory even if he fears missing the prayer, like the promise of water. The basis of the difference is whether ability (qudra) regarding what is other than water is established by substitution (badal) and permissibility (ibaha). Imam said: no, it is only established by ownership (milk) or ownership of its substitute if it is sold. They said: it is established by them just as it is established by the two (ownership and sale) by analogy to water. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 123] 'Seeking water': he mentioned it absolutely, so it includes if he seeks himself or by his messenger, and the mentioned amount for seeking is considered from his assumption, and if he assumes it in the four directions, he must seek from them. The definition of closeness (qurb) is that he assumes that between him and the water is less than a mile. Assumption of closeness of water happens sometimes by seeing a bird, sometimes by seeing greenery, sometimes by a report of a reporter. 'Otherwise not': meaning if he does not assume closeness of water, or assumes it but not with safety, because he fears an enemy, then he does not seek it. [Marq al-Falah: 124] 'Except for its equivalent price': this is of three types: either he gives it for its equivalent value in the nearest place where water is scarce, or for a slight overpayment (ghaban yasir), or for an excessive overpayment (ghaban fahish). In the first and second cases, tayammum is not sufficient for him, because the ability (qudra) on water is realized; for the ability to pay is an ability on water, so the permissibility of tayammum is prevented, just as the ability to pay the price of a slave prevents expiation by fasting. In the third case, tayammum is permissible for him due to harm (darar), for the sanctity of a Muslim's wealth is like the sanctity of his person, and harm to the person is excusable, so likewise in wealth. The obligation to seek water is conditioned by the possibility of obtaining it at its equivalent price, so it includes if it can be obtained for less than its equivalent price a fortiori. And in the obligation of seeking, he included if it can be obtained for a slight increase, and excluded from it if it can be obtained by an excessive overpayment, which is that which does not fall under the valuation of appraisers. He said in al-Nawadir: it is twice the value in that place, and al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa: if he is able to buy water worth two dirhams for a dirham and a half, he does not perform tayammum.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is from the section on 'Ahkam al-Tayammum' in the commentary. It explains the rulings on when to delay tayammum and the obligation to seek water. The opening states that it is obligatory to delay the prayer if one is promised water, even if it means missing the prayer time, but this is restricted to when the water is present with the promiser or within a mile. Similarly, if one lacks a garment (for covering), a promise of a garment or a water-skin also obligates delay, but according to Imam Abu Hanifa, only if one does not fear missing the prayer; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) say it is obligatory even with fear of missing the prayer. The basis of this difference is whether the ability to obtain something other than water (like a garment) is established by substitution and permissibility (the Sahibayn) or only by ownership (Imam). The passage then discusses the obligation to seek water up to four hundred steps in directions where water is assumed near and safety is present. If water can be obtained only by purchasing, the ruling depends on the price: if at fair market value or with a slight overpayment, tayammum is not allowed because the person is effectively able to obtain water; if at an exorbitant price (more than double the value), tayammum is allowed due to harm.

Key Terms
الوعد بالماء (al-wa'd bi al-ma'): A promise of water from someone, which obligates delay of tayammum if conditions met.
ميل (mil): A mile, used as the threshold distance within which water must be available to obligate delay.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does a promise of water obligate a person to delay prayer?
A) Always, regardless of distance.
B) Only if the water is present with the promiser or within a mile.
C) Only if the promiser is a reliable person.
D) Only if the prayer time is long enough to wait.

Key Takeaway
A promise of water obligates delay only if the water is immediately obtainable (within a mile); otherwise, tayammum is permitted.

The Garment Promise Dispute: Delay or Tayammum?
Explains the intra-Hanafi dispute on garment promise and its basis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding delaying prayer due to a promise of a garment and identify the basis of the disagreement.

Core Idea
Imam Abu Hanifa allows tayammum when fearing missing prayer; the two students insist on delaying even with fear.

This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether a promise of a garment (or water-skin) obligates delay of prayer even if one fears missing the time. The source text contrasts the position of Imam Abu Hanifa with that of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) and explains the underlying principle: the nature of ability (qudra) for non-water items.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Contested Ruling
Find the sentence that states the ruling on delaying prayer for a promised garment/water-skin.
The text says 'بالثوب: أي يجب على عادم الثوب... أن يؤخر الصلاة كما في الماء، ولكن ما لم يخف القضاء'.
2
Contrast the Two Positions
Note Imam Abu Hanifa's condition (no fear of missing prayer) vs the Sahibayn's unconditional obligation.
Imam: delay only if no fear of missing; Sahibayn: delay even with fear.
3
Extract the Basis of Difference
Locate the sentence explaining the basis: whether ability (qudra) for non-water items is established by substitution (badal) and permissibility (ibaha).
The text: 'ومبنى الخلاف أن القدرة على ما سوى الماء هل تثبت بالبدل، والإباحة'.
4
Apply the Ruling to a Scenario
Imagine a person lacks a garment and is promised one. Prayer time is short. According to Imam, what should he do? According to Sahibayn?
Imam: tayammum and pray; Sahibayn: wait even if prayer is missed.

أحكام التيمم الوقت، ويجب التأخير بالوعد بالماء ولو خاف القضاء، ويجب التأخير بالوعد بالثوب أو السقاء ما لم يخف القضاء، ويجب طلب الماء إلى مقدار أربعمائة خطوة إن ظن قربه مع الأمن، وإلا فلا، ويجب طلبه ممن هو معه إن كان في محل لا تشح به النفوس، وإن لم يعطه إلا بثمن مثله. الوقت أراد به الوقت المستحب وهو أول النصف الأخير من الوقت في صلاة يندب تأخيرها كما في 'النهر' بحيث يقع الأداء في وقت الاستحباب، وقيل: إلى آخر وقت الجواز والأول هو الصحيح كما في 'الجوهرة'، وعلى الأول فلا يؤخر العصر إلى تغير الشمس، وكذا لا يؤخر المغرب عن أول وقتها، وقيل: لا بأس إلى قبيل مغيب الشفق [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۱۲۳] ويجب التأخير أي يفترض تأخير الصلاة إذا وعد أحد بالماء وإن خاف فوات الصلاة، وهذا مقيد بما إذا كان الماء موجوداً عند الواعد أو قريباً منه دون ميل؛ فإنه إذا لم يوجد عنده أو كان بعيدا منه ميلاً فأكثر لا يجب عليه التأخير ; لأن الشارع أباح له التيمم. بالثوب: أي يجب على عادم الثوب إذا وعد له أحدٌ بالثوب أو بالسقاء كحبل ودلو أن يؤخر الصلاة كما في الماء، ولكن ما لم يخف القضاء، وهذا عند الإمام، فإن خاف القضاء تيمم وصلى وقالا يجب التأخير ولو خاف القضاء كالوعد بالماء. ومبنى الخلاف أن القدرة على ما سوى الماء هل تثبت بالبدل، والإباحة، قال الإمام: لا، وإنما تثبت بالملك أو بملك بدله إذا كان يباع، وقالا : تثبت بها كما تثبت بهما قياساً على الماء. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٢٣] طلب الماء: أطلقه فشمل ما إذا طلب بنفسه أو برسوله، والمقدار المذكور للطلب يعتبر من جانب ظنه، وإن ظنه في الجهات الأربع وجب الطلب منها وحد القرب أن يظن أن ما بينه وبين الماء دون ميل، والظن بقرب الماء يكون تارة برؤية طير، وتارة برؤية خضرة، وتارة بخبر مخبر. وإلا فلا أي وإن لم يظن قرب الماء، أو ظنه ولكن لا مع الأمن بأن خاف عدواً فلا يطلبه. [مراقي الفلاح: ١٢٤] إلا بثمن مثله هذه على ثلاثة أوجه إما إن أعطاه بمثل قيمته في أقرب موضع من المواضع التي يعز فيها الماء، أو بالغبن اليسير، أو بالغبن الفاحش، ففي الوجه الأول والثاني لا يجزئه التيمم؛ لتحقق القدرة على الماء؛ فإن القدرة على البذل قدرة على الماء، فيمتنع جواز التيمم كما أن القدرة على ثمن الرقبة تمنع التكفير بالصوم، وفي الوجه الثالث جاز له التيمم لوجود الضرر ; فإن حرمة مال المسلم كحرمة نفسه، والضرر في النفس مسقط، فكذا في المال. قيد لزوم الطلب بما إذا أمكن تحصيله بثمن المثل، فدخل ما إذا أمكن تحصيله بأقل. من ثمن مثله بالأولى، وألحق في لزوم الطلب ما إذا أمكن تحصيله بزيادة يسيرة واحترز به عما إذا أمكن تحصيله بغبن فاحش، وهو ما لا يدخل تحت تقويم المقومين قال في 'النوادر : وهو ضعف القيمة في ذلك المكان، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة: إذا قدر أن يشتري ماء يساوي دره هما بدرهم ونصف، لا يتيمم
Rulings of Tayammum: The time, and it is obligatory to delay (the prayer) due to a promise of water even if one fears missing the prayer, and it is obligatory to delay due to a promise of a garment or a water-skin as long as one does not fear missing the prayer, and it is obligatory to seek water up to four hundred steps if one thinks it is close with safety, otherwise not, and it is obligatory to seek it from one who is with him if he is in a place where souls are not stingy (i.e., water is usually shared), even if he does not give it except for its equivalent price. The time intended is the recommended time, which is the beginning of the last half of the time in a prayer whose delay is recommended, as in 'al-Nahr', such that the performance falls in the recommended time, and it is said: until the end of the permissible time, and the first is correct as in 'al-Jawhara'. According to the first, one should not delay Asr until the sun changes, nor delay Maghrib from its first time, and it is said: there is no harm until just before the disappearance of the twilight. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 123] 'And it is obligatory to delay': meaning it is obligatory to delay the prayer if someone promises him water, even if he fears missing the prayer, and this is restricted to when the water is present with the promiser or close to him within a mile; because if it is not present with him or is far more than a mile away, then he is not obligated to delay, because the Lawgiver has permitted tayammum for him. 'By a garment': meaning it is obligatory for one who lacks a garment, if someone promises him a garment or a water-skin like a rope and bucket, to delay the prayer as in the case of water, but as long as he does not fear missing the prayer, and this is according to Imam (Abu Hanifa). If he fears missing the prayer, he performs tayammum and prays. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: the delay is obligatory even if he fears missing the prayer, like the promise of water. The basis of the difference is whether ability (qudra) regarding what is other than water is established by substitution (badal) and permissibility (ibaha). Imam said: no, it is only established by ownership (milk) or ownership of its substitute if it is sold. They said: it is established by them just as it is established by the two (ownership and sale) by analogy to water. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 123] 'Seeking water': he mentioned it absolutely, so it includes if he seeks himself or by his messenger, and the mentioned amount for seeking is considered from his assumption, and if he assumes it in the four directions, he must seek from them. The definition of closeness (qurb) is that he assumes that between him and the water is less than a mile. Assumption of closeness of water happens sometimes by seeing a bird, sometimes by seeing greenery, sometimes by a report of a reporter. 'Otherwise not': meaning if he does not assume closeness of water, or assumes it but not with safety, because he fears an enemy, then he does not seek it. [Marq al-Falah: 124] 'Except for its equivalent price': this is of three types: either he gives it for its equivalent value in the nearest place where water is scarce, or for a slight overpayment (ghaban yasir), or for an excessive overpayment (ghaban fahish). In the first and second cases, tayammum is not sufficient for him, because the ability (qudra) on water is realized; for the ability to pay is an ability on water, so the permissibility of tayammum is prevented, just as the ability to pay the price of a slave prevents expiation by fasting. In the third case, tayammum is permissible for him due to harm (darar), for the sanctity of a Muslim's wealth is like the sanctity of his person, and harm to the person is excusable, so likewise in wealth. The obligation to seek water is conditioned by the possibility of obtaining it at its equivalent price, so it includes if it can be obtained for less than its equivalent price a fortiori. And in the obligation of seeking, he included if it can be obtained for a slight increase, and excluded from it if it can be obtained by an excessive overpayment, which is that which does not fall under the valuation of appraisers. He said in al-Nawadir: it is twice the value in that place, and al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa: if he is able to buy water worth two dirhams for a dirham and a half, he does not perform tayammum.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is from the section on 'Ahkam al-Tayammum' in the commentary. It explains the rulings on when to delay tayammum and the obligation to seek water. The opening states that it is obligatory to delay the prayer if one is promised water, even if it means missing the prayer time, but this is restricted to when the water is present with the promiser or within a mile. Similarly, if one lacks a garment (for covering), a promise of a garment or a water-skin also obligates delay, but according to Imam Abu Hanifa, only if one does not fear missing the prayer; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) say it is obligatory even with fear of missing the prayer. The basis of this difference is whether the ability to obtain something other than water (like a garment) is established by substitution and permissibility (the Sahibayn) or only by ownership (Imam). The passage then discusses the obligation to seek water up to four hundred steps in directions where water is assumed near and safety is present. If water can be obtained only by purchasing, the ruling depends on the price: if at fair market value or with a slight overpayment, tayammum is not allowed because the person is effectively able to obtain water; if at an exorbitant price (more than double the value), tayammum is allowed due to harm.

Key Terms
البدل (al-badal): Substitution; the ability to obtain an item through a substitute (e.g., money, barter).
الإباحة (al-ibaha): Permissibility; the legal ability to use something without ownership (e.g., borrowing with permission).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling if a person is promised a garment but fears missing the prayer?
A) He must delay the prayer and wait for the garment.
B) He may perform tayammum and pray.
C) He must leave the area and find water.
D) He is excused from prayer altogether.

Key Takeaway
The garment promise dispute hinges on whether permissibility (ibaha) constitutes ability; Imam says no, Sahibayn say yes via qiyas on water.

Obligation to Seek Water: Distance, Safety, and Directions
States conditions for obligatory seeking of water before tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions that obligate seeking water for wudu and apply the rules regarding distance, safety, and directions.

Core Idea
Seeking water is only obligatory if you assume it is near and safe; otherwise, you may perform tayammum.

This lesson covers the obligation to physically seek water before resorting to tayammum. The source text specifies the maximum distance (400 steps), the requirement of safety (amur), and the method of determining which direction to search based on assumptions. It also addresses seeking water from companions and the price threshold.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Obligation and Its Conditions
Find the sentence that states the obligation to seek water up to 400 steps, conditional on assuming it is close with safety.
The text: 'ويجب طلب الماء إلى مقدار أربعمائة خطوة إن ظن قربه مع الأمن'.
2
Define 'Closeness' (Qurb)
Locate the definition: assuming the water is less than a mile away.
The text: 'وحد القرب أن يظن أن ما بينه وبين الماء دون ميل'.
3
Understand the Exception: No Safety
If there is fear of an enemy, the obligation is lifted.
The text: 'وإلا فلا أي وإن لم يظن قرب الماء، أو ظنه ولكن لا مع الأمن بأن خاف عدواً فلا يطلبه'.
4
Apply to Multiple Directions
If the person assumes water is in multiple directions, he must search in all those directions.
The text: 'وإن ظنه في الجهات الأربع وجب الطلب منها'.

Commentary
This passage is from the section on 'Ahkam al-Tayammum' in the commentary. It explains the rulings on when to delay tayammum and the obligation to seek water. طلب الماء (talab al-ma'): The act of searching for water before performing tayammum.
قرب (qurb): Closeness; defined as less than a mile.

Purchasing Water: When the Price Permits Tayammum
Explains when tayammum is permitted due to high water price

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between fair price, slight overpayment, and excessive overpayment for water, and determine when tayammum is allowed.

Core Idea
Tayammum is only allowed if buying water would require an exorbitant price (more than double the market value).

This lesson explains the rulings on obtaining water by purchase. The source text outlines three price scenarios: fair market value (thaman al-mithl), slight overpayment (ghaban yasir), and excessive overpayment (ghaban fahish). The threshold for allowing tayammum is the excessive overpayment, defined as more than double the value in that location.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Price Categories
Locate the three scenarios: (1) fair price, (2) slight overpayment, (3) excessive overpayment.
The text: 'على ثلاثة أوجه إما إن أعطاه بمثل قيمته ... أو بالغبن اليسير، أو بالغبن الفاحش'.
2
Apply the Rule for Fair Price and Slight Overpayment
In these two cases, tayammum is not allowed because the person has the ability (qudra) to pay.
The text: 'ففي الوجه الأول والثاني لا يجزئه التيمم'.
3
Apply the Rule for Excessive Overpayment
In this case, tayammum is allowed due to harm (darar) to wealth.
The text: 'وفي الوجه الثالث جاز له التيمم لوجود الضرر'.
4
Define Excessive Overpayment
Find the definition: what does not fall under the valuation of appraisers; specifically, twice the value in that place.
The text: 'وهو ما لا يدخل تحت تقويم المقومين ... وهو ضعف القيمة في ذلك المكان'.

Source Text

أحكام التيمم الوقت، ويجب التأخير بالوعد بالماء ولو خاف القضاء، ويجب التأخير بالوعد بالثوب أو السقاء ما لم يخف القضاء، ويجب طلب الماء إلى مقدار أربعمائة خطوة إن ظن قربه مع الأمن، وإلا فلا، ويجب طلبه ممن هو معه إن كان في محل لا تشح به النفوس، وإن لم يعطه إلا بثمن مثله. الوقت أراد به الوقت المستحب وهو أول النصف الأخير من الوقت في صلاة يندب تأخيرها كما في 'النهر' بحيث يقع الأداء في وقت الاستحباب، وقيل: إلى آخر وقت الجواز والأول هو الصحيح كما في 'الجوهرة'، وعلى الأول فلا يؤخر العصر إلى تغير الشمس، وكذا لا يؤخر المغرب عن أول وقتها، وقيل: لا بأس إلى قبيل مغيب الشفق [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۱۲۳] ويجب التأخير أي يفترض تأخير الصلاة إذا وعد أحد بالماء وإن خاف فوات الصلاة، وهذا مقيد بما إذا كان الماء موجوداً عند الواعد أو قريباً منه دون ميل؛ فإنه إذا لم يوجد عنده أو كان بعيدا منه ميلاً فأكثر لا يجب عليه التأخير ; لأن الشارع أباح له التيمم. بالثوب: أي يجب على عادم الثوب إذا وعد له أحدٌ بالثوب أو بالسقاء كحبل ودلو أن يؤخر الصلاة كما في الماء، ولكن ما لم يخف القضاء، وهذا عند الإمام، فإن خاف القضاء تيمم وصلى وقالا يجب التأخير ولو خاف القضاء كالوعد بالماء. ومبنى الخلاف أن القدرة على ما سوى الماء هل تثبت بالبدل، والإباحة، قال الإمام: لا، وإنما تثبت بالملك أو بملك بدله إذا كان يباع، وقالا : تثبت بها كما تثبت بهما قياساً على الماء. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٢٣] طلب الماء: أطلقه فشمل ما إذا طلب بنفسه أو برسوله، والمقدار المذكور للطلب يعتبر من جانب ظنه، وإن ظنه في الجهات الأربع وجب الطلب منها وحد القرب أن يظن أن ما بينه وبين الماء دون ميل، والظن بقرب الماء يكون تارة برؤية طير، وتارة برؤية خضرة، وتارة بخبر مخبر. وإلا فلا أي وإن لم يظن قرب الماء، أو ظنه ولكن لا مع الأمن بأن خاف عدواً فلا يطلبه. [مراقي الفلاح: ١٢٤] إلا بثمن مثله هذه على ثلاثة أوجه إما إن أعطاه بمثل قيمته في أقرب موضع من المواضع التي يعز فيها الماء، أو بالغبن اليسير، أو بالغبن الفاحش، ففي الوجه الأول والثاني لا يجزئه التيمم؛ لتحقق القدرة على الماء؛ فإن القدرة على البذل قدرة على الماء، فيمتنع جواز التيمم كما أن القدرة على ثمن الرقبة تمنع التكفير بالصوم، وفي الوجه الثالث جاز له التيمم لوجود الضرر ; فإن حرمة مال المسلم كحرمة نفسه، والضرر في النفس مسقط، فكذا في المال. قيد لزوم الطلب بما إذا أمكن تحصيله بثمن المثل، فدخل ما إذا أمكن تحصيله بأقل. من ثمن مثله بالأولى، وألحق في لزوم الطلب ما إذا أمكن تحصيله بزيادة يسيرة واحترز به عما إذا أمكن تحصيله بغبن فاحش، وهو ما لا يدخل تحت تقويم المقومين قال في 'النوادر : وهو ضعف القيمة في ذلك المكان، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة: إذا قدر أن يشتري ماء يساوي دره هما بدرهم ونصف، لا يتيمم
Rulings of Tayammum: The time, and it is obligatory to delay (the prayer) due to a promise of water even if one fears missing the prayer, and it is obligatory to delay due to a promise of a garment or a water-skin as long as one does not fear missing the prayer, and it is obligatory to seek water up to four hundred steps if one thinks it is close with safety, otherwise not, and it is obligatory to seek it from one who is with him if he is in a place where souls are not stingy (i.e., water is usually shared), even if he does not give it except for its equivalent price. The time intended is the recommended time, which is the beginning of the last half of the time in a prayer whose delay is recommended, as in 'al-Nahr', such that the performance falls in the recommended time, and it is said: until the end of the permissible time, and the first is correct as in 'al-Jawhara'. According to the first, one should not delay Asr until the sun changes, nor delay Maghrib from its first time, and it is said: there is no harm until just before the disappearance of the twilight. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 123] 'And it is obligatory to delay': meaning it is obligatory to delay the prayer if someone promises him water, even if he fears missing the prayer, and this is restricted to when the water is present with the promiser or close to him within a mile; because if it is not present with him or is far more than a mile away, then he is not obligated to delay, because the Lawgiver has permitted tayammum for him. 'By a garment': meaning it is obligatory for one who lacks a garment, if someone promises him a garment or a water-skin like a rope and bucket, to delay the prayer as in the case of water, but as long as he does not fear missing the prayer, and this is according to Imam (Abu Hanifa). If he fears missing the prayer, he performs tayammum and prays. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: the delay is obligatory even if he fears missing the prayer, like the promise of water. The basis of the difference is whether ability (qudra) regarding what is other than water is established by substitution (badal) and permissibility (ibaha). Imam said: no, it is only established by ownership (milk) or ownership of its substitute if it is sold. They said: it is established by them just as it is established by the two (ownership and sale) by analogy to water. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 123] 'Seeking water': he mentioned it absolutely, so it includes if he seeks himself or by his messenger, and the mentioned amount for seeking is considered from his assumption, and if he assumes it in the four directions, he must seek from them. The definition of closeness (qurb) is that he assumes that between him and the water is less than a mile. Assumption of closeness of water happens sometimes by seeing a bird, sometimes by seeing greenery, sometimes by a report of a reporter. 'Otherwise not': meaning if he does not assume closeness of water, or assumes it but not with safety, because he fears an enemy, then he does not seek it. [Marq al-Falah: 124] 'Except for its equivalent price': this is of three types: either he gives it for its equivalent value in the nearest place where water is scarce, or for a slight overpayment (ghaban yasir), or for an excessive overpayment (ghaban fahish). In the first and second cases, tayammum is not sufficient for him, because the ability (qudra) on water is realized; for the ability to pay is an ability on water, so the permissibility of tayammum is prevented, just as the ability to pay the price of a slave prevents expiation by fasting. In the third case, tayammum is permissible for him due to harm (darar), for the sanctity of a Muslim's wealth is like the sanctity of his person, and harm to the person is excusable, so likewise in wealth. The obligation to seek water is conditioned by the possibility of obtaining it at its equivalent price, so it includes if it can be obtained for less than its equivalent price a fortiori. And in the obligation of seeking, he included if it can be obtained for a slight increase, and excluded from it if it can be obtained by an excessive overpayment, which is that which does not fall under the valuation of appraisers. He said in al-Nawadir: it is twice the value in that place, and al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa: if he is able to buy water worth two dirhams for a dirham and a half, he does not perform tayammum.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is from the section on 'Ahkam al-Tayammum' in the commentary. It explains the rulings on when to delay tayammum and the obligation to seek water. The opening states that it is obligatory to delay the prayer if one is promised water, even if it means missing the prayer time, but this is restricted to when the water is present with the promiser or within a mile. Similarly, if one lacks a garment (for covering), a promise of a garment or a water-skin also obligates delay, but according to Imam Abu Hanifa, only if one does not fear missing the prayer; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) say it is obligatory even with fear of missing the prayer. The basis of this difference is whether the ability to obtain something other than water (like a garment) is established by substitution and permissibility (the Sahibayn) or only by ownership (Imam). The passage then discusses the obligation to seek water up to four hundred steps in directions where water is assumed near and safety is present. If water can be obtained only by purchasing, the ruling depends on the price: if at fair market value or with a slight overpayment, tayammum is not allowed because the person is effectively able to obtain water; if at an exorbitant price (more than double the value), tayammum is allowed due to harm.

Key Terms
ثمن المثل (thaman al-mithl): Fair market price in the nearest place where water is scarce.
الغبن الفاحش (al-ghaban al-fahish): Exorbitant overpayment, defined as more than double the market value.
الغبن اليسير (al-ghaban al-yasir): Slight overpayment that does not exceed the threshold.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If water can be bought at a price that is three times the market value, what is the ruling on tayammum?
A) Tayammum is allowed because the price is excessive.
B) Tayammum is not allowed because the person can afford it.
C) Tayammum is recommended but not required.
D) Tayammum is invalid under any circumstances.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is permissible only when purchasing water would require an excessive overpayment (more than double the market price).

Ruling on Delaying Prayer Due to Promise of Water or Clothing
States the obligation to delay prayer upon promise of water or clothing, with intra-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the obligation to delay prayer upon a promise of clothing or waterskin when fearing missing the prayer time, and identify the operative fatwa position.

Core Idea
A promise of clothing obligates delay only if you do not fear missing the prayer — unless you follow the Sahibayn.

When you lack water or clothing and need to perform tayammum, a promise to provide the item may require you to delay your prayer. But what if the promise comes just before the time ends? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on this very point, rooted in a deeper usul question about what constitutes 'capability' (qudra) over an item. This lesson unpacks the ruling for water versus clothing, and the reasoning behind the preferred fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
Recognize the situation: a person lacks water or clothing, is promised the item, but fears the prayer time may end. The ruling depends on the type of item and the certainty of the promise.
The promise must be reliable; water must exist with the promisor within a mile.
2
Distinguish between promise of water vs promise of clothing
For water, the matn states that delay is obligatory even if the time is lost. For clothing or waterskin, the text adds a condition: 'as long as he does not fear missing the prayer' — revealing the dispute.
This condition reflects Abu Hanifa's view; the Sahibayn remove it.
3
Understand the usul basis of the ikhtilaf
The disagreement turns on whether capability over an item is established by ownership (milk) or by mere promise and permission (ibaha/badal). Abu Hanifa insists on ownership; the Sahibayn accept promise as sufficient, analogizing to water.
This is a classic example of qiyas and its limits within the Hanafi school.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Later authorities like al-Tahtawi and al-Haskafi prefer the Sahibayn's view: delay is obligatory even if the time is missed. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
The fatwa hierarchy gives weight to this position despite Abu Hanifa's original view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحكام التيمم
الوقت، ويجب التأخير بالوعد بالماء ولو خاف القضاء، ويجب التأخير بالوعد بالثوب أو السقاء ما لم يخف القضاء، ويجب طلب الماء إلى مقدار أربعمائة خطوة إن ظن قربه مع الأمن، وإلا فلا، ويجب طلبه ممن هو معه إن كان في محل لا تشح به النفوس، وإن لم يعطه إلا بثمن مثله
الوقت أراد به الوقت المستحب وهو أول النصف الأخير من الوقت في صلاة يندب تأخيرها كما في "النهر" بحيث يقع الأداء في وقت الاستحباب، وقيل: إلى آخر وقت الجواز والأول هو الصحيح كما في "الجوهرة"، وعلى الأول فلا يؤخر العصر إلى تغير الشمس، وكذا لا يؤخر المغرب عن أول وقتها، وقيل: لا بأس إلى قبيل مغيب الشفق [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۱۲۳] ويجب التأخير أي يفترض تأخير الصلاة إذا وعد أحد بالماء وإن خاف فوات الصلاة، وهذا مقيد بما إذا كان الماء موجوداً عند الواعد أو قريباً منه دون ميل؛ فإنه إذا لم يوجد عنده أو كان بعيدا منه ميلاً فأكثر لا يجب عليه التأخير ؛ لأن الشارع أباح له التيمم. بالثوب: أي يجب على عادم الثوب إذا وعد له أحدٌ بالثوب أو بالسقاء كحبل ودلو أن يؤخر الصلاة كما في الماء، ولكن ما لم يخف القضاء، وهذا عند الإمام، فإن خاف القضاء تيمم وصلى وقالا يجب التأخير ولو خاف القضاء كالوعد بالماء. ومبنى مسألة أن القدرة على ما سوى الماء هل تثبت بالبدل والإباحة، قال الإمام: لا، وإنما تثبت بالملك أو بملك بدله إذا كان يباع، وقالا : تثبت بها كما تثبت بهما قياساً على الماء. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٢٣]
The time [for performing prayer with tayammum] is the recommended time, and it is obligatory to delay [prayer] upon a promise of water even if he fears missing [the prayer], and it is obligatory to delay upon a promise of a garment or a waterskin as long as he does not fear missing the prayer. And it is obligatory to seek water up to a distance of four hundred steps if he thinks it is near with safety, otherwise no. And it is obligatory to seek it from someone who is with him if he is in a place where souls are not stingy with it, even if he does not give it to him except for its like price. The 'time' intended is the recommended time, which is the beginning of the last half of time in a prayer whose delay is recommended, according to al-Nahr, so that the performance occurs within the recommended time. It is also said: until the end of the permissible time, and the first is correct according to al-Jawhara. According to the first, 'Asr should not be delayed until the sun changes, nor should Maghrib be delayed from its first time, and it is said: no harm until just before the disappearance of twilight. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 123] 'And it is obligatory to delay' means that delaying prayer is obligatory if someone promises water, even if he fears missing the prayer. This is restricted to when the water exists with the promisor or near him within a mile; if it is not with him or is distant a mile or more, he is not required to delay, because the Lawgiver allowed him tayammum. 'By the garment': It is obligatory for one who lacks a garment, if someone promises him a garment or a waterskin like a rope and bucket, to delay the prayer as with water, but as long as he does not fear missing the prayer. This according to Imam [Abu Hanifa]; if he fears missing the prayer, he performs tayammum and prays. And the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] say: delaying is obligatory even if he fears missing the prayer, like the promise of water. The basis of the issue is whether capability over something other than water is established by an alternative (badal) and permission (ibaha). Imam said: No, it is only established by ownership or ownership of its substitute if it is sold. And the two said: It is established by them just as it is established by the two, by analogy with water. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 123]
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah with its hashya by al-Tahtawi deals with the conditions under which a person who intends to perform tayammum must delay his prayer if he is promised water, clothing, or a water vessel. The hashya explains that the time referred to is the recommended time (al-waqt al-mustahab), not the permissible time. It then clarifies the obligation to delay: if someone promises water and the water exists with the promisor within a mile, the one without water must wait, even if it means missing the prayer time. But if the water is not present or is beyond a mile, he may perform tayammum. The same applies to a promise of clothing or a waterskin, but here there is a dispute: Abu Hanifa says if he fears missing the prayer, he does tayammum and prays, while the Sahibayn say he must still delay even if he fears missing. The basis of the disagreement is whether capability over these items is established by mere promise (badal and ibaha) or only by actual ownership. Abu Hanifa holds that capability is only through ownership, while the two hold that promise establishes capability, analogizing to water. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute where the mufta bihi is the view of the Sahibayn as per later authorities (al-Tahtawi).

Key Terms
الوعد (al-wa'd): A reliable promise that one will be given the item in question (water, garment, or waterskin).
البدل (al-badal): The substitute or alternative to water for purification, such as earth for tayammum; also refers to the item promised as a substitute for water.
الإباحة (al-ibaha): Permission or permissibility to use something; in this context, having permission to use the substitute (e.g., earth) does not constitute actual capability over water.
الملك (al-milk): Ownership of the item; the basis for capability according to Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a person is promised a garment but fears missing the prayer time, what must he do?
A) Delay the prayer
B) Perform tayammum and pray
C) Wait until the garment arrives and then pray
D) Perform wudu with sand

Key Takeaway
The obligation to delay prayer due to a promise of clothing depends on whether one fears missing the prayer time, and the fatwa follows the Sahibayn's view that delay is required even if the time is missed.

Seeking Water for Tayammum
Obligation and conditions for seeking water before tayammum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which seeking water is wajib and identify when it is not required.

Core Idea
Seeking water is wajib only if you think water is near and it is safe.

Before performing tayammum, one must seek water if there is a reasonable expectation of finding it. This lesson details the obligation: the seeker must search in the directions he suspects, up to about a mile, but only if he feels safe. If there is fear of an enemy, the obligation drops.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is seeking water (talab al-ma'). The ruling is wajib when there is hope of finding it and safety.
The text explicitly says 'wajib' through implication—the obligation to seek before tayammum.
2
Determine the condition of estimation
The obligation depends on the person's estimation (zann) that water is near. If he does not think water is near, seeking is not required.
Indications of nearness: seeing birds, greenery, or reliable informant.
3
Set the required distance and directions
Nearness is defined as less than a mile. If he thinks water might be in multiple directions, he must search all four directions.
The distance is measured from his current location.
4
Note the exception for safety
Even if he thinks water is near, if he fears an enemy or danger, seeking is not wajib.
Safety overrides the obligation; the principle is that harm to life or limb takes precedence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
طلب الماء: أطلقه فشمل ما إذا طلب بنفسه أو برسوله، والمقدار المذكور للطلب يعتبر من جانب ظنه، وإن ظنه في الجهات الأربع وجب الطلب منها وحد القرب أن يظن أن ما بينه وبين الماء دون ميل، والظن بقرب الماء يكون تارة برؤية طير، وتارة برؤية خضرة، وتارة بخبر مخبر. وإلا فلا أي وإن لم يظن قرب الماء، أو ظنه ولكن لا مع الأمن بأن خاف عدواً فلا يطلبه. [مراقي الفلاح: ١٢٤] إلا بثمن مثله هذه على ثلاثة أوجه إما إن أعطاه بمثل قيمته في أقرب موضع من المواضع التي يعز فيها الماء، أو بالغبن اليسير، أو بالغبن الفاحش، ففي الوجه الأول والثاني لا يجزئه التيمم؛ لتحقق القدرة على الماء؛ فإن القدرة على البذل قدرة على الماء، فيمتنع جواز التيمم كما أن القدرة على ثمن الرقبة تمنع التكفير بالصوم، وفي الوجه الثالث جاز له التيمم لوجود الضرر ؛ فإن حرمة مال المسلم كحرمة نفسه، والضرر في النفس مسقط، فكذا في المال. قيد لزوم الطلب بما إذا أمكن تحصيله بثمن المثل، فدخل ما إذا أمكن تحصيله بأقل. من ثمن مثله بالأولى، وألحق في لزوم الطلب ما إذا أمكن تحصيله بزيادة يسيرة واحترز به عما إذا أمكن تحصيله بغبن فاحش، وهو ما لا يدخل تحت تقويم المقومين قال في "النوادر : وهو ضعف القيمة في ذلك المكان، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة: إذا قدر أن يشتري ماء يساوي دره هما بدرهم ونصف، لا يتيمم
بيان لـ"ما"
لزمه شراؤه به إن كان معه فاضلا عن نفقته
Seeking water: He [the author] stated it generally, so it includes whether he seeks by himself or by his messenger. The mentioned amount for seeking is considered from the side of his estimation. If he thinks it is in the four directions, he must seek from them. The limit of nearness is that he thinks that between him and water is less than a mile. Thinking that water is near may occur sometimes by seeing a bird, sometimes by seeing greenery, sometimes by news from an informant. 'Otherwise no' meaning if he does not think water is near, or thinks it is near but without safety, i.e., he fears an enemy, then he does not seek it. [Maraqi al-Falah: 124] 'Except for its like price' has three aspects: either he gives it for its like value in the nearest place where water is scarce, or with a slight overcharge (ghubn yasir), or with a gross overcharge (ghubn fahish). In the first and second aspects, tayammum is not permissible for him because capability for water is established; indeed, capability to pay is capability to obtain water, so permissibility of tayammum is prevented, just as capability to pay the price of a slave prevents expiation by fasting. In the third aspect, tayammum is permissible for him due to harm; for the sanctity of a Muslim's wealth is like the sanctity of his self, and harm to the self removes the obligation, so likewise to wealth. He restricted the necessity of seeking to when it can be obtained at the like price; so it includes when it can be obtained for less than its like price by priority. And he attached to the necessity of seeking the case when it can be obtained with a slight increase, and thereby excluded the case when it can be obtained with a gross overcharge, which is that which does not fall under the valuation of valuators. He said in al-Nawadir: it is double the value in that place. And al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa: if he is able to buy water worth two dirhams for a dirham and a half, he does not perform tayammum.
Explanation of 'what' (ma): He must buy it with it if he has it surplus to his expenses.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This section covers two main obligations: seeking water and purchasing it. The seeking is obligatory up to 400 steps from where he thinks water might be, but only if he has a reasonable expectation of finding it and it is safe. The seeking must be done in the directions he suspects. If he cannot seek due to fear of enemies, the obligation drops. Then the text addresses purchasing water: if someone demands the like price (thaman mithl), meaning a fair market price, the person must pay it and cannot do tayammum. If the seller demands a gross overcharge (ghubn fahish), then he may do tayammum due to harm. The hashya explains that ghubn fahish is double the value or more. The ruling is based on the principle that financial harm is excused like physical harm. A qiyas is made: just as being able to pay the price of a slave prevents expiation by fasting (since one must free a slave if able), similarly being able to pay for water prevents tayammum.

Key Terms
ظن (zann): Estimation or strong probability; the standard for triggering the obligation to seek water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the maximum distance that triggers the obligation to seek water for tayammum?
A) Half a mile
B) Less than a mile
C) Two miles
D) Any distance if water is thought to exist

Key Takeaway
Seeking water before tayammum is wajib only when you think water is within a mile and you are safe.
