Purchasing Water and Gross Overcharge
Ruling on purchasing water and the effect of price on permissibility of tayammum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between fair price and gross overcharge (ghubn fahish) and state when tayammum is permissible if water is sold at an exorbitant price.

Core Idea
If water is sold at its like price or slight overcharge, you must buy it; but if the overcharge is double or more, you may do tayammum.

When water is available for purchase, the obligation to use water depends on the price. If the seller demands a fair market price (thaman mithl) or only a slight overcharge, you must pay and cannot do tayammum. However, if the seller demands a gross overcharge (ghubn fahish), defined as double the market value, then you may perform tayammum because of the harm to your wealth. This ruling is supported by a qiyas (analogy) to the case of buying a slave for expiation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three price scenarios
The text outlines three cases: (1) like price (thaman mithl), (2) slight overcharge (ghubn yasir), (3) gross overcharge (ghubn fahish).
The ruling for case 1 and 2 is the same: tayammum not allowed.
2
Define ghubn fahish
Ghubn fahish is defined in al-Nawadir as double the market value in that place. From Abu Hanifa: if water worth 2 dirhams is sold for 1.5, that is not fahish.
The threshold is specific to Hanafi school.
3
Apply the qiyas analogy
Just as ability to pay the price of a slave prevents expiation by fasting (one must free a slave if affordable), similarly ability to pay for water at like price prevents tayammum.
The effective cause ('illa) is capability to pay (milk al-thaman).
4
Determine the ruling for each scenario
For fair price or slight overcharge: tayammum is invalid, one must buy water. For gross overcharge: tayammum is valid due to harm.
Harm to wealth is treated like harm to self, as per the principle that Muslim's wealth is sacred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
طلب الماء: أطلقه فشمل ما إذا طلب بنفسه أو برسوله، والمقدار المذكور للطلب يعتبر من جانب ظنه، وإن ظنه في الجهات الأربع وجب الطلب منها وحد القرب أن يظن أن ما بينه وبين الماء دون ميل، والظن بقرب الماء يكون تارة برؤية طير، وتارة برؤية خضرة، وتارة بخبر مخبر. وإلا فلا أي وإن لم يظن قرب الماء، أو ظنه ولكن لا مع الأمن بأن خاف عدواً فلا يطلبه. [مراقي الفلاح: ١٢٤] إلا بثمن مثله هذه على ثلاثة أوجه إما إن أعطاه بمثل قيمته في أقرب موضع من المواضع التي يعز فيها الماء، أو بالغبن اليسير، أو بالغبن الفاحش، ففي الوجه الأول والثاني لا يجزئه التيمم؛ لتحقق القدرة على الماء؛ فإن القدرة على البذل قدرة على الماء، فيمتنع جواز التيمم كما أن القدرة على ثمن الرقبة تمنع التكفير بالصوم، وفي الوجه الثالث جاز له التيمم لوجود الضرر ؛ فإن حرمة مال المسلم كحرمة نفسه، والضرر في النفس مسقط، فكذا في المال. قيد لزوم الطلب بما إذا أمكن تحصيله بثمن المثل، فدخل ما إذا أمكن تحصيله بأقل. من ثمن مثله بالأولى، وألحق في لزوم الطلب ما إذا أمكن تحصيله بزيادة يسيرة واحترز به عما إذا أمكن تحصيله بغبن فاحش، وهو ما لا يدخل تحت تقويم المقومين قال في "النوادر : وهو ضعف القيمة في ذلك المكان، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة: إذا قدر أن يشتري ماء يساوي دره هما بدرهم ونصف، لا يتيمم
بيان لـ"ما"
لزمه شراؤه به إن كان معه فاضلا عن نفقته
Seeking water: He [the author] stated it generally, so it includes whether he seeks by himself or by his messenger. The mentioned amount for seeking is considered from the side of his estimation. If he thinks it is in the four directions, he must seek from them. The limit of nearness is that he thinks that between him and water is less than a mile. Thinking that water is near may occur sometimes by seeing a bird, sometimes by seeing greenery, sometimes by news from an informant. 'Otherwise no' meaning if he does not think water is near, or thinks it is near but without safety, i.e., he fears an enemy, then he does not seek it. [Maraqi al-Falah: 124] 'Except for its like price' has three aspects: either he gives it for its like value in the nearest place where water is scarce, or with a slight overcharge (ghubn yasir), or with a gross overcharge (ghubn fahish). In the first and second aspects, tayammum is not permissible for him because capability for water is established; indeed, capability to pay is capability to obtain water, so permissibility of tayammum is prevented, just as capability to pay the price of a slave prevents expiation by fasting. In the third aspect, tayammum is permissible for him due to harm; for the sanctity of a Muslim's wealth is like the sanctity of his self, and harm to the self removes the obligation, so likewise to wealth. He restricted the necessity of seeking to when it can be obtained at the like price; so it includes when it can be obtained for less than its like price by priority. And he attached to the necessity of seeking the case when it can be obtained with a slight increase, and thereby excluded the case when it can be obtained with a gross overcharge, which is that which does not fall under the valuation of valuators. He said in al-Nawadir: it is double the value in that place. And al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa: if he is able to buy water worth two dirhams for a dirham and a half, he does not perform tayammum.
Explanation of 'what' (ma): He must buy it with it if he has it surplus to his expenses.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This section covers two main obligations: seeking water and purchasing it. The seeking is obligatory up to 400 steps from where he thinks water might be, but only if he has a reasonable expectation of finding it and it is safe. The seeking must be done in the directions he suspects. If he cannot seek due to fear of enemies, the obligation drops. Then the text addresses purchasing water: if someone demands the like price (thaman mithl), meaning a fair market price, the person must pay it and cannot do tayammum. If the seller demands a gross overcharge (ghubn fahish), then he may do tayammum due to harm. The hashya explains that ghubn fahish is double the value or more. The ruling is based on the principle that financial harm is excused like physical harm. A qiyas is made: just as being able to pay the price of a slave prevents expiation by fasting (since one must free a slave if able), similarly being able to pay for water prevents tayammum.

Key Terms
الغبن الفاحش (al-ghubn al-fahish): Gross overcharge that does not fall under normal valuation; defined in al-Nawadir as double the value in that place.
ثمن المثل (thaman al-mithl): Fair market price; the price that would be given in a normal transaction without overcharge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Nawadir, what is ghubn fahish?
A) Any price above market
B) Double the market value
C) A price that the buyer cannot afford
D) A price set by a monopolist

Key Takeaway
You must buy water at its like price; only when the overcharge is double or more may you use tayammum.

Multiple Prayers with One Tayammum and Purification for the Wounded
Explains Hanafi ruling on multiple prayers with one tayammum and purification of wounded person.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on performing multiple prayers with one tayammum, explain the evidence against the Shafi'i view, and apply the rule for purifying with wounds based on whether the majority of the body is sound or wounded.

Core Idea
One tayammum for many prayers; for wounds, wash sound parts and wipe wounds; majority by limbs for wudu, area for ghusl.

This lesson addresses two crucial purification scenarios: the permissibility of using a single tayammum for multiple obligatory and voluntary prayers, and how a wounded person should perform purification. The Hanafi school takes a lenient view on tayammum, allowing multiple prayers, while the Shafi'i school requires renewal for each fard. For the wounded, the ruling depends on whether the majority of the body is sound or wounded, with a nuanced intra-madhhab difference on how to measure majority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is performing multiple prayers with one tayammum. The Hanafi position allows it; the Shafi'i requires a new tayammum for each fard prayer.
2
Examine the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafi school relies on the hadith 'the earth has been made for me a place of prayer and a means of purification' and the principle that a substitute follows the rules of the original. Since wudu suffices for multiple prayers until nullified, so does tayammum.
This hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i counter-dalil
The Shafi'i view considers tayammum a 'necessary purification' (taharat darurah), and necessity is limited to its extent. Thus, each fard requires a new tayammum.
4
Respond from the Hanafi side
The necessity is the absence of water, not the performance of each prayer; as long as water is absent, the necessity continues. It is recommended to repeat tayammum for each fard to exit the disagreement.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.
5
Apply the wounded person rules
If most of the body is wounded, perform tayammum; if most is sound, wash sound parts and wipe wounds. Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: majority measured by number of limbs (mukhtar) for wudu, by area for ghusl.
Special case: a person with amputated hands/feet and a facial wound prays without purification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويصلي بالتيمم الواحد ما شاء من الفرائض والنوافل، وصح تقديمه على الوقت، ولو كان أكثر البدن أو نصفه جريحا تيمم، وإن كان أكثره صحيحا غسله ومسح الجريح، ولا يجمع بين الغسل والتيمم، وينقضه ناقض الوضوء، والقدرة على استعمال الماء الكافي، ومقطوع اليدين والرجلين إذا كان بوجهه جراحة يصلي بغير طهارة ولا يعيد. وهو الأصح
ويصلي في وقت واحد أو أوقات متعددة ما لم يجد الماء أو يحدث (الكفاية) وعند الشافعي: يتيمم لكل فرض؛ لأنها طهارة ضرورية، فلا يصلي به أكثر من فريضة واحدة ويصلي به ما شاء من النوافل ما دام في الوقت، ولو تيمم للنافلة أن يودي به الفريضة، وعند الشافعي لا يجوز [الجوهرة النيرة: ٢٨/١] الفرائض والأولى إعادته لكل فرض خروجا من خلاف الشافعي، فإنه لا يصلي به عنده أكثر من فريضة واحدة، ويصلي به ما شاء من النوافل تبعا [مراقي الفلاح (۱۲٥] أكثر إلخ: اعلم أن الكثرة تعتبر من حيث عدد الأعضاء في المختار، فإذا كان بالرأس والوجه واليدين جراحة - ولو قلت - وليس بالرجلين جراحة تيمم، ومنهم من اعتبرها في نفس كل عضو، فإن كان أكثر كل عضو منها جريحاً تيمم، وإلا فلا مراقي الفلاح (١٥] لا يخفى أن هذا الخلاف إنما هو في الوضوء، وأما في الغسل، فالظاهر اعتبار الكثرة من حيث المساحة. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٢٦] البدن: الأولى للمصنف حذف "البدن"، ويقول: ولو كان الأكثر من الأعضاء أو النصف منها جريحاً تيمم؛ ليكون كلامه متناولاً للصغرى والكبرى. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۱۲٦] تيمم أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان الجريح متيمم، وهذا على الأصح من المذهب، وقيل: يغسل الصحيح ويمسح الجريح [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٢٦] أكثره: وإن كان النصف جريحاً والنصف صحيحاً لا رواية فيه، واختلف فيه المشايخ: فمنهم من أوجب التيمم؛ لأنه طهارة كاملة، أوجب غسل الصحيح ومسح الجريح؛ لأنهما طهارة حقيقية وحكمية، فكان ومنهم من أولى. ومسح الجريح أفاد بإطلاقه أن المسح على حسب الاستطاعة، فبمرور يده على الجسد إن استطاع، وإن لم يستطع فعلى خرقةٍ، وإن ضره تركه [مراقي الفلاح: ١٢٦]
الوضوء لو قال: "ناقض الأصل؛ ليعم الغسل والوضوء لكان أحسن وأجاب الحموي بأن المراد بالوضوء الطهارة أعم من أن تكون عن حدث أو جنابة، بطريق استعمال الخاص في العام مجازاً. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٢٦] الكافي : أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان يكفيه مرة مرة، فلو ثلث الغسل، وفني الماء قبل إكمال الوضوء، بطل تيممه في المختار؛ لانتهاء طهورية التراب بالحديث. [مراقي الفلاح: ١٢٧]
And he may pray with one tayammum as many obligatory and supererogatory prayers as he wishes, and its performance is valid before the time. And if most of the body or half of it is wounded, he performs tayammum; if most of it is sound, he washes the sound parts and wipes the wound. And one does not combine ghusl and tayammum. And it (tayammum) is nullified by whatever nullifies wudu, and by the ability to use sufficient water. And a person with amputated hands and feet, if he has a wound on his face, prays without purification and does not repeat. And that is the most sound opinion.
He prays in one time or multiple times as long as he does not find water or becomes hadath. According to al-Shafi'i: he performs tayammum for every obligatory prayer because it is a necessary purification, so he cannot pray more than one obligatory prayer with it, but he may pray as many supererogatory prayers as he wishes within the time. If he performs tayammum for a supererogatory prayer, he can also perform the obligatory prayer with it, but according to al-Shafi'i it is not permissible. [al-Jawhara al-Nayyira 1/28] The obligatory prayers: it is recommended to repeat tayammum for every obligatory prayer to exit the disagreement with al-Shafi'i, for according to him he cannot pray more than one obligatory prayer with it, and he may pray as many supererogatory prayers as he wishes. [Maraqi al-Falah 125] 'More' etc.: Know that the majority is considered in terms of the number of limbs in the chosen view. So if there are wounds on the head, face, and hands - even if few - and no wounds on the feet, he performs tayammum. Some consider it in the same limb: if the majority of each limb is wounded, he performs tayammum, otherwise not. [Maraqi al-Falah 15] It is not hidden that this difference is only in wudu; as for ghusl, the apparent is to consider the majority by area. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 126] 'Al-badan': It would have been better for the author to drop 'al-badan' and say: 'If the majority of the limbs or half of them are wounded, he performs tayammum' so that his speech covers both minor and major. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 126] 'Tayammum': He stated it generally, so it includes if the wounded person is in a state of janabah. This is the most sound opinion of the madhhab. It is said: he washes the sound parts and wipes the wound. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 126] 'Most of it': If half is wounded and half sound, there is no narration, and the mashayikh differed. Some obliged tayammum because it is a complete purification, others obliged washing the sound and wiping the wound because they are real and ruling purification, and that is more appropriate. And wiping the wound indicates by its generality that wiping is according to ability: if he can, he passes his hand over his body; if he cannot, he wipes with a cloth; if it harms him, he leaves it. [Maraqi al-Falah 126]
'Wudu': If he said 'nullifier of the origin' to include ghusl and wudu, that would be better, and al-Hamawi replied that by 'wudu' is meant purification, general whether from hadath or janabah, by way of using the specific for the general metaphorically. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 126] 'Al-kafi': He stated it generally, so it includes if it suffices once; if he begins ghusl and the water runs out before completing wudu, his tayammum is invalid in the chosen view because the earth loses its purifying property by hadath. [Maraqi al-Falah 127]
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This lesson has two main parts: the permissibility of multiple prayers with one tayammum, and the rulings for a wounded person. For the first, the Hanafi school holds that one tayammum suffices for multiple prayers (fard and nafl) as long as one has not found water or nullified the tayammum. This is in opposition to Shafi'i who requires a new tayammum for each fard prayer. The Hanafi position is based on the principle that tayammum is a substitute for wudu and ghusl, and substitutes follow the same rules. The text also notes that it is recommended to repeat tayammum for each fard to avoid the disagreement with Shafi'i. For the wounded person, the ruling depends on whether the majority of the body is wounded or sound. If most of the body is wounded, tayammum is performed; if most is sound, one washes the sound parts and wipes over the wounds. There is a difference of opinion on how to measure majority: by number of limbs or by area per limb. The preferred view in wudu is by number of limbs, but in ghusl by area. Special cases: a person with no hands/feet and a facial wound prays without any purification and does not repeat.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry purification with earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
ناقض الوضوء (naqid al-wudu): Things that nullify wudu, such as breaking wind, urination, etc., which also nullify tayammum.
مجروح (majruh): A person with wounds on the body; special rules apply for purification depending on the extent of wounds.
أكثر البدن (akthar al-badan): Majority of the body; considered by number of limbs or area depending on context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what nullifies tayammum?
A) Completion of one fard prayer
B) Finding water or a nullifier of wudu
C) The passage of its time
D) Intention to pray the next prayer

Key Takeaway
One tayammum remains valid for multiple prayers until water is found or a nullifier occurs; for wounds, purification depends on majority soundness, measured by limbs for wudu and area for ghusl.

intermediate
8 min
Multiple Prayers with One Tayammum
Ruling with proof and dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing multiple obligatory prayers with a single tayammum and explain the dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
One tayammum suffices for any number of prayers—it is a full substitute, not a limited concession.

You know tayammum is a dry purification when water is unavailable. But how many prayers can you pray with one tayammum? This lesson dives into the Hanafi position and the Shafi'i counterview.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act? Tayammum. What is the ruling? One tayammum suffices for multiple prayers. Note the hukm level: it is valid (sahih).
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites al-Kifaya: 'He prays in one time or multiple times as long as he does not find water or does not break wudu.' This is based on the principle that tayammum is a badal (substitute).
The dalil is a proof from the Sunna/consensus, though not directly quoted.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Tayammum is a complete substitute for wudu, so it remains valid until nullified. The Shafi'i argument is that it is a darura (necessity) limited to one fard.
The Hanafi view relies on istihsan (juristic preference) for the substitute nature.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that each fard prayer requires its own tayammum. The thamarah al-khilaf is practical: Hanafi can pray all fard in one go.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The text recommends renewing tayammum for each fard to avoid disagreement, but the relied-upon position is that one suffices.
The mufta bihi is the Hanafi position; renewal is precaution (ihtiyat).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة ٤٦ أحكام التيمم بيان لـ'ما' لزمه شراؤه به إن كان معه فاضلا عن نفقته، ويصلي بالتيمم الواحد ما شاء من الفرائض والنوافل، وصح تقديمه على الوقت، ولو كان أكثر البدن أو نصفه جريحا تيمم، وإن كان أكثره صحيحا غسله ومسح الجريح، ولا يجمع بين الغسل والتيمم، وينقضه ناقض الوضوء، والقدرة على استعمال الماء الكافي، ومقطوع اليدين والرجلين إذا كان بوجهه جراحة يصلي بغير طهارة ولا يعيد. وهو الأصح مبتدأ لزمه شراؤه إلخ: اعلم أن شروط لزوم الشراء ثلاثة كما بينا، فلا يلزم الشراء لو طلب الغبن الفاحش، أو طلب ثمن المثل وليس معه فلا يستدين للماء، أو احتاجه لنفقته. مراقي الفلاح ١٢٥ ويصلي في وقت واحد أو أوقات متعددة ما لم يجد الماء أو يحدث (الكفاية) وعند الشافعي: يتيمم لكل فرض؛ لأنها طهارة ضرورية، فلا يصلي به أكثر من فريضة واحدة ويصلي به ما شاء من النوافل ما دام في الوقت، ولو تيمم للنافلة أن يودي به الفريضة، وعند الشافعي لا يجوز [الجوهرة النيرة: ٢٨/١] الفرائض والأولى إعادته لكل فرض خروجا من خلاف الشافعي ، فإنه لا يصلي به عنده أكثر من فريضة واحدة، ويصلي به ما شاء من النوافل تبعا [مراقي الفلاح (۱۲٥] أكثر إلخ: اعلم أن الكثرة تعتبر من حيث عدد الأعضاء في المختار، فإذا كان بالرأس والوجه واليدين جراحة - ولو قلت - وليس بالرجلين جراحة تيمم، ومنهم من اعتبرها في نفس كل عضو، فإن كان أكثر كل عضو منها جريحاً تيمم، وإلا فلا مراقي الفلاح (١٥] لا يخفى أن هذا الخلاف إنما هو في الوضوء، وأما في الغسل، فالظاهر اعتبار الكثرة من حيث المساحة. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٢٦] البدن: الأولى للمصنف حذف 'البدن'، ويقول: ولو كان الأكثر من الأعضاء أو النصف منها جريحاً تيمم؛ ليكون كلامه متناولاً للصغرى والكبرى. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۱۲٦] تيمم أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان الجريح متيمم، وهذا على الأصح من المذهب، وقيل: يغسل الصحيح ويمسح الجريح [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٢٦] أكثره: وإن كان النصف جريحاً والنصف صحيحاً لا رواية فيه، واختلف فيه المشايخ: فمنهم من أوجب التيمم؛ لأنه طهارة كاملة، أوجب غسل الصحيح ومسح الجريح؛ لأنهما طهارة حقيقية وحكمية، فكان ومنهم من أولى. ومسح الجريح أفاد بإطلاقه أن المسح على حسب الاستطاعة، فبمرور يده على الجسد إن استطاع ، وإن لم يستطع فعلى خرقةٍ، وإن ضره تركه [مراقي الفلاح: ١٢٦] الوضوء لو قال: 'ناقض الأصل؛ ليعم الغسل والوضوء لكان أحسن وأجاب الحموي بأن المراد بالوضوء الطهارة أعم من أن تكون عن حدث أو جنابة، بطريق استعمال الخاص في العام مجازاً. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٢٦] الكافي : أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان يكفيه مرة مرة، فلو ثلث الغسل، وفني الماء قبل إكمال الوضوء، بطل تيممه في المختار؛ لانتهاء طهورية التراب بالحديث. [مراقي الفلاح: ١٢٧]
The Book of Purification. Section on Tayammum. Explanation: It is obligatory for him to buy water if he has surplus beyond his expenses. He may pray with one tayammum as many obligatory and supererogatory prayers as he wishes. It is valid to perform it before the time. If most of the body or half of it is wounded, he makes tayammum. If most of it is healthy, he washes the healthy and wipes the wound. He should not combine washing (ghusl) and tayammum. It is nullified by nullifiers of wudu and by ability to use sufficient water. One with amputated hands and feet who has a wound on his face prays without purification and does not repeat. This is the most correct. 'It is obligatory for him to buy water etc.': Know that the conditions for obligation of purchase are three as we explained. Purchase is not obligatory if he demands excessive profit, or demands the equivalent price and he does not have it, so he does not borrow for water, or if he needs it for his expenses. (Maraqi al-Falah 125) He prays in one time or multiple times as long as he does not find water or does not break wudu (al-Kifaya). According to al-Shafi'i, he makes tayammum for every obligatory prayer because it is a necessitated purification, so he cannot pray more than one obligatory prayer with it, but he may pray as many supererogatory prayers as he wishes within the time. If he makes tayammum for a supererogatory prayer, he cannot perform an obligatory prayer with it. According to al-Shafi'i it is not permissible (al-Jawhara al-Nayyira 1/28). It is better to renew it for each obligatory prayer to avoid disagreement with al-Shafi'i, for he does not pray more than one obligatory prayer with it according to him. 'Most of the body etc.': Know that majority is considered by number of limbs according to the chosen view. If there is a wound on the head, face, and hands, even if small, and there is no wound on the feet, he makes tayammum. Some scholars consider majority within each limb: if most of each limb is wounded, he makes tayammum; otherwise not (Maraqi al-Falah 15). It is not hidden that this difference is only in wudu; as for ghusl, the apparent view is to consider majority by area. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 126). 'Body': The author should have omitted 'body' and said: if most of the limbs or half of them are wounded, he makes tayammum, so that his statement includes the minor and major. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 126). 'Tayammum' is absolute and includes the case where the wounded person makes tayammum. This is the most correct in the madhhab. It is said: he washes the healthy and wipes the wound. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 126). 'Most of it': If half is wounded and half is healthy, there is no transmission (riwaya). Scholars differed: some obligated tayammum because it is a complete purification; others obligated washing the healthy and wiping the wound because they are real and ruling purifications, and whichever is more preferable. Wiping the wound, by its absolute expression, indicates that wiping is according to ability: by passing his hand over the body if able; if not able, then over a cloth; if it harms him, he leaves it. (Maraqi al-Falah 126). 'Wudu': If he had said 'nullifier of the origin' to include ghusl and wudu, it would have been better. Al-Hamawi responded that 'wudu' here means purification, whether from minor or major impurity, using the specific for the general metaphorically. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 126). 'Sufficient': It is absolute and includes if it is sufficient once or twice. If he starts washing, and the water runs out before completing wudu, his tayammum becomes invalid according to the chosen view, because the purification of soil ends with the hadith. (Maraqi al-Falah 127).
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Nur al-Idah, explaining multiple rulings of tayammum. The author begins by stating the obligation to buy water if one has surplus beyond essential expenses; this is conditional on not being cheated, not having to borrow, and not needing the money for essentials. Then, he clarifies that a single tayammum suffices for any number of obligatory and supererogatory prayers, valid before the prayer time. This is in contrast to Imam al-Shafi'i, who requires separate tayammum for each obligatory prayer. The Hanafi position is based on the principle that tayammum is a complete substitute for wudu, and its validity continues until nullified. The passage then addresses the case of a wounded person: if more than half the body (or limbs) is wounded, tayammum is made; if more than half is healthy, the healthy parts are washed and the wound is merely wiped. The text discusses the criteria for 'majority' by limb count, with a difference of opinion on whether to consider each limb individually or the whole. In ghusl, area is considered. The nullifiers of tayammum are those of wudu and the ability to use sufficient water. A person with amputated limbs and a facial wound prays without any purification and does not repeat. The commentary ends with a note that if water runs out during wudu, tayammum is invalidated because the soil's purification ends with the hadith.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ritual purification using clean soil as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or cannot be used.
ناقض الوضوء (naqid al-wudu): Anything that invalidates wudu, which also nullifies tayammum.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many obligatory prayers can one perform with a single tayammum?
A) Only one obligatory prayer
B) Any number of obligatory prayers as long as no nullifier occurs
C) Only one obligatory prayer and any number of supererogatory prayers
D) Only supererogatory prayers, not obligatory

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, one tayammum suffices for all prayers until water is found or wudu is broken.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
Tayammum for the Wounded: Majority Wounds and Mixed States
Expounds rulings on tayammum for the wounded and nullifiers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine when a wounded person must perform tayammum instead of washing the healthy parts, and identify the nullifiers of tayammum.

Core Idea
If wounds cover most of the body or limbs, tayammum replaces wudu; if mostly healthy, wash healthy and wipe wounds.

A person with wounds cannot fully use water. How should they purify? The Hanafi school provides detailed criteria based on majority of wounds, considering limbs individually or the whole body. This lesson unpacks these rules and also explains what nullifies tayammum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act is purification for prayer when a person has wounds. The ruling depends on the extent of wounds.
2
Classify the wounded person
Determine if the majority of the body (or limbs) is wounded. If most is wounded, tayammum is performed. If most is healthy, wash healthy parts and wipe over wounds.
3
Apply the majority criterion
There is a dispute: some say majority by limb count, others by area within each limb. The chosen view (mukhtar) is by limb count. For ghusl, area is considered.
4
Handle the half-wounded case
If exactly half wounded and half healthy, there is no transmitted ruling; scholars differed: some say tayammum, others say wash healthy and wipe wounds.
5
Identify nullifiers
Tayammum is nullified by any wudu nullifier and by the ability to use sufficient water. Also, if water runs out during wudu, tayammum is invalidated.

Source Text

Basic Ruling and First Condition for Wiping over Khuffs
Opens chapter on masah with ruling and first condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of wiping over khuffs and explain the first condition regarding the timing of wearing them.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs is a sunna for minor impurity, provided the khuffs are worn after washing the feet.

This lesson introduces the chapter on wiping over khuffs (khuffain) from Nur al-Idah. The ruling is that wiping is valid for minor impurity, not major, and for both men and women. The text lists seven conditions but details only the first: wearing the khuffs after washing the feet, even before completing wudu, as long as wudu is completed before a nullifier occurs. The commentary clarifies that wiping is not obligatory (unlike tayammum) and that it is a sunna.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being discussed and its legal category (fard/sunnah/mubah). The text says 'sahha al-mash' meaning it is valid (sahih) and the commentary notes it is not obligatory.
Wiping is a substitute for washing; its validity does not mean obligation.
2
List the conditions mentioned
The text states seven conditions but only elaborates the first: wearing after washing both feet. Note the condition that wudu must be completed before any nullifier.
The condition allows wearing before completing wudu if wudu is later completed before breaking.
3
Analyze the commentary on 'sahh'
Al-Ayni explains that 'sahh' indicates it is valid but not obligatory, unlike tayammum which is obligatory when water is present.
This distinguishes mash from other substitutes.
4
Exclude major impurity
The text restricts to 'minor impurity', thus wiping is not allowed for janaba (major impurity). The commentary provides a hypothetical scenario for a junub to illustrate.
This is a key limitation based on Hadith.

Source Text

كتاب الطهارة ٤٧ المسح على الخفين باب المسح على الخفين صح المسح على الخفين في الحدث الأصغر للرجال والنساء، ولو كانا من شيء ثخين غير الجلد سواء كان لهما نعل من جلد أو لا. [شروط جوازه ] ويشترط الجواز المسح على الخفين سبعة شرائط : الأول: لبسهما بعد غسل الرجلين ولو قبل كمال الوضوء، إذا أتمه قبل حصول ناقض للوضوء ولو كان اللبس قبل كمال الوضوء. صح إلخ: قال العيني: ونبه بقوله: 'صح' على أنه إذا ترك المسح فلا بأس عليه، بخلاف التيمم؛ فإنه فرض عند الماء. الشلبي على تبيين الحقائق (۱۳۷۱] الأصغر: قيد به فخرجت به الجنابة ونحوها، فإنه لا فيها المسح؛ لورود النص بذلك، وصوّر حافظ الدين في 'الكافي' صورة مسح الجنب تقريباً للمتعلم: بأن توضاً ولبس جوربين مجلدين ثم أجنب، ليس له أن يشدهما ويغسل سائر جسده مضطجعا أو مادا رجليه على شيء مرتفع ويمسح عليه [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٢٨] من شيء ثخين إلخ : أي يجوز المسح على الجورب إذا كان منعلاً أو مجلداً أو ثخيناً، والمجلد: هو الذي وضع الجلد على أعلاه ،وأسفله والمنعل هو الذي وضع الجلد على أسفله كالنعل للقدم، وقيل: يكون إلى الكعب، وأما الثخين فالمذكور وحده: أن يستمسك على الساق من غير ربط وأن لا يرى ما تحته وقال أبو حنيفة : لا يجوز المسح عليه، ويروى رجوع أبي حنيفة إلى قولهما قبل موته بثلاثة أيام وقيل بسبعة أيام وعليه الفتوى. [تبيين الحقائق: ١٥١/١] واعلم أن المسألة على ثلاثة وجوه إن كانا رقيقين غير منعلين لا يجوز المسح عليهما اتفاقاً، وإن كانا ثخينين منعلين اتفاقاً، وإن كانا ثخينين غير منعلين فهو محل الاختلاف [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۱۲۸] غسل الرجلين أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان الغسل حكما كجبيرة بالرجلين أو بإحداهما مسحهما ولبس الخف، الجبيرة كالغسل مراقي الفلاح (۱۲۹]. فلو مسح جبيرة إحدى رجليه، ولبس الخف في إحدى رجليه، لا يجوز المسح عليه؛ لأنه يصير جامعاً بين الغسل والمسح. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٢٩] ولو أي ولو كان اللبس قبل كمال الوضوء. مراقي الفلاح: (۱۲۹] ولو لبسهما بعد الغسل جاز المسح؛ لأنه وضوء وزيادة، إلا إذا كان متيمماً فلابد من نزعهما إذا وجد الماء. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٢٩] قبل كمال إلخ: فلو غسل رجليه ولبس خفيه وأحدث قبل تمام الوضوء، لابد من نزعهما. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٢٩] جاز يمسح خفه؛ لأن مسح
Book of Purification 47: Wiping over Khuffs. Chapter on Wiping over Khuffs. Wiping over khuffs is valid for minor impurity for men and women, even if they are made of thick material other than leather, whether they have a leather sole or not. [Conditions for its Permissibility] And for the permissibility of wiping over khuffs, seven conditions are required: First: Wearing them after washing both feet, even if before completing wudu, provided he completes wudu before a nullifier occurs, even if the wearing was before completing wudu. 'Is valid etc.': al-Ayni said: By his statement 'is valid' he indicates that if one leaves wiping, there is no sin on him, unlike tayammum, for it is obligatory when water is present. Al-Shalabi on Tabyin al-Haqa'iq (1371). 'Minor': He restricted it, thus excluding major impurity and the like, for wiping is not done there due to the text that came. Hafiz al-Din in al-Kafi depicted a case of a junub wiping approximately for the learner: that he performs wudu and wears two leather-lined socks, then becomes junub; he does not have to remove them and washes the rest of his body lying down or stretching his legs on something elevated and wipes over them. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 128). 'Of thick material etc.': That is, wiping over socks is permissible if they are soled, leather-covered, or thick. Al-mujallad is that which has leather placed on its top and bottom. Al-mun'al is that which has leather placed on its bottom like a sole for the foot. It is said it extends to the ankle. As for the thick, it is mentioned alone: that it stays on the shin without tying and that what is underneath is not visible. Abu Hanifa said: wiping over it is not permissible, and it is reported that Abu Hanifa retracted to their view three days before his death, and some say seven days, and the fatwa is upon that. (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 1/151). Know that the matter is on three cases: if they are thin and unsoled, wiping over them is not permissible by agreement; if they are thick and soled, it is permissible by agreement; if they are thick and unsoled, that is the place of disagreement. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 128). 'Washing both feet': It is absolute and includes the case where the washing is legal, like a splint on both feet or one of them, wiping them and wearing the khuff; the splint is like washing. (Maraqi al-Falah 129). So if one wiped a splint on one foot and wore the khuff on one foot, it is not permissible to wipe over it because it becomes a combination of washing and wiping. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 129). 'Even if' meaning even if the wearing was before completing wudu. (Maraqi al-Falah 129). If he wears them after washing, wiping is permissible because it is wudu and extra, except if he is mutayammim, then he must remove them when he finds water. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 129). 'Before completing etc.': So if he washed his feet and wore his khuffs and then broke wudu before completing wudu, he must remove them. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 129). It is permissible to wipe his khuff because wiping...
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on wiping over khuffs (leather socks) from Nur al-Idah with commentary. The ruling: wiping over khuffs is valid for minor impurity (not major) for both men and women, even if the khuffs are made of thick material other than leather. Seven conditions are required; the text only details the first: wearing after washing both feet, even before completing wudu, as long as wudu is completed before any nullifier. The commentary by al-Ayni notes that wiping is not obligatory (sunna) unlike tayammum. The text then discusses the material: wiping is allowed on socks that are soled (mun'al), leather-covered (mujallad), or thick (thakhin). There is a famous intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa initially disallowed wiping on thick unsoled socks, but he reportedly retracted to the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the sahibayn) before his death, and the fatwa is now on their position. The passage clarifies three cases: thin unsoled socks (no wiping by agreement), thick soled socks (wiping allowed by agreement), thick unsoled socks (the point of disagreement, now resolved with the retraction). The later commentary discusses washing of feet: if one has a splint (jabira) on the foot, wiping over it counts as washing, and one cannot combine splint wiping and khuff wiping on different feet. Also, if one wears khuffs after ghusl, wiping is allowed, but a mutayammim must remove them when water is found. If wudu is broken before completing wudu, wearing the khuffs is invalid and they must be removed. The text ends mid-sentence.

Key Terms
خف (khuff): A foot covering, traditionally made of leather, worn over the foot for wiping.
مسح (mash): Wiping over the khuff with wet hands as a substitute for washing the feet in wudu.
حدث أصغر (hadath asghar): Minor impurity that necessitates wudu, such as passing wind, urine, or stool.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first condition, when must the khuffs be worn?
A) Only after completing the entire wudu
B) After washing both feet, but wudu must be completed before a nullifier occurs
C) At any time, even before washing the feet
D) Only after taking a full bath (ghusl)

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuffs is a sunna for minor impurity, conditional on wearing the khuffs after washing the feet and completing wudu before any break.

Material Requirements and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains material conditions and intra-Hanafi disagreement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three categories of socks (thin unsoled, thick soled, thick unsoled) and state the relied-upon Hanafi position on wiping over thick unsoled socks.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school now permits wiping over thick unsoled socks, due to Abu Hanifa's retraction to the view of his two students.

This lesson delves into the material requirements for a khuff to be valid for wiping. The text clarifies that wiping is allowed on socks that are either soled (mun'al), leather-covered (mujallad), or thick (thakhin). A famous intra-Hanafi dispute is then presented: Imam Abu Hanifa initially forbade wiping on thick unsoled socks, but he retracted to the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, making it permissible. The fatwa now follows this permissive position. The lesson also outlines three scenarios with different rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the material categories
The text mentions three types of socks that qualify: soled (mun'al), leather-covered (mujallad), and thick (thakhin). Understand each definition from the commentary.
Thick means it stays on without tying and does not reveal the foot.
2
Understand the three cases
The text outlines three cases: thin unsoled (no wiping by agreement), thick soled (wiping allowed by agreement), thick unsoled (area of dispute). This clarifies where ikhtilaf occurs.
The third case is the subject of the intra-Hanafi dispute.
3
Trace the dispute
Abu Hanifa's original view was prohibition; his two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) allowed it. He reportedly retracted to their view before his death, and the fatwa is now on permissibility.
The retraction shows the evolution of Hanafi doctrine.
4
Apply the mufta bihi
Know that the relied-upon position today is the permissibility of wiping over thick unsoled socks, as stated in the text: 'wa alayhi al-fatwa'.
This is the operative ruling for practice.

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on wiping over khuffs (leather socks) from Nur al-Idah with commentary. The ruling: wiping over khuffs is valid for minor impurity (not major) for both men and women, even if the khuffs are made of thick material other than leather. Key Terms
منعل (mun'al): A sock that has a leather sole attached to its bottom, like a shoe sole.
مجلد (mujallad): A sock that is covered with leather on both the top and bottom.
ثخين (thakhin): Thick; a condition for socks to qualify for wiping, meaning they stay on without tying and do not reveal the foot.

Special Cases: Splints, Tayammum, and Timing of Wearing
Adds special case rulings for splints, tayammum, and timing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rulings for wiping over khuffs in special situations involving splints, tayammum, and incomplete wudu at the time of wearing.

Core Idea
If wudu is broken before completion, the khuffs must be removed; a splint on the foot counts as washing; and a mutayammim must remove khuffs when water is found.

This lesson continues the discussion of conditions for wiping over khuffs, focusing on three special cases. First, if a person wears khuffs after washing his feet but then breaks wudu before completing the rest, the wearing is invalid and he must remove them for proper wudu. Second, the text discusses the case of a splint (jabira) on the foot: wiping over the splint is considered equivalent to washing, and one cannot combine wiping over a splint on one foot with wearing a khuff on the other. Third, if a person is in a state of tayammum (dry ablution) and wears khuffs, then finds water, he must remove the khuffs for proper wudu because his tayammum is nullified. The passage ends mid-sentence but these points are clear.

Guided Path
1
Understand the timing condition for wearing
Review the first condition: wearing after washing feet. The commentary adds that if wudu is broken before completion, the wearing becomes invalid and khuffs must be removed for a proper wudu.
This is an extension of the first condition.
2
Analyze the splint (jabira) case
The text says that a splint on the foot is legally considered like washing (ghusl hukmi). If one has a splint on one foot and wears a khuff on the other, wiping over the khuff is not permissible because it combines washing (via splint) and wiping, which is inconsistent.
This prevents mixing different modes of purification.
3
Examine the tayammum situation
If a person performs tayammum and wears khuffs, then finds water, he must remove the khuffs and perform wudu (including washing feet). The reason is that tayammum is only a temporary substitute and is nullified by the presence of water.
This underscores the conditional nature of tayammum.

كتاب الطهارة ٤٧ المسح على الخفين باب المسح على الخفين صح المسح على الخفين في الحدث الأصغر للرجال والنساء، ولو كانا من شيء ثخين غير الجلد سواء كان لهما نعل من جلد أو لا. [شروط جوازه ] ويشترط الجواز المسح على الخفين سبعة شرائط : الأول: لبسهما بعد غسل الرجلين ولو قبل كمال الوضوء، إذا أتمه قبل حصول ناقض للوضوء ولو كان اللبس قبل كمال الوضوء. صح إلخ: قال العيني: ونبه بقوله: 'صح' على أنه إذا ترك المسح فلا بأس عليه، بخلاف التيمم؛ فإنه فرض عند الماء. الشلبي على تبيين الحقائق (۱۳۷۱] الأصغر: قيد به فخرجت به الجنابة ونحوها، فإنه لا فيها المسح؛ لورود النص بذلك، وصوّر حافظ الدين في 'الكافي' صورة مسح الجنب تقريباً للمتعلم: بأن توضاً ولبس جوربين مجلدين ثم أجنب، ليس له أن يشدهما ويغسل سائر جسده مضطجعا أو مادا رجليه على شيء مرتفع ويمسح عليه [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٢٨] من شيء ثخين إلخ : أي يجوز المسح على الجورب إذا كان منعلاً أو مجلداً أو ثخيناً، والمجلد: هو الذي وضع الجلد على أعلاه ،وأسفله والمنعل هو الذي وضع الجلد على أسفله كالنعل للقدم، وقيل: يكون إلى الكعب، وأما الثخين فالمذكور وحده: أن يستمسك على الساق من غير ربط وأن لا يرى ما تحته وقال أبو حنيفة : لا يجوز المسح عليه، ويروى رجوع أبي حنيفة إلى قولهما قبل موته بثلاثة أيام وقيل بسبعة أيام وعليه الفتوى. [تبيين الحقائق: ١٥١/١] واعلم أن المسألة على ثلاثة وجوه إن كانا رقيقين غير منعلين لا يجوز المسح عليهما اتفاقاً، وإن كانا ثخينين منعلين اتفاقاً، وإن كانا ثخينين غير منعلين فهو محل الاختلاف [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۱۲۸] غسل الرجلين أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان الغسل حكما كجبيرة بالرجلين أو بإحداهما مسحهما ولبس الخف، الجبيرة كالغسل مراقي الفلاح (۱۲۹]. فلو مسح جبيرة إحدى رجليه، ولبس الخف في إحدى رجليه، لا يجوز المسح عليه؛ لأنه يصير جامعاً بين الغسل والمسح. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٢٩] ولو أي ولو كان اللبس قبل كمال الوضوء. مراقي الفلاح: (۱۲۹] ولو لبسهما بعد الغسل جاز المسح؛ لأنه وضوء وزيادة، إلا إذا كان متيمماً فلابد من نزعهما إذا وجد الماء. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٢٩] قبل كمال إلخ: فلو غسل رجليه ولبس خفيه وأحدث قبل تمام الوضوء، لابد من نزعهما. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٢٩] جاز يمسح خفه؛ لأن مسح
Book of Purification 47: Wiping over Khuffs. Chapter on Wiping over Khuffs. Wiping over khuffs is valid for minor impurity for men and women, even if they are made of thick material other than leather, whether they have a leather sole or not. [Conditions for its Permissibility] And for the permissibility of wiping over khuffs, seven conditions are required: First: Wearing them after washing both feet, even if before completing wudu, provided he completes wudu before a nullifier occurs, even if the wearing was before completing wudu. 'Is valid etc.': al-Ayni said: By his statement 'is valid' he indicates that if one leaves wiping, there is no sin on him, unlike tayammum, for it is obligatory when water is present. Al-Shalabi on Tabyin al-Haqa'iq (1371). 'Minor': He restricted it, thus excluding major impurity and the like, for wiping is not done there due to the text that came. Hafiz al-Din in al-Kafi depicted a case of a junub wiping approximately for the learner: that he performs wudu and wears two leather-lined socks, then becomes junub; he does not have to remove them and washes the rest of his body lying down or stretching his legs on something elevated and wipes over them. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 128). 'Of thick material etc.': That is, wiping over socks is permissible if they are soled, leather-covered, or thick. Al-mujallad is that which has leather placed on its top and bottom. Al-mun'al is that which has leather placed on its bottom like a sole for the foot. It is said it extends to the ankle. As for the thick, it is mentioned alone: that it stays on the shin without tying and that what is underneath is not visible. Abu Hanifa said: wiping over it is not permissible, and it is reported that Abu Hanifa retracted to their view three days before his death, and some say seven days, and the fatwa is upon that. (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 1/151). Know that the matter is on three cases: if they are thin and unsoled, wiping over them is not permissible by agreement; if they are thick and soled, it is permissible by agreement; if they are thick and unsoled, that is the place of disagreement. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 128). 'Washing both feet': It is absolute and includes the case where the washing is legal, like a splint on both feet or one of them, wiping them and wearing the khuff; the splint is like washing. (Maraqi al-Falah 129). So if one wiped a splint on one foot and wore the khuff on one foot, it is not permissible to wipe over it because it becomes a combination of washing and wiping. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 129). 'Even if' meaning even if the wearing was before completing wudu. (Maraqi al-Falah 129). If he wears them after washing, wiping is permissible because it is wudu and extra, except if he is mutayammim, then he must remove them when he finds water. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 129). 'Before completing etc.': So if he washed his feet and wore his khuffs and then broke wudu before completing wudu, he must remove them. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 129). It is permissible to wipe his khuff because wiping...
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on wiping over khuffs (leather socks) from Nur al-Idah with commentary. The ruling: wiping over khuffs is valid for minor impurity (not major) for both men and women, even if the khuffs are made of thick material other than leather. Seven conditions are required; the text only details the first: wearing after washing both feet, even before completing wudu, as long as wudu is completed before any nullifier. The commentary by al-Ayni notes that wiping is not obligatory (sunna) unlike tayammum. The text then discusses the material: wiping is allowed on socks that are soled (mun'al), leather-covered (mujallad), or thick (thakhin). There is a famous intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa initially disallowed wiping on thick unsoled socks, but he reportedly retracted to the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the sahibayn) before his death, and the fatwa is now on their position. The passage clarifies three cases: thin unsoled socks (no wiping by agreement), thick soled socks (wiping allowed by agreement), thick unsoled socks (the point of disagreement, now resolved with the retraction). The later commentary discusses washing of feet: if one has a splint (jabira) on the foot, wiping over it counts as washing, and one cannot combine splint wiping and khuff wiping on different feet. Also, if one wears khuffs after ghusl, wiping is allowed, but a mutayammim must remove them when water is found. If wudu is broken before completing wudu, wearing the khuffs is invalid and they must be removed. The text ends mid-sentence.

Key Terms
جبيرة (jabira): A splint or cast used for a broken bone; in fiqh, wiping over it counts as washing.
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution using clean earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must a mutayammim do if he finds water while wearing khuffs after performing tayammum?
A) He may continue to wipe over the khuffs
B) He must remove the khuffs and perform wudu
C) He may perform tayammum again
D) He needs to remove only one khuff

Key Takeaway
Special conditions: mixing splint and khuff on different feet invalidates wiping; broken wudu before completion requires removing khuffs; and a mutayammim must remove khuffs upon finding water.

Ruling and First Condition of Wiping over Khuffayn
Ruling and first condition of wiping over khuff, with intra-Hanafi dispute on thick socks.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping over khuffayn and apply the first condition regarding washing the feet before wearing them.

Core Idea
Mash on khuff is a valid substitute; omitting it carries no blame, but wearing after washing is a condition.

This passage opens the chapter on wiping over khuffayn, establishing its basic validity for minor hadath and listing seven conditions. It focuses on the first condition: the khuff must be worn after washing the feet. The commentary also resolves an intra-Hanafi dispute over thick socks, guiding the fatwa toward permissibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its general ruling
Note that the text begins with 'صح المسح' (valid), indicating permissibility. This is not wajib, as omitting it causes no blame.
Contrast with tayammum, which becomes obligatory when water is absent.
2
Determine the scope: minor hadath only
The ruling applies exclusively to minor hadath; janabah is excluded because the textual evidence restricts mash to minor impurity.
The commentary clarifies that even a junub wearing khuff cannot wipe; he must wash the body while keeping the khuff on.
3
Extract the first condition
Wearing the khuff must occur after washing both feet, even if before completing wudu, provided wudu is completed before any nullifier.
If he wears them before washing feet, or nullifies before completing wudu, the condition fails.
4
Analyze the dispute on thick socks
The passage defines thick socks (thakhīn) that stay on without tying. Abu Hanifa initially disallowed wiping; his students allowed it. His retraction shifts the mufta bihi to permissibility.
Three categories: thin unsoled (invalid by consensus), thick soled (valid by consensus), thick unsoled (disputed, fatwa on permissibility).
5
Apply condition to special cases
If a person has a splint (jabirah) on one foot, wiping the splint counts as washing, so wearing a khuff on that foot invalidates mash. Similarly, a mutayammim must remove khuff upon finding water.
These exceptions reinforce that the condition of 'washing feet' is literal or legal.

Source Text

باب المسح على الخفين
صح المسح على الخفين في الحدث الأصغر للرجال والنساء، ولو كانا من شيء ثخين غير الجلد سواء كان لهما نعل من جلد أو لا.
[شروط جوازه]
ويشترط الجواز المسح على الخفين سبعة شرائط : الأول: لبسهما بعد غسل الرجلين ولو قبل كمال الوضوء، إذا أتمه قبل حصول ناقض للوضوء.
وصلية: قال العيني: ونبه بقوله: "صح" على أنه إذا ترك المسح فلا بأس عليه، بخلاف التيمم؛ فإنه فرض عند الماء. [الشلبي على تبيين الحقائق (۱۳۷۱] الأصغر: قيد به فخرجت به الجنابة ونحوها، فإنه لا فيها المسح؛ لورود النص بذلك، وصوّر حافظ الدين في "الكافي" صورة مسح الجنب تقريباً للمتعلم: بأن توضاً ولبس جوربين مجلدين ثم أجنب، ليس له أن يشدهما ويغسل سائر جسده مضطجعاً أو مادا رجليه على شيء مرتفع ويمسح عليه [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٢٨] من شيء ثخين إلخ : أي يجوز المسح على الجورب إذا كان منعلاً أو مجلداً أو ثخيناً، والمجلد: هو الذي وضع الجلد على أعلاه، وأسفله والمنعل هو الذي وضع الجلد على أسفله كالنعل للقدم، وقيل: يكون إلى الكعب، وأما الثخين فالمذكور وحده: أن يستمسك على الساق من غير ربط وأن لا يرى ما تحته وقال أبو حنيفة : لا يجوز المسح عليه، ويروى رجوع أبي حنيفة إلى قولهما قبل موته بثلاثة أيام وقيل بسبعة أيام وعليه الفتوى. [تبيين الحقائق: ١٥١/١] واعلم أن المسألة على ثلاثة وجوه إن كانا رقيقين غير منعلين لا يجوز المسح عليهما اتفاقاً، وإن كانا ثخينين منعلين اتفاقاً، وإن كانا ثخينين غير منعلين فهو محل الاختلاف [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۱۲۸] غسل الرجلين أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان الغسل حكما كجبيرة بالرجلين أو بإحداهما مسحهما ولبس الخف، الجبيرة كالغسل [مراقي الفلاح (۱۲۹]. فلو مسح جبيرة إحدى رجليه، ولبس الخف في إحدى رجليه، لا يجوز المسح عليه؛ لأنه يصير جامعاً بين الغسل والمسح. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٢٩] ولو أي ولو كان اللبس قبل كمال الوضوء. [مراقي الفلاح: (۱۲۹] ولو لبسهما بعد الغسل جاز المسح؛ لأنه وضوء وزيادة، إلا إذا كان متيمماً فلابد من نزعهما إذا وجد الماء. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۱۲۹] قبل كمال إلخ: فلو غسل رجليه ولبس خفيه وأحدث قبل تمام الوضوء، لابد من نزعهما. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٢٩]
Chapter of Wiping over Khuffayn. Wiping over khuffayn is valid for minor hadath for men and women, even if they are made of thick material other than leather, whether or not they have a sole made of leather. [Conditions for its validity] For the validity of wiping over khuffayn, seven conditions are required: First: wearing them after washing the feet, even if before completing wudu, provided he completes it before a nullifier of wudu occurs. And commentary: al-Ayni said: He indicated by his saying 'valid' that if he omits wiping there is no blame on him, unlike tayammum, for it is obligatory when water is present. [Minor hadath: restricted thus, so janabah and the like are excluded, for wiping is not permitted in them due to the text. Hafiz al-Din in al-Kafi depicted the case of a junub's wiping for the learner: that he performs wudu and wears two thick socks, then becomes junub; he may not remove them but washes the rest of his body lying on his side or extending his legs on something raised and wipes over them.] From 'something thick' etc.: i.e., wiping over a sock is permissible if it is soled or faced with leather or thick. The faced one is that on which leather is placed on its upper part, and the soled one is that on which leather is placed on its lower part like a sole for the foot; it is said it reaches up to the ankle. As for the thick one, what is mentioned alone: that it stays on the shin without tying and that what is underneath it is not visible. Abu Hanifa said: Wiping over it is not permissible, and it is narrated that Abu Hanifa retracted to their view three days before his death, and it is said seven days, and upon that is the fatwa. Know that the matter has three aspects: if they are thin and unsoled, wiping over them is impermissible by agreement; if they are thick and soled, permissible by agreement; if they are thick and unsoled, that is the point of disagreement. 'Washing the feet' is general, so it includes when the washing is legal, like a splint on the feet or one of them, wiping over them and wearing the khuff; a splint is like washing. If he wipes over a splint on one foot and wears the khuff on the other foot, wiping over it is not permissible because he combines washing and wiping. 'Even if' means even if the wearing is before completing wudu. If he wears them after washing, wiping is permissible because it is wudu and extra, except if he is a mutayammim, then he must remove them when he finds water. 'Before completing' etc.: so if he washed his feet and wore his khuff and then nullified wudu before completing wudu, he must remove them.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an intra-Hanafi dispute. It begins by stating the basic ruling that wiping over khuff (leather socks) is valid for minor hadath (the state of impurity that requires wudu) for both men and women. The khuff need not be made of leather; it can be of any thick material, with or without a leather sole. The word 'thick' (thakhīn) is defined later. The passage then lists the first condition for valid mash: the khuff must be worn after washing the feet. Washing can be before completing wudu, but the wudu must be completed before any nullifier occurs. The commentary clarifies that if one omits wiping altogether, there is no sin, unlike tayammum which becomes obligatory when water is absent. It also restricts 'hadath' to minor hadath, excluding major impurity (janabah) because the textual evidence only permits mash for minor hadath. A hypothetical scenario for a junub is described to illustrate that even if one becomes junub, mash is not allowed—rather one must wash the body while keeping the khuff on. The passage then delves into a detailed discussion on thick socks (jūrab thakhīn). It defines three types: soled (mun‘al) with leather on the bottom, faced (mujallad) with leather on top, and thick (thakhīn) which stays on the shin without tying and hides the skin. According to Abu Hanifa, wiping over thick socks is not permissible, but he is reported to have retracted before his death, and the fatwa is on the permissibility. The dispute is summarized into three scenarios: thin and unsoled socks are unanimously invalid; thick and soled are unanimously valid; thick but unsoled are disputed. Finally, the passage discusses the application of the first condition to cases where one has a splint (jabirah) on the foot: wiping over a splint is like washing, so if one wipes over a splint and then wears a khuff, valid mash is not allowed because it combines washing and wiping. The condition also applies to a mutayammim, who must remove the khuff upon finding water.

Key Terms
الخف (al-khuff): A leather sock worn over the foot, covering the ankles, made of leather or thick material
الحدث الأصغر (al-hadath al-asghar): Minor impurity requiring wudu, such as passing wind, urine, stool, sleep
ثخين (thakhīn): Thick enough to stay on the shin without tying and so that the skin underneath is not visible

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Not permissible under any condition
B) Permissible because Abu Hanifa retracted to the view of his students
C) Permissible only if it is made of leather
D) Not permissible unless it has a leather sole

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuff is a valid concession for minor hadath, requiring the khuff to be worn after washing feet; for thick socks, the mufta bihi is permissibility.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
The Six Remaining Conditions for Wiping over Khuffayn (Conditions 2-7)
Listing and explaining conditions 2-7 for valid mash over khuffayn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six conditions (2-7) for valid mash over khuffayn and apply each condition to determine whether a particular khuff permits mash.

Core Idea
A valid khuff must be thick, waterproof, ankle-covering, walkable, hole-free, self-standing, and worn on a sufficiently intact foot.

The permissibility of wiping over khuffayn (leather socks) is a concession (rukhsah) in wudu, but not every foot covering qualifies. In this passage, the author lists six additional conditions—beyond the first condition of wearing them after washing the feet—that a khuff must satisfy. Understanding these conditions helps you avoid common mistakes, such as assuming any sock or boot can be wiped over.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the first condition from the rest
Realize that condition 1 (wearing after washing) is temporal; conditions 2-7 are physical characteristics of the khuff and the foot. All are shurut (validity conditions), not arkan.
Shurut must be present at the time of mash; if any is missing, mash is invalid.
2
Analyze condition 2: covering the ankles
Note that the khuff must cover the sides of the ankles; the top may be open. The commentary explains that seeing the ankles from above does not harm.
The Arabic text mentions 'ستر الجوانب' (covering the sides).
3
Analyze condition 4: hole size and measurement
Understand the two scenarios: if the hole exposes a non-finger area, measure by the smallest toe; if it exposes the toes themselves, measure by the actual toes exposed, not the smallest.
The example: if the big toe and its neighbor are exposed and together equal three smallest fingers, it is valid; otherwise invalid.
4
Analyze condition 7: sufficient foot length
If the front part of the foot is amputated, at least three finger-widths (of the hand) must remain below the ankle for mash to be valid. Otherwise, the remaining part must be washed, and wiping cannot be combined with washing.
This condition ensures that the area that would be wiped is large enough to merit the concession.
5
Synthesize a full test
Given a hypothetical khuff, check each condition in order. If all are satisfied, mash is permissible; if any is missing, the feet must be washed normally.
Practice with the practice tasks below.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثاني : سترهما للكعبين والثالث: إمكان متابعة المشي فيهما، فلا يجوز على خف من زجاج أو خشب أو حديد والرابع خلو كل منهما عن خرق قدر ثلاث أصابع من أصغر أصابع القدم، والخامس: استمساكهما على الرجلين من غير شَدّ، والسادس: منعهما وصول الماء إلى الجسد والسابع أن يبقى من مقدم القدم قدر ثلاث أصابع من أصغر أصابع اليد، فلو كان فاقدا مقدم قدمه لا يمسح على خفه، ولو كان عقب القدم موجوداً. [ومعنى ستر الرجلين] أطلقه وهو مقيد بستر الجوانب؛ فإنه لا يضر نظر الكعبين من أعلى خف قصير الساق. [مراقي الفلاح: ۱۳۰] من زجاج أي مصنوع من زجاج إلخ، وما رأينا خفا مصنوعاً من زجاج أو خشب أو حديد، ولعلهم كانوا يصنعون شيئا كالخف من هذه الأشياء ونحوها، أو المسألة على سبيل الفرض. من أصغر إلخ إنما يعتبر الأصغر إذا انكشف موضع غير موضع الأصابع، وأما إذا انكشف الأصابع نفسها يعتبر أن ينكشف الثلاث أيتها كانت ولا يعتبر الأصغر؛ لأن كل إصبع أصل بنفسها، فلا يعتبر بغيرها، حتى لو انكشفت الإبهام مع جارتها، وهما قدر ثلث أصابع من أصغرها، يجوز المسح، فإن كان جاريتها لا يجوز المسح. [تبيين الحقائق: ١٤٦/١] أن يبقى إلخ فإذا قطعت رجل فوق الكعب جاز مسح خف الباقية، وإن بقي من دون الكعب أقل من ثلاث أصابع لا يمسح؛ لافتراض غسل الباقي، وهو لا يجمع مع مسح خف الصحيحة. [مراقي الفلاح: ١٣١]
And the second: their covering of the two ankles. And the third: the possibility of continuous walking in them, so it is not permissible to wipe over a khuff made of glass, wood, or iron. And the fourth: the absence in each of them of a hole measuring three fingers from the smallest toes of the foot. And the fifth: their staying on the feet without tying. And the sixth: their preventing water from reaching the body. And the seventh: that remains from the front part of the foot an amount of three fingers from the smallest fingers of the hand. So if one lacks the front part of his foot, he should not wipe over his khuff, even if the heel of the foot is present. [And the meaning of covering the feet] It was mentioned absolutely, but it is restricted to covering the sides; for looking at the ankles from above a khuff with a short leg does not harm. 'Of glass' i.e., made of glass etc. We have not seen a khuff made of glass, wood, or iron; perhaps they used to make something like a khuff from these things and the like, or the issue is hypothetical. 'From the smallest' etc.: The smallest is considered only if a place other than the place of the fingers is exposed. But if the fingers themselves are exposed, it is considered that three fingers are exposed whichever they are, and the smallest is not considered; because each finger is an original by itself, so it is not considered by others. So if the thumb and its neighbor are exposed, and they amount to three fingers of the smallest, wiping is permissible; if it is its neighbor, wiping is not permissible. 'That remains' etc.: If a foot is cut above the ankle, wiping over the khuff of the remaining part is permissible. But if less than three fingers remain below the ankle, he should not wipe, because washing the remaining part is obligatory, and it cannot be combined with wiping over the khuff of the healthy foot.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage lists conditions two through seven for the validity of wiping over khuffayn. Condition two: the khuff must cover the ankles (al-ka'bayn). The commentary clarifies that this means the sides must be covered; it is not harmful if the ankles are visible from above if the khuff has a short leg. Condition three: it must be possible to walk continuously in them. Thus, a khuff made of glass, wood, or iron is not valid because it would not allow normal walking. Condition four: the khuff must be free of a hole measuring three fingers (of the smallest toes). If the hole exposes the fingers themselves, the measurement is taken from whatever fingers are exposed, not necessarily the smallest, because each finger is considered independently. For example, if the big toe and its neighbor are exposed and together equal three of the smallest fingers, wiping is valid; otherwise not. Condition five: the khuff must stay on the feet without needing to be tied. Condition six: it must prevent water from reaching the skin (i.e., it must be waterproof). Condition seven: the wearer must have a remaining front part of the foot measuring three small fingers (of the hand). If the foot is amputated above the ankle, wiping over the khuff of the remaining part is permissible. But if less than three fingers remain below the ankle, wiping is not allowed because the remaining part must be washed (it is not covered by the khuff), and that would combine washing and wiping, which is impermissible.

Key Terms
الكعبين (al-ka'bayn): The ankles, the two protruding bones on either side of the foot at the junction with the leg
خرق (kharq): A hole or tear in the khuff

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a khuff has a hole that exposes only the wearer's big toe and the second toe, and together they measure the width of three of the smallest toes, is wiping valid?
A) Valid, because the hole does not expose the smallest toe
B) Invalid, because when fingers are exposed, three actual fingers must be exposed, not three smallest
C) Valid, because the condition only cares about the smallest toe
D) Invalid, because any hole invalidates

Key Takeaway
Six conditions define a mash-permissible khuff: ankle coverage, walkability, hole-free (<3 fingers), self-staying, waterproof, and sufficient foot length.

Duration of Wiping: One Day for Resident, Three for Traveler
Establishes time limits for mash and starts of counting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time limits for wiping over khuff for a resident and traveler, and identify the correct starting point of the period according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The wiping period begins at the first hadath after wearing, not at the time of wearing or first wipe.

This lesson establishes the time limits for wiping over khuff. The Hanafi school specifies one day and night for a resident and three days and nights for a traveler. A critical point is when the counting starts: the correct view (الصحيح) is from the first hadath after donning the khuff, not from the time of wearing or the first wipe. This has practical implications for the duration available and is a point of valid scholarly disagreement.

Guided Path
1
State the durations
Identify the ruling: resident wipes 1 day/night, traveler wipes 3 days/nights. Note that these are maximum periods.
2
Identify the starting point
The text explicitly says 'ابتداء المدة من وقت الحدث بعد لبس الخفين' (the beginning of the period is from the time of hadath after wearing). This is the relied-upon Hanafi view.
3
Compare with alternative views
Other imams differ: al-Awza'i held it begins at wearing; Imam Ahmad held it begins at the first wipe. Understand their reasoning and the Hanafi response.
4
Apply to a scenario
Work through an example: a resident wears khuff at dawn, nullifies at noon. The period begins at noon and ends 24 hours later. Compare with Awza'i's view to see the practical difference.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is key to understanding why the starting point matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويمسح المقيم يوماً وليلةً والمسافر ثلاثة أيام بلياليها، وابتداء المدة من وقت الحدث بعد لبس الخفين. [ومعنى ستر الرجلين] أطلقه وهو مقيد بستر الجوانب؛ فإنه لا يضر نظر الكعبين من أعلى خف قصير الساق. [مراقي الفلاح: ۱۳۰] من زجاج أي مصنوع من زجاج إلخ، وما رأينا خفا مصنوعاً من زجاج أو خشب أو حديد، ولعلهم كانوا يصنعون شيئا كالخف من هذه الأشياء ونحوها، أو المسألة على سبيل الفرض. من أصغر إلخ إنما يعتبر الأصغر إذا انكشف موضع غير موضع الأصابع، وأما إذا انكشف الأصابع نفسها يعتبر أن ينكشف الثلاث أيتها كانت ولا يعتبر الأصغر؛ لأن كل إصبع أصل بنفسها، فلا يعتبر بغيرها، حتى لو انكشفت الإبهام مع جارتها، وهما قدر ثلث أصابع من أصغرها، يجوز المسح، فإن كان جاريتها لا يجوز المسح. [تبيين الحقائق: ١٤٦/١] أن يبقى إلخ فإذا قطعت رجل فوق الكعب جاز مسح خف الباقية، وإن بقي من دون الكعب أقل من ثلاث أصابع لا يمسح؛ لافتراض غسل الباقي، وهو لا يجمع مع مسح خف الصحيحة. [مراقي الفلاح: ١٣١] وليلة أطلقها فشملت مستقبلة أو ماضية، فلو لبس الخفين يوم السبت بعد ما طلع الشمس، جاز له أن يمسح إلى طلوع الشمس من يوم الأحد مع أن الليلة المتوسطة بين يوم السبت والأحد ليوم الأحد لا ليوم السبت؛ فإن الليل مقدم على النهار شرعا، فظهر مما قلنا: إن الإضافة في قوله : "بلياليها" لأدنى الملابسة. من وقت الحدث إلخ: هذا هو الصحيح، وقيل: من وقت اللبس وبه قال الأوزاعي، وقيل: من وقت المسح، وبه قال أحمد، فلو لبس الخفين لصلاة الفجر ، ثم أحدث قبل الزوال ومسح على الخفين وقت التوضؤ لصلاة الظهر بعد الزوال، فعند الأوزاعي: تمام مدة يوم وليلة طلوع الفجر من الغد، وعندنا قبل الزوال، وعند أحمد: بعد الزوال، ومن ألطف مسائل المسح ما في شرح الزاهدي" للقدوري قلت والمقيم في مدة مسحه قد لا يتمكن المسح إلا من أربع صلوات وقتية بالمسح كمن توضأ ولبس خفيه قبل الفجر، فلما طلع صلى الفجر وقعد قدر التشهد فأحدث، =
And the resident wipes for one day and one night, and the traveler for three days with their nights. And the beginning of the period is from the time of the hadath after wearing the khuffayn. [And the meaning of covering the feet] It was mentioned absolutely, but it is restricted to covering the sides; for looking at the ankles from above a khuff with a short leg does not harm. 'Of glass' i.e., made of glass etc... [duplicate text omitted] ... And 'night' is used absolutely, so it includes the coming night or the past night. So if one wears the khuff on Saturday after sunrise, he may wipe until sunrise on Sunday, even though the night intervening between Saturday and Sunday belongs to Sunday not Saturday; for the night precedes the day legally. So it is clear that the addition 'with their nights' indicates the slightest connection. 'From the time of the hadath' etc.: This is the correct view. It is said: from the time of wearing, and al-Awza'i held that. It is said: from the time of wiping, and Ahmad held that. So if one wears the khuff for dawn prayer, then nullifies before noon, and wipes over the khuff when performing wudu for noon prayer after noon, according to al-Awza'i: the end of the one day and night period is at dawn of the next day; according to us, before noon; according to Ahmad, after noon. And among the subtlest issues of wiping is what is in Sharh al-Zahidi al-Quduri: I said: The resident during his wiping period may not be able to wipe except for four obligatory prayers with wiping, such as one who performs wudu and wears his khuff before dawn, then at dawn prays Fajr and sits for the amount of tashahhud and nullifies, ...
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage establishes the time limits for wiping over khuff. A resident (muqim) may wipe for one day and one night (24 hours), and a traveler (musafir) for three days and three nights (72 hours). The counting begins from the time the hadath occurs after wearing the khuff, not from the time of wearing. The commentary clarifies that 'night' includes the coming or past night; for example, if one wears the khuff after sunrise on Saturday, the 24-hour period extends to sunrise on Sunday. The night between Saturday and Sunday is attributed to Sunday because in Islamic law, night precedes day. The correct starting point is the time of hadath (first occurrence of minor impurity after wearing). Alternative views are mentioned: al-Awza'i said from the time of wearing, and Imam Ahmad from the time of the first wipe. The practical difference is illustrated with an example: someone wears khuff before Fajr, nullifies before noon, and then wipes for Dhuhr. According to the Hanafi position, the period ends before noon (since the hadath occurred before noon), so the Dhuhr wipe is valid if within 24 hours from that hadath. The passage ends with an incomplete sentence about a subtler case where a resident can only manage four obligatory prayers within his period.

Key Terms
المقيم (al-muqim): A resident, one not traveling; for mash, the period is one day and night.
المسافر (al-musafir): A traveler, one on a journey at least 48 miles, and not intending to stay 15 days.
ابتداء المدة (ibtida' al-muddah): The beginning of the time period for mash, which is from the first hadath after wearing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Until Fajr the next day
B) Until 10 AM the next day
C) Until Maghrib the same day
D) Until 10 AM the same day

Key Takeaway
The wiping period begins at the first hadath after wearing; one day/night for resident, three days/nights for traveler.
