Conditions for Wiping over Khuffayn
Listing conditions for masah validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the six conditions for valid masah over khuffayn as given in Nur al-Idah and apply them to determine if a particular khuff is acceptable.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuff is valid only if the khuff covers the ankles, is wearable, tear-free, stays on without ties, is waterproof, and covers the full foot including the front.

In the Hanafi school, wiping over leather socks (khuffayn) is a concession that replaces washing the feet in wudu, but it is only valid under strict conditions. This passage from Nur al-Idah lists six specific conditions (the second through seventh) that the khuff must meet. Understanding these conditions is essential for correctly performing this alternative form of purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wiping (masah) over khuffayn (leather socks) during wudu. In the Hanafi school, this is a permissible substitute for washing the feet (rukhsah), but it has conditions for validity.
The ruling is that masah is jaiz (permissible) but only if all conditions are met.
2
Classify the passage type
This passage is a ruling statement listing conditions (shurut) that must be present for the act to be valid. It is not providing evidence; it is a memorization anchor for the rules.
Conditions are external prerequisites, not pillars (arkan).
3
List each condition with its rationale
Go through conditions 2-7 one by one: (2) covers ankles, (3) can be walked in normally, (4) no tear larger than three small toes, (5) stays on without tying, (6) waterproof, (7) front part of foot present. Understand the reason behind each.
The first condition (material being leather or similar) is not mentioned here but is found elsewhere.
4
Note the exceptions and edge cases
Condition 7 includes an exception: if the front part of the foot is missing, wiping is invalid even if the heel remains. This shows the school's thoroughness.
The condition is about the foot itself, not the khuff.
5
Apply the conditions to a hypothetical khuff
Test a scenario: e.g., a leather sock that covers the ankle, has a small tear (less than three toes), fits snugly without ties, is waterproof, and the wearer has a complete foot. Conclude that wiping is valid.
All conditions must be fulfilled simultaneously.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة
المسح على الخفين
والثاني : سترهما للكعبين والثالث: إمكان متابعة المشي فيهما، فلا يجوز على خف من زجاج أو خشب أو حديد والرابع خلو كل منهما عن خرق قدر ثلاث أصابع من أصغر أصابع القدم، والخامس: استمساكهما على الرجلين من غير شَدّ، والسادس: منعهما وصول الماء إلى الجسد والسابع أن يبقى من مقدم القدم قدر ثلاث أصابع من أصغر أصابع اليد، فلو كان فاقدا مقدم قدمه لا يمسح على خفه، ولو كان عقب القدم موجوداً،
The Book of Purification. Wiping over the khuffayn. The second: covering the two ankles. The third: ability to walk in them continuously, so it is not permissible to wipe over a khuff made of glass, wood, or iron. The fourth: each of them is free from a tear measuring three of the smallest toes of the foot. The fifth: they stay on the legs without tying. The sixth: they prevent water from reaching the body. The seventh: there remains from the front part of the foot [a portion] measuring three of the smallest fingers of the hand. So if one has lost the front part of his foot, he does not wipe over his khuff, even if the heel is present.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a statement of the conditions for the validity of wiping over leather socks (khuffayn) in the Hanafi school. The text lists six conditions, starting from the second (the first condition, likely that the khuff is permissible to wear, was on an earlier page). The second condition requires the khuff to cover the ankles. The third requires that it is possible to walk in them normally, so socks made of rigid materials like glass, wood, or iron are invalid. The fourth condition: there must be no hole in either khuff larger than three of the smallest toes of the foot. The fifth: the khuff must stay on the foot without tying (i.e., it is snug enough not to fall off). The sixth: it must be impermeable to water, because if water can reach the foot, the purpose of wiping is defeated. The seventh: the front part of the foot (the toes and part of the sole) must be present; if the front is amputated, wiping is invalid even if the heel remains. These conditions are all from the Hanafi school and must be met for the masah to be valid.

Key Terms
خف (khuff): A leather sock or boot worn over the foot, used for wiping (masah) in ablution instead of washing the feet.
مسح (masah): Wiping the surface of the khuff with wet hand instead of washing the feet in wudu.
كعب (ka'b): The ankle bone, which the khuff must cover.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi conditions in this passage, which of the following would INVALIDATE wiping over khuff?
A) The khuff covers the ankles.
B) The khuff has a tear of two toes in size.
C) The khuff is made of thin cotton fabric.
D) The khuff stays on without tying.

Key Takeaway
For valid masah over khuffayn, all six conditions (cover ankles, walkable, no large tear, stays without tie, waterproof, foot intact) must be satisfied.

Duration of Wiping and Start of the Period
Explaining the duration of wiping for resident and traveler, and when the period begins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the duration of wiping for resident and traveler and identify when the period begins according to the Hanafi school, and distinguish it from the positions of al-Awza'i and Ahmad.

Core Idea
The wiping period starts from the first hadath after wearing, not from the time of wearing or wiping.

In this lesson, we examine the timeframe within which wiping over khuffayn is valid. The Hanafi school specifies different durations for residents and travelers, and, crucially, the clock does not start ticking from the moment you put on the khuff. Instead, it begins only when you first break your wudu after wearing them. This seemingly small detail has significant practical consequences and is a point of disagreement with other scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is wiping over khuffayn (mash 'ala al-khuffayn). The ruling specifies how long this wiping can be performed without rewashing the feet: one day and one night for a resident, three days and nights for a traveler.
2
Note the beginning of the period
According to the Hanafi school, the start of the period is from the time of the first hadath (ritual impurity) after putting on the khuff — not from the time of wearing or from the first wipe.
For example, if you wear khuff at Fajr and then your wudu breaks before Dhuhr, the period starts at that moment, not at Fajr.
3
Recognize the disagreement
Other scholars disagree on the starting point. Al-Awza'i held it begins from the moment of wearing; Ahmad ibn Hanbal held it begins from the time of the first wipe. The Hanafi view is considered the correct one (mufta bihi) in our school.
The passage states: 'هذا هو الصحيح' (this is the correct view).
4
Apply the practical difference
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: if a person wears khuff at Fajr, has hadath before Dhuhr, and then wipes at Dhuhr, the period ends before Dhuhr the next day (Hanafi), at Fajr (al-Awza'i), or after Dhuhr (Ahmad).
The timing affects when the feet must be washed again.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

٤٩
نواقض المسح
لا يمكنه أن يصلي من الغد على هيئة الأولى؛ لاعتراض ظهور الحدث في آخر صلاته، هكذا أورده مطلقاً، وقد يصلي خمساً، وقد يصلي بالمسح ستّاً كمن أخر الظهر إلى آخر الوقت ثم أحدث وتوضأ ومسح، وصلى الظهر في آخر وقته ثم صلى الظهر من ا الغد في أوله. وإلا إلخ أي وإن لم يقم المسافر بعد ما مسح يوماً وليلة، بل أقام وقد مسح دون يوم وليلة، يتم يوماً وليلة.
The resident wipes for one day and one night, and the traveler for three days with their nights. The beginning of the period is from the time of the hadath (nullifying event) after putting on the khuff. ... [commentary on various issues] ... And otherwise etc. meaning if the traveler did not stay after wiping for one day and night, but rather stayed after wiping less than one day and night, he completes one day and night.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling and a detailed commentary on the duration of wiping over khuffayn. The ruling: a resident can wipe for one day and one night, a traveler for three days and nights. The period starts from the first hadath (ritual impurity) after wearing the khuff. The commentary clarifies various points: the khuff must cover the sides as well; the measurement for holes uses the smallest toe; if the entire foot above the ankle is amputated, wiping on the remaining part is valid; the night included can be either the coming or previous night; and there is a dispute with al-Awza'i and Ahmad regarding the start of the period. The correct Hanafi view is that the period begins from the time of hadath, not from the time of wearing or wiping. The passage also includes a subtle ruling about how many prayers a resident can perform with the wipe, sometimes four, five, or six.

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): A nullifier of wudu (e.g., passing wind, urine, etc.).
مدة المسح (muddat al-masah): The time limit during which wiping is valid without needing to rewash the feet.
مقيم (muqim): A person who is not traveling (i.e., resident).
مسافر (musafir): A traveler, typically one who intends a journey of three days or more (according to Hanafi).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does the period of wiping over khuffayn begin?
A) From the moment the khuff is put on.
B) From the first hadath after putting on the khuff.
C) From the moment of the first wipe.
D) From the beginning of the travel.

Key Takeaway
The period of wiping over khuff starts from the first hadath after wearing, and lasts for one day and night for a resident, three days and nights for a traveler.

The Obligatory Amount and Sunnah of Wiping
Defining the fard amount of wiping and its sunnah method.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligatory minimum area for wiping the khuff in the Hanafi school and describe the sunnah method.

Core Idea
The fard of wiping is the area of three small fingers on the front top of each foot; anything less is insufficient.

Wiping over khuffayn is a concession that lightens the obligation of washing feet in wudu. However, this concession has a minimum requirement: a specific area must be wiped. This lesson clarifies that obligatory amount and the recommended method based on the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Wiping over khuffayn is allowed in place of washing feet. The wiping itself is a rukn, but there is a minimal area that must be wiped. The text gives the fard amount.
Fard here means obligatory, the minimum requirement for the wipe to be valid.
2
State the prescribed measure
The measure is three of the smallest fingers of the hand. This is based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as transmitted in the Hanafi school.
The smallest fingers refer to three fingers placed side by side, typically the three middle fingers are used for measurement.
3
Define the area to be wiped
The area is on the visible part (zaahir) of the front (muqaddam) of each foot, i.e., the top part from the toes to where the shoe covers.
The sides, heel, and sole are not included.
4
Describe the sunnah method
The sunnah is to spread the fingers apart and begin from the tips of the toes, wiping upward to the shin. This ensures full coverage and follows the Prophet's practice.
The sunnah is not obligatory but recommended.

Source Text

وفرض المسح قدر ثلاث أصابع من أصغر أصابع اليد على ظاهر مقدم كل رجل، وسننه: مد الأصابع مفرجة من رؤوس أصابع القدم إلى الساق.
[ نواقض المسح] وينقض مسح الخف أربعة أشياء: كل شيء ينقض الوضوء، ونزع خف ولو بخروج أكثر القدم إلى ساق الخف، وإصابة الماء أكثر إحدى القدمين في الخف
And the obligatory amount of wiping is the measure of three of the smallest fingers of the hand on the visible part of the front of each foot. Its sunnah is to spread the fingers apart from the tips of the toes up to the shin. [Nullifiers of wiping] Four things nullify the wiping of the khuff: everything that nullifies wudu, removing the khuff even if only most of the foot comes out to the shin, and water reaching most of one of the feet while in the khuff.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage first defines the obligatory amount (fard) of wiping: three of the smallest fingers of the hand, wiped over the visible upper surface of the front part of each foot. This is the minimum required; wiping less than that is insufficient. The sunnah method is to spread the fingers apart and wipe from the toes upwards to the shin. Then it lists the four nullifiers of the wipe: (1) anything that nullifies wudu (e.g., passing wind, urine), (2) removing the khuff (even partially, if most of the foot comes out), (3) water reaching most of one foot while the khuff is on (e.g., stepping in a puddle), and (4) the fourth nullifier is not mentioned here but typically it is the expiration of the time period for the excused person. The commentary in the original text notes that the fourth nullifier (large hole and expiry of time) are encompassed by the first three, so they are not listed separately.

Key Terms
فرض المسح (fard al-masah): The obligatory minimum area to be wiped on the khuff.
نقض المسح (naqd al-masah): Anything that invalidates the state of wiping, requiring removal of the khuff and washing the feet.
نزع الخف (naz' al-khuff): Removing the khuff (even partly) which nullifies the wipe.

The obligatory minimum for wiping on khuff is the area of three small fingers on the top front of each foot; wiping less invalidates the wipe.

The Four Nullifiers of Wiping (Nawāqid al-Masah)
Listing the nullifiers of wiping on the khuff.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four nullifiers of wiping over khuffayn in the Hanafi school and explain why each nullifies.

Core Idea
The state of wiping is nullified by anything that breaks wudu, removing the khuff, or water entering the khuff; these render the feet needing washing.

Wiping over khuffayn is a temporary concession that can be lost easily. This lesson covers the factors that nullify the state of wiping, requiring you to remove the khuff and wash your feet. Understanding these nullifiers ensures your wudu remains valid.

Guided Path
1
List the nullifiers as given in the text
The passage lists three explicit nullifiers and implies a fourth. First, anything that nullifies wudu. Second, removing the khuff (even partially if most of the foot comes out). Third, water reaching most of one foot while in the khuff.
The fourth nullifier (expiry of the time period for the excused person or holes) is not explicitly listed but is covered under these three.
2
Explain the first nullifier: any wudu-breaker
Since wiping is a substitute for washing the feet, any event that breaks wudu (like passing wind, urine, etc.) also nullifies the wipe (naqd al-masah). This is because the wipe is part of wudu.
Once wudu is broken, the wipe becomes invalid. The person must remove the khuff and wash the feet upon new wudu.
3
Explain the second nullifier: removing the khuff
Taking off the khuff, even if only partially, nullifies the wipe. The Hanafi criterion is: if most of the foot comes out (i.e., beyond the ankle or to the shin), the wipe is broken. If only the front part exits (like toes), it does not nullify.
Removing one khuff nullifies only that foot's wipe; the other foot's wipe remains valid unless the first foot is washed.
4
Explain the third nullifier: water reaching the foot
If water enters the khuff and reaches most of one foot (e.g., stepping in a puddle or immersing the foot), the wipe is nullified. This is because the original obligation (washing the foot) is effectively fulfilled by water touching the skin.
It is important not to deliberately soak your feet while wearing khuff, as it breaks the wipe.
5
Note the fourth nullifier implicitly included
The text says 'four things' but only lists three. The fourth is either the expiry of the time period for a traveler or resident (maskh mash) or a large hole in the khuff, as these are encompassed by the first three.
In practice, the time limit is also a nullifier for the excused person.

Source Text

Key Takeaway

Nullifiers of Wiping over Khuffs
Lists and explains the four nullifiers of wiping over leather socks.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four nullifiers of wiping over khuffs and apply them to determine whether the wiping remains valid in a given scenario.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs is nullified by four things: breaking wudu, removing the khuff, water inside, and time expiry.

This passage from Nur al-Idah lists the events that end the concession of wiping over leather socks. Understanding these nullifiers is crucial for maintaining purity correctly. The author concisely states four nullifiers, each with a clear basis in the purpose of wiping as a substitute for washing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four nullifiers
List the four items mentioned: (1) anything that nullifies wudu, (2) removing the khuff (even partially), (3) water reaching most of one foot inside the khuff, and (4) expiry of the period (one day/night for resident, three for traveler).
The first nullifier is general; the other three are specific to khuffs.
2
Understand the rationale for each
For each nullifier, consider why it invalidates wiping. Breaking wudu nullifies because wiping is part of wudu. Removal breaks the condition of covering. Water inside effectively washes the foot, ending the need for wiping. Expiry ends the temporary concession.
The Hanafi school considers these as logical consequences of the nature of wiping.
3
Apply the exception for fear of cold
The text says the period nullifier does not apply if one fears losing a foot or part of it from cold. This is a concession (rukhsah) allowing continued wiping beyond the normal period.
This exception is based on necessity and is limited to actual fear of harm.
4
Distinguish from other coverings
The passage ends by stating that wiping is not allowed on turban, cap, face veil, or gloves. These are not analogous to khuffs because they do not cover the required body part for wiping (feet) and are not worn for the same purpose.
This clarifies that the ruling is specific to footwear.
5
Synthesize the nullification consequences
After the last three specific nullifiers, one only needs to wash the feet, not repeat the whole wudu. However, if wudu is nullified, the entire wudu must be redone.
The nullifiers do not always require a full repetition of wudu; they only end the wiping concession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وينقض مسح الخف أربعة أشياء: كل شيء ينقض الوضوء، ونزع خف ولو بخروج أكثر القدم إلى ساق الخف، وإصابة الماء أكثر إحدى القدمين في الخف على الصحيح، ومضي المدة إن لم يخف ذهاب رجله كلها أو بعضها من البرد، وبعد الثلاثة الأخيرة غسل رجليه فقط، ولا يجوز المسح على عمامة، وقلنسوة، وبرقع، وقفازين.
And wiping over the khuff is nullified by four things: everything that nullifies wudu, removing the khuff even if by exiting most of the foot to the leg of the khuff, water reaching most of one foot inside the khuff according to the correct view, and the expiry of the period if one does not fear losing his entire foot or part of it due to cold. And after the three latter (nullifiers), he washes only his feet. And it is not permissible to wipe over a turban, a cap, a face veil, or gloves.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on nullifiers of wiping over khuffs. The author states four nullifiers. First, anything that nullifies wudu also nullifies the wiping because wiping is a substitute for washing the feet. Second, removing the khuff, even partially (most of the foot out), nullifies it because the condition of wiping is that the khuff remains on the foot. Third, water reaching most of one foot inside the khuff (e.g., wading in water) nullifies it, based on the correct view, because it necessitates washing the foot. Fourth, the expiry of the period (one day and night for a resident, three days and nights for a traveler) nullifies it unless one fears harm from cold, in which case he may continue. After the last three nullifiers, one only needs to wash the feet, not repeat the whole wudu. The passage also notes that wiping is not allowed on a turban, cap, face veil, or gloves because these are not like khuffs in covering the required area for wiping.

Key Terms
نزع خف (naz' khuff): Removing the leather sock, even partially, which nullifies the wiping.
إصابة الماء أكثر القدم (isabat al-ma' akthar al-qadam): Water reaching most of the foot inside the khuff, nullifying the wiping.
مضي المدة (madi al-muddah): Expiry of the period for wiping (one day/night for resident, three for traveler).

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Wiping over a turban

Key Takeaway
The four nullifiers of wiping over khuffs are: anything that nullifies wudu, removal of the khuff (even partially), water reaching most of the foot inside, and expiry of the prescribed period.

Wiping over a Splint: No Wudu Condition
Introduces the section on splints and lists differences from khuffs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping over a splint and identify the key difference from wiping over khuffs regarding the condition of being applied after wudu.

Core Idea
Wiping over a splint is permitted without it being tied after wudu, unlike khuffs.

This short passage from Nur al-Idah opens the discussion on a practical concession: when a wound or fracture prevents washing, the splint (jabira) may be wiped instead. The author immediately highlights a crucial difference from the well-known ruling on wiping over khuffs: the timing of application. Understanding this distinction is essential to correctly applying the rules of taharah in medical contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act in question is 'wiping over a splint' (al-mash 'ala al-jabira). Determine its legal status in the Hanafi school: it is wajib to wipe over the splint in place of washing the affected part when washing would cause harm.
Wiping here substitutes for washing, not a separate act.
2
Recognize the condition compared to khuffs
The text states that wiping over a splint differs from wiping over khuffs in several ways. The first difference is that the splint does not require being tied or applied after a state of wudu (la yushtarat shadduha 'ala wudu'). Understand that for khuffs, they must be put on after completing wudu.
This condition is exclusive to khuffs; splints are a necessity concession.
3
Understand the rationale
The lack of a wudu condition for splints stems from the fact that injuries occur at any time, often when one is not in wudu. Requiring wudu before applying the splint would impose hardship, contradicting the principle of removal of hardship (raf' al-haraj).
This is an application of the maxim 'al-mashaqqah tajlib al-taysir' (hardship brings ease).

Source Text

فصل في الجبيرة ونحوها إذا افتصد أو جرح أو كسر عضوه فشده بخرقة المتوضي : اعلم أن المسح على الجبيرة يخالف المسح على الخف من وجوه :أحدها: أن الجبيرة لا يشترط شدّها على وضوء =
Section on the splint and similar: When one has blood drawn, or is wounded, or has a bone broken, and bandages it with a cloth—the person performing wudu: Know that wiping over the splint differs from wiping over the khuff in several aspects: One of them: that the splint is not required to be tied after wudu.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage opens a new section on the legal ruling of wiping over a splint (jabira) and similar medical bandages. Unlike wiping over khuffs, the splint does not require that it be applied after a state of wudu; it can be applied even when one is not in wudu. The author lists differences between wiping over a splint and over khuffs, but only the first difference is given in this excerpt. The full treatment would cover that wiping over a splint is a concession for necessity, and its validity conditions differ.

Key Terms
الجبيرة (al-jabirah): A splint or bandage applied to a fracture or wound.
فتصد (iftasada): To have blood drawn (phlebotomy), causing a wound.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The splint must be tied only by a doctor.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows wiping over a splint without requiring it to be applied after wudu, unlike khuffs.

Wiping Over a Splint (Jabirah): Conditions and Nature
Explains the conditions and nature of wiping over a splint.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions that make wiping over a splint wajib and explain why it is a rukhsat tafreeh with no time limit and no requirement of prior purity.

Core Idea
Wiping over a splint is a water-based concession, not a soil-based one, hence no niyyah and no time limit.

When a limb is injured, cupped, or broken, and washing the area is harmful, the Hanafi school permits wiping over the splint or bandage. This lesson unpacks the conditions for this obligation, the nature of the ruling as a concession of relief (rukhsat tafreeh), and its key differences from wiping over khuff.

Guided Path
1
Identify when wiping over a splint becomes wajib
The passage states that if one has a wound, cupping, or fracture and cannot wash the area nor wipe directly, it becomes wajib to wipe over the majority of the bandage.
The inability to wash may be due to harm from water, even hot water (as per the preferred view).
2
Understand the concept of rukhsat tafreeh
The text explains that wiping over a splint is a rukhsat tafreeh – a concession of relief where the original obligation (washing) remains permissible in theory. This means the allowance is genuine, not a replacement that abrogates the original.
Contrast with masah over khuff, which is a rukhsat isqat (abrogating the original requirement of washing feet).
3
Note that wiping over a splint is not time-bound
Unlike khuff (24 hours for resident, 3 days for traveler), wiping over a splint has no fixed duration. It remains valid as long as the splint is needed and the condition of harm persists.
The text says 'فلا يتوقت بمدة' (it is not delimited by time).
4
Recognize that no prior state of purity is required
One may apply the splint even when in a state of impurity (janabah or minor hadath). The wiping is valid regardless.
This is another difference from khuff, which requires the feet to be purified before wearing.
5
Distinguish from wiping over khuff in these aspects
The passage highlights that these differences (no time limit, no prior purity, falling off without healing does not invalidate) set jabirah apart from khuff.
These leniencies are due to the necessity of the splint and the nature of the injury.

Source Text

المسح، وإن ضره المسح ،تركه، ولا يفتقر إلى النية في مسح الخف والجبيرة والرأس.
جبيرة
بخلاف الخف، وإليه أشار الشيخ بقوله: "ولا يشترط إلخ " ، ثانيها : أن المسح على الجبيرة غير موقت بخلاف الخف، وإليه أشار بقوله : "فلا يتوقت إلخ " ، ثالثها: أن الجبيرة إذا سقطت عن غير برء لا ينتقض المسح بخلاف الخف، وإليه أشار بقوله: ولا يبطل إلخ، رابعها : إذا سقطت عن برء لا يجب عليه إلا غسل ذلك الموضع إذا كان على وضوء، بخلاف الخف حيث يجب عليه غسل الأخرى، وإليه أشار بقوله: "ويجوز مسح جبيرة إلخ"، خامسها: أن الجبيرة يستوي فيها الحدث الأكبر والأصغر بخلاف الخف، وإليه أشار بعدم اشتراط الطهارة في مسح الجبيرة، سادسها: أن الجبيرة يجب استيعابها في رواية بخلاف الخف؛ فإنه لا يجب استيعابه في رواية واحدة تبيين الحقائق: ١٥٦/١] وهي عيدان من جريدة تلف بورق وتربط على العضو المنكسر. [مراقي الفلاح: ١٣٤] غسل العضو : أطلقه فأفاد شرطية عدم استطاعة الغسل مطلقا لا بماء حار ولا بماء بارد، وقيل: لا يجب استعمال الماء الحار مراقي الفلاح ۱۳٥] كالغسل أشار إلى أنه ليس ببدل بخلاف المسح على الخفين، ولهذا لا يمسح على الخف في إحدى الرجلين ويغسل الأخرى؛ لأنه يؤدي إلى الجمع بين الأصل والبدل، ولو كانت الجبيرة في إحدى رجليه مسح عليها، وغسل الأخرى، ولا يكون ذلك جمعاً بين الأصل والبدل. تبيين الحقائق: ١٥٣/١] فلا يتوقت إلخ أي لا يتوقت المسح على الجبيرة؛ لأنه كالغسل لما تحتها على ما تقدم، والغسل لا يتوقت فكذا .هذا تبيين الحقائق: ١٥٤/١] ولا يشترط إلخ: أي جاز المسح على الجبيرة ونحوها وإن شدها على غير وضوء؛ لما قلنا أن صحة المسح لا يشترط لها شدها على طهر. ولا يبطل المسح إلخ : أي إن لم يكن سقوط الجبيرة ونحوها عن برء لا يبطل المسح. وأمر أي أمره طبيب حاذق مسلم مرارة : كيس لاصق بالكبد تختزن فيه الصفراء يقال له بالأردية پت ولا يفتقر إلخ وفي جوامع" "الفقه للعتابي : يشترط النية في المسح على الخفين فجعله كالتيمم؛ إذ كل واحد منهما بدل والأول أظهر؛ لأنه طهارة بالماء، فلا يفتقر إلى النية كالوضوء. تبيين الحقائق: ١٥٧/١]
The Book of Purification. Wiping over the splint. According to the correct view, the period passes if he does not fear loss of his foot entirely or partially due to cold, and after the last three he washes only his feet, and wiping over the turban, cap, face-veil, and mitts is not permitted. Section on the splint and similar items. If he underwent cupping, or was wounded, or his limb was broken and he ties it with a cloth... According to the correct view, this is based on the fact that wiping is a concession of relief (rukhsat tafreeh) while the resolution (azima) remains permissible...
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a detailed fiqh discussion on the rules of wiping over a splint (jabirah) in the Hanafi school. It begins with the general ruling that wiping over a splint is valid when washing is harmful. It then explains the conditions: the splint must be applied to a wound or break, and the person must be unable to wash or wipe the area directly. The passage clarifies that wiping over a splint is like washing (ghusl) in that it has no time limit, unlike wiping over khuff (leather socks). It also distinguishes between jabirah and khuff in six ways: (1) jabirah does not require prior ablution (wudu), (2) it is not time-bound, (3) if it falls off before healing, the wiping remains valid, (4) if it falls off after healing, only that spot needs washing, (5) it applies equally to major and minor impurity, and (6) in one narration, it must cover the entire splint. The text also addresses cases like eye inflammation (ramad) or broken nail, where medication is applied, and the ruling that intention (niyyah) is not required for wiping on khuff or jabirah, unlike for tayammum. The overall theme is that jabirah wiping is a substitute for washing and has leniencies.

Key Terms
جبيرة (jabīrah): Splint: sticks from a palm branch wrapped with paper and tied on a broken limb to set it.
رخصة ترفيه (rukṣat tarfīh): A concession of relief; the original act (azima) remains permissible alongside the concession.
عمامة (imāmah): Turban: a head covering wound around the head.
قلنسوة (qalansuwah): Cap: a skullcap worn under the turban.
برقع (burqu‘): Face veil: a piece of cloth covering the face, worn by women.
قفازين (quffāzayn): Mitts/gloves: padded hand covers worn by women for cold, or by falconers for protection.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a condition for wiping over a splint to be wajib?
A) The splint must have been applied in a state of wudu.
B) The person must be unable to wash the area due to harm.
C) The splint must remain on for at least 24 hours.
D) The injury must be on the feet or hands only.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over a splint is a water-based concession with leniencies: no time limit, no requirement of prior purity, and no invalidation if it falls off before healing.

Taharah — Purification

Six Differences Between Wiping Over Splint and Khuff
Lists and explains six differences between wiping over a splint and wiping over khuff.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list and explain the six differences between wiping over a splint (jabirah) and wiping over khuff as stated in the passage.

Core Idea
Six legal differences separate jabirah from khuff: intention, time, prior purity, falling off, equal treatment of impurites, and extent of wiping.

The passage explicitly enumerates six ways in which wiping over a splint differs from wiping over khuff. Understanding these differences is crucial for correctly applying the rulings in purification. This lesson walks through each difference with its practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six differences from the passage
The text lists: (1) jabirah does not require prior purity, (2) no time limit, (3) falling off before healing does not invalidate, (4) falling off after healing only requires washing that spot, (5) applies to both major and minor impurity, (6) in one narration, the entire splint must be wiped (as opposed to khuff where partial wiping suffices).
These are clearly enumerated in the passage after 'اعلم أن المسح على الجبيرة يخالف المسح على الخف من وجوه'.
2
Understand the first difference: no requirement of prior purity
For khuff, one must have washed the feet and then worn them in a state of wudu. For jabirah, the splint can be applied even in janabah.
This is because jabirah is a rukhsat tafreeh, not an abrogation.
3
Understand the second difference: no time limit
Khuff wiping is limited to one day and night for residents, three days for travelers. Jabirah wiping has no fixed duration; it remains valid as long as the splint is needed.
The text says 'فلا يتوقت بمدة'.
4
Understand the third and fourth differences: falling off
If the splint falls off before the injury heals, the wiping remains valid. If it falls off after healing, only that specific spot needs washing. For khuff, removing the khuff invalidates the wiping, and both feet must be washed.
The passage says 'لا يبطل المسح بسقوطها قبل البرء' and 'إذا سقطت عن برء لا يجب عليه إلا غسل ذلك الموضع'.
5
Understand the fifth and sixth differences: impurity and extent
Jabirah applies equally to major and minor impurity (no special condition), while khuff requires prior purity from minor hadath. Also, one narration requires wiping the entire splint (istī‘āb), unlike khuff where partial wiping suffices.
The sixth difference is limited to one riwaya; the relied-upon view may differ.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Wiping Over a Splint: Hanafi Rulings and Distinctions
Defines rulings for wiping over a splint on a broken limb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions and rulings of wiping over a splint (jabirah) and distinguish it from wiping over khuff.

Core Idea
Wiping over a splint is like washing, not a substitute — no time limit, no purity condition.

When a limb is broken and splinted, the usual obligation to wash that limb during wudu may be replaced by wiping over the splint. This concession has its own rules, which differ significantly from the familiar wiping over leather socks (khuff). Understanding these rules is essential for anyone who might face such an injury. The following passage from the Hanafi text explains the key rulings and the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling and its hukm level
Locate the main statement: wiping over the splint is wajib when the limb cannot be washed or wiped directly. Note that it is not fard; it is a concession that fulfills the obligation of washing.
The text uses 'wajaba' (وجب) indicating obligation.
2
Understand the conditions that trigger wajib
Identify the conditions: inability to wash the limb (with any water, hot or cold) and inability to wipe directly on the wound. Also note that the wiping must cover the majority of the splint.
The condition of inability is absolute — not just with cold water.
3
Compare with khuff to grasp the six differences
The passage enumerates six differences between wiping over a splint and wiping over khuff. For each, understand the ruling and the rationale: (1) no purity condition, (2) no time limit, (3) splint falling before recovery does not invalidate, (4) upon recovery only the spot needs washing, (5) valid for major and minor impurity, (6) full coverage recommended but not obligatory.
These distinctions stem from one key principle: wiping over a splint is like washing.
4
Analyze the reasoning (talil) that wiping is like washing
The text states 'wal-mash kāl-ghusl' (wiping is like washing). This principle explains why no time limit, no purity condition, and why combining wiping on one leg and washing the other is allowed (unlike khuff).
It is not a substitute (badal) but a direct performance of the obligation through wiping.
5
Apply to exceptional cases (ophthalmia, broken nail)
The passage extends the ruling to eye medicine or a broken nail with medicine: if washing is harmful and removal harmful, wiping over the dressing is allowed. Intention is not required for any wiping (khuff, splint, head).
This shows the principle of harm prevention (ḍarar) overrides normal requirements.

المسح على الجبيرة أو جبيرة، وكان لا يستطيع غسل العضو ولا يستطيع مسحه، وجب المسح على أكثر ما شد به العضو، وكفى المسح على ما ظهر من الجسد بين عصابة المفتصد، والمسح كالغسل فلا يتوقت بمدة، ولا يشترط شد الجبيرة على طهر، ويجوز مسح جبيرة هو الصحيح المسح على الجبيرة - إحدى الرجلين مع غسل الأخرى، ولا يبطل المسح بسقوطها قبل البرء، ويجوز تبديلها الرجل الصحة بعد مسحها بغيرها، ولا يجب إعادة المسح عليها، والأفضل إعادته، وإذا رمد وأمر أن لا يغسل الموضوعة بدلا على الثانية عينه، أو انكسر ظفره، وجعل عليه دواء وعلكا أو جلدة مرارة، وضره نزعه، جاز له المسح، وإن ضره المسح ،تركه، ولا يفتقر إلى النية في مسح الخف والجبيرة والرأس. جبيرة بخلاف الخف، وإليه أشار الشيخ بقوله: "ولا يشترط إلخ " ، ثانيها : أن المسح على الجبيرة غير موقت بخلاف الخف، وإليه أشار بقوله : "فلا يتوقت إلخ " ، ثالثها: أن الجبيرة إذا سقطت عن غير برء لا ينتقض المسح بخلاف الخف، وإليه أشار بقوله: ولا يبطل إلخ، رابعها : إذا سقطت عن برء لا يجب عليه إلا غسل ذلك الموضع إذا كان على وضوء، بخلاف الخف حيث يجب عليه غسل الأخرى، وإليه أشار بقوله: "ويجوز مسح جبيرة إلخ"، خامسها: أن الجبيرة يستوي فيها الحدث الأكبر والأصغر بخلاف الخف، وإليه أشار بعدم اشتراط الطهارة في مسح الجبيرة، سادسها: أن الجبيرة يجب استيعابها في رواية بخلاف الخف؛ فإنه لا يجب استيعابه في رواية واحدة تبيين الحقائق: ١٥٦/١] وهي عيدان من جريدة تلف بورق وتربط على العضو المنكسر. [مراقي الفلاح: ١٣٤] غسل العضو : أطلقه فأفاد شرطية عدم استطاعة الغسل مطلقا لا بماء حار ولا بماء بارد، وقيل: لا يجب استعمال الماء الحار مراقي الفلاح ۱۳٥] كالغسل أشار إلى أنه ليس ببدل بخلاف المسح على الخفين، ولهذا لا يمسح على الخف في إحدى الرجلين ويغسل الأخرى؛ لأنه يؤدي إلى الجمع بين الأصل والبدل، ولو كانت الجبيرة في إحدى رجليه مسح عليها، وغسل الأخرى، ولا يكون ذلك جمعاً بين الأصل والبدل. تبيين الحقائق: ١٥٣/١] فلا يتوقت إلخ أي لا يتوقت المسح على الجبيرة؛ لأنه كالغسل لما تحتها على ما تقدم، والغسل لا يتوقت فكذا .هذا تبيين الحقائق: ١٥٤/١] ولا يشترط إلخ: أي جاز المسح على الجبيرة ونحوها وإن شدها على غير وضوء؛ لما قلنا أن صحة المسح لا يشترط لها شدها على طهر. ولا يبطل المسح إلخ : أي إن لم يكن سقوط الجبيرة ونحوها عن برء لا يبطل المسح. وأمر أي أمره طبيب حاذق مسلم مرارة : كيس لاصق بالكبد تختزن فيه الصفراء يقال له بالأردية پت ولا يفتقر إلخ وفي جوامع" "الفقه للعتابي : يشترط النية في المسح على الخفين فجعله كالتيمم؛ إذ كل واحد منهما بدل والأول أظهر؛ لأنه طهارة بالماء، فلا يفتقر إلى النية كالوضوء. تبيين الحقائق: ١٥٧/١] من
Wiping over the splint: Or a splint, and if he cannot wash the limb nor wipe it, then wiping is obligatory over most of what the limb is tied with, and wiping suffices on what appears of the body between the bandage of the phlebotomist, and wiping is like washing, so it is not limited by a duration, and it is not a condition that the splint be tied upon purity, and it is permissible to wipe the splint – this is the correct position. Wiping over the splint in one of the two legs along with washing the other, and wiping is not invalidated by its falling before recovery, and it is permissible to replace it after wiping it with another, and it is not obligatory to repeat wiping upon it, and it is better to repeat it. And if one has ophthalmia and is ordered not to wash the eye, or his nail breaks and he puts medicine and gum or a piece of gallbladder on it, and removing it harms him, it is permissible for him to wipe, and if wiping harms him, he leaves it, and intention is not needed for wiping over the khuff, the splint, and the head. Splint differs from khuff, and the shaykh pointed to it by his saying: “It is not conditional etc.” Second: that wiping over the splint is not time-limited unlike khuff, and he pointed to it by his saying: “So it is not limited etc.” Third: if the splint falls without recovery, wiping is not invalidated unlike khuff, and he pointed to it by his saying: “it is not invalidated etc.” Fourth: if it falls after recovery, he is only required to wash that spot if he is in a state of wudu, unlike khuff where he must wash the other foot, and he pointed to it by his saying: “and it is permissible to wipe the splint etc.” Fifth: the splint makes equal major and minor impurity unlike khuff, and he pointed to it by not requiring purity for wiping the splint. Sixth: the splint must be fully covered according to one narration unlike khuff; for it is not obligatory to cover fully according to one narration. Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 1/156: They are sticks from a palm branch wrapped with paper and tied on the broken limb. [Maraqi al-Falah 134] Washing the limb: he gave it absolutely, so it indicates the condition of inability to wash absolutely, not with hot water nor with cold water, and it is said: using hot water is not obligatory. [Maraqi al-Falah 135] Like washing: he indicated that it is not a substitute unlike wiping over khuff, and for this reason one does not wipe over the khuff on one foot and wash the other; because it leads to combining the original and substitute, but if there is a splint on one of his feet, he wipes over it and washes the other, and that is not combining the original and substitute. Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 1/153: “So it is not limited etc.” meaning wiping over the splint is not time-limited because it is like washing what is underneath as stated, and washing is not limited, so likewise. Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 1/154: “It is not conditional etc.” meaning it is permissible to wipe over the splint and the like even if he tied it without wudu; because we said the validity of wiping does not require tying it in a state of purity. “And wiping is not invalidated etc.” meaning if the splint or the like does not fall after recovery, wiping is not invalidated. “And ordered” meaning he ordered a skillful Muslim doctor. “Gallbladder”: a sac attached to the liver storing bile, called in Urdu “پت”. “And it does not require etc.” And in Jami' al-Fiqh by al-'Utabi: intention is required for wiping over khuff, making it like tayammum; since each of them is a substitute, but the first is more apparent because it is purification with water, so it does not require intention like wudu. Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 1/157.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-elaboration on wiping over a splint (jabirah) for a broken limb. The text first states the ruling: if a person cannot wash the injured limb or wipe directly on the injury, then wiping over the majority of the splint is obligatory. Wiping over the exposed skin between the bandages is sufficient. Then it draws a key distinction: wiping over a splint is like washing (ghusl) in that it does not have a fixed time limit, unlike wiping over khuff (leather socks). Further, it is not required that the splint be applied while in a state of purity (wudu). The text then lists six differences between wiping over a splint and wiping over khuff, as highlighted by the commentary: (1) no condition of purity for splint, (2) no time limit, (3) if splint falls before recovery, wiping is not invalidated, (4) if splint falls upon recovery, only that spot needs washing if in wudu, (5) splint applies to both major and minor impurity, (6) according to one narration, one must wipe the entire splint. The commentary from Tabyin al-Haqa'iq explains the reasoning: it is like washing the underlying part, not a substitute, hence it does not combine original and substitute. The passage also covers cases of eye medicine or broken nail where wiping is allowed if washing is harmful. Intention is not required for wiping over khuff, splint, or head, as it is a water-based purification akin to wudu.

Key Terms
جبيرة (jabīrah): Splint made from palm sticks or similar, wrapped with cloth and tied on a broken limb.
مسح (mash): Wiping with a wet hand over the splint or socks.
الخف (al-khuff): Leather socks worn over the feet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Wiping over a splint requires the splint to be tied in a state of purity.
D) Wiping over a splint is invalidated if the splint falls before recovery.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over a splint is a lenient obligation: no time limit, no purity condition, and intention not required—making it unlike khuff in six specific ways.

Taharah — Purification

Definition and Types of Female Bleeding (Hayd, Nifas, Istihadah)
defines the three types of female bleeding and their criteria

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of hayd, nifas, and istihadah, and apply the temporal limits to determine whether a particular bleeding episode is hayd or istihadah.

Core Idea
Hayd is womb-blood of a mature, healthy, non-pregnant, pre-menopausal woman lasting 3-10 days; bleeding outside these parameters is istihadah.

This lesson introduces the foundational categories of female bleeding in Hanafi fiqh. Understanding these definitions is crucial for correctly applying rulings related to prayer, fasting, and ritual purity. We will parse the precise conditions that make blood hayd and distinguish it from other types.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types
Read the opening sentence: 'yakhruju min al-farj hayḍ wa nifās wa istiḥāḍah'. List them.
These are the three recognized types in the madhhab.
2
Parse the definition of hayd
Break down the definition: 'dam tunfiḍuhu raḥim bālighatin lā dāa bihā wa lā ḥibl wa lam tablugh sinn al-iyās'. Identify each exclusionary clause.
Each clause excludes a specific case: womb vs. vein, puberty, illness, pregnancy, menopause.
3
Note the temporal limits
Memorize: aqall 3 days, awsaṭ 5, akthar 10. Understand that these include nights and that intermittent bleeding still counts as hayd if blood is seen at the beginning and end.
Continuous flow is not required; presence of blood at start and end suffices.
4
Understand wasted blood
Read the commentary on 'al-dam al-ḍāʾiʿ'—blood seen before age nine. It carries no legal rulings and differs from istihadah in that it does not 'corrupt' a subsequent valid hayd.
This is an additional category from later scholars, not in the original definition.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a woman's bleeding pattern, check the conditions and duration to classify the blood as hayd or istihadah.
Use the conditions as a checklist.

باب الحيض والنفاس والاستحاضة يخرج من الفرج حيض ونفاس واستحاضة، فالحيض: دم ينفضه رحم بالغة لا داء بها ولا حبل و لم تبلغ سن الإياس، وأقل الحيض ثلاثة أيام، وأوسطه خمسة، وأكثره عشرة. بلياليها يخرج: اعلم أن الدماء المختصة بالنساء ثلاثة حيض ونفاس واستحاضة، وقد جعلها بعض المتأخرين أربعة أقسام: هذه الثلاثة والضائع، قالوا: والدم الضائع ما تراه قبل وقت البلوغ، وإنما سموه الضائع بمعنيين: أحدهما: أنه لا يترتب عليها أحكام الاستحاضة من الوضوء والصلاة والصوم وغيرها والثاني: أن دم الاستحاضة يفسد دم الحيض بالشوب، وهذا الدم لا يفسد حتى أن المراهقة إذا رأت قبل تمام تسع سنين خمسة أيام، وعقبها بعد تمام التسع ثمانية أيام، وطهرت طهراً صحيحاً، كانت الثمانية عادة لها بالإجماع، ولو كان دم استحاضة لفسد بها الثمانية. [الكفاية ١٤٢/١] فالحيض إلخ احترز بقوله: "رحم" عن الرعاف والدماء الخارجة . من الجراحات، ودم المستحاضة؛ فإنها دم عرق لا دم رحم، ويقوله: "لا داء بها عن دم النفاس؛ فإن النفساء في حكم المريضة حتى اعتبر تبرعاتها. وبقوله: "بالغة" عن دم تراه الصغيرة قبل أن تبلغ تسع سنين؛ فإنه ليس بمعتبر في الشرع، وفيه نوع إشكال، فإن ما تراه الصغيرة استحاضة، وليس بدم رحم ظاهرا، فخرج بقوله: "ينفضه رحم إلخ"، فلا حاجة إلى ذكره، وأيضا يتكرر إخراج الاستحاضة؛ لأن قوله: "لا داء بها" يخرجه كما يخرجه الأول، فتعريفه بلا استدراك، ولا تكرر دم من الرحم لا لولادة. من الثلث رحم: هو محل تربية ولد من نطفة بالغة أي بالغة تسع سنين، هو ما عليه الفتوى، وقيل: يتأتى حيضها فيما بين الخمس إلى التسع، وأما بنت خمس فلا تحيض بالإجماع مراقي الفلاح وحاشية الطحطاوي: ١٣٨] لا داء بها: أطلقه وهو مقيد بداء تقتضي خروج دم ،بسببه، فإن مرضت مرضا وسلمت رحمها، فالدم الخارج من رحمها حيض ألبتة، وعلى إطلاقه يمتنع كونه حيضا، فإن بها داء. منه ولا حبل الأجل إنسداد فم الرحم] قيد به؛ لأن عادة الله تعالى جرت بأن ينسد فم رحم الحامل، فلا يخرج شيء حتى يخرج الولد أو أكثره الإياس : قال في "المراقي": هو خمس وخمسون سنة على المفتى به. [ص: ۱۳۹] وفي "العناية": الإياس يحصل بانقطاع الدم مرة، لا تصلح لنصب العادة عند ستين سنة، وعند أكثرهم عند خمس وخمسين، والفتوى في زماننا عند الخمسين. ثلاثة: فإن قلت: لا يصح الحمل؛ لأن الحيض ليست من جنس الأيام، قلنا: هذا على تقدير مضاف أي زمن أقل الحيض. أيام: اعلم أنه لا يشترط أن يستغرق نزول الدم ثلاثة أو عشرة؛ لأن ذلك نادر، فرؤيته كل يوم ولو شيئا قليلا تكفي كما في "السراج"، بل المعتبر وجوده في أول المدة وآخرها ولو تخلل بينهما طهر، ويجعل الكل حيضاً. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٣٩]
Chapter on Hayd, Nifas, and Istihadah. From the private part comes hayd, nifas, and istihadah. Hayd (menstruation) is blood that the womb expels from a balighah (woman past puberty), who has no illness, no pregnancy, and has not reached the age of menopause. The minimum of hayd is three days, its average is five, and its maximum is ten, including their nights. Explanation: Know that the bloods specific to women are three: hayd, nifas, and istihadah. Some later scholars made them four divisions: these three and al-da'i' (wasted blood). They said: wasted blood is what a girl sees before the time of puberty. They called it wasted in two senses: first, that the rulings of istihadah (wudu, prayer, fasting, etc.) do not apply to it; second, that istihadah blood corrupts hayd blood by mixture, but this blood does not corrupt, so if a girl nearing puberty sees five days before completing nine years, and after completing nine years sees eight days and then has a true purification, the eight days become her habit by consensus, and if it were istihadah blood, it would corrupt the eight. [Kifayah 1/142] “Al-hayd etc.” He guarded by his saying “womb” from nosebleed and blood coming from wounds, and from the blood of the mustahadah (woman with non-menstrual bleeding) because it is blood from a vein, not womb blood. And by his saying “no illness” he guards against postpartum blood; for the woman in nifas is in the ruling of a sick person such that her voluntary bequests are considered. And by his saying “balighah” he guards against blood that a minor girl sees before reaching nine years; for it is not considered in Shari'ah, and there is some difficulty because what the minor sees is istihadah and not womb blood apparently, so it is excluded by his saying “the womb expels it etc.” So there is no need to mention it, and also it repeats the exclusion of istihadah because his saying “no illness” excludes it as the first does. So his definition is without redundancy and without repetition: blood from the womb not due to childbirth. The womb is the place of rearing a child from a sperm; “balighah” means nine years old – this is what the fatwa is upon. And it is said her hayd can occur between five and nine years, but a five-year-old does not menstruate by consensus. [Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 138] “No illness” he gave absolutely, but it is restricted to an illness that necessitates the exit of blood; if she is sick but her womb is sound, the blood from her womb is definitely hayd, but if taken absolutely, it would prevent it from being hayd because she has an illness. “And no pregnancy” is a restriction because Allah's custom is that the mouth of the womb of a pregnant woman is closed, so nothing comes out until the child or most of it emerges. “Menopause”: al-Maraqi said it is fifty-five years according to the fatwa. [p.139] In al-'Inayah, menopause occurs by the cessation of blood once, and it is not suitable for establishing a habit at sixty years, and according to most it is at fifty-five, but the fatwa in our time is at fifty. “Three”: if you say the count is not correct because hayd is not of the same genus as days, we say this is with an implicit addition, i.e., the time of minimum hayd is three days. “Days”: know that it is not required that the bleeding last continuously for three or ten because that is rare; seeing it every day even a little suffices as in al-Siraj, but rather what counts is its presence at the beginning and end of the period even if a pure period intervenes, and it is all considered hayd. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 139]
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on the three types of female bleeding: hayd (menstruation), nifas (postpartum bleeding), and istihadah (non-menstrual uterine bleeding). The text first defines hayd as blood expelled from the womb of a woman who is balighah (past the age of puberty, set at nine years), with no illness (that causes the bleeding), no pregnancy, and not yet menopausal. The minimum period is three full days and nights, the average five, and the maximum ten. The commentary explains that some later scholars add a fourth type, 'wasted blood' (al-da'i'), which is blood seen before puberty and carries no legal rulings. The definition of 'womb' excludes blood from other sources (nosebleeds, wounds) and istihadah (which comes from a vein, not the womb). 'No illness' excludes postpartum blood, since the postpartum woman (nafsa') is treated as sick for certain rulings. 'Balighah' excludes blood of minors under nine, which is considered istihadah. The commentary clarifies that the minimum and maximum durations are counted by presence of blood at the start and end, even if pure days intervene, as long as blood is seen at least during those times. The age of menopause is given as fifty-five years according to the fatwa, but in current times it is fixed at fifty.

Key Terms
الحيض (al-ḥayḍ): Blood that the womb expels from a balighah woman without illness, pregnancy, or menopause, lasting between three and ten days.
النفاس (al-nifās): Blood that exits after childbirth or when most of the child has emerged; treated like hayd in most rulings.
الاستحاضة (al-istiḥāḍah): Non-menstrual bleeding from a vein (not the womb); woman performs wudu for each prayer, fasts, etc.
الدم الضائع (al-dam al-ḍāʾiʿ): Blood seen before puberty (under nine years) according to some later Hanafi scholars; has no legal consequences.
الإياس (al-iyās): Age of menopause beyond which a woman does not expect menstruation; set at fifty-five years in the fatwa, but at fifty in current practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum duration of menstruation (hayd) according to this passage?
A) One day
B) Three days and their nights
C) Five days
D) Ten days

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of hayd is precise: blood from the womb of a balighah woman, free from illness and pregnancy, not menopausal, lasting 3-10 days; any uterine bleeding outside these parameters is istihadah.

Taharah — Purification
beginner

Definitions of Hayd, Nifas, and Istihadah
Defining female-specific blood types and their limits.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definitions and limits of hayd, nifas, and istihadah, and identify the conditions that distinguish istihadah from hayd and nifas.

Core Idea
Hayd has a fixed range (3–10 days); nifas max 40 days; istihadah is any bleeding outside these bounds.

This passage lays out the foundational categories of female-specific blood in Hanafi fiqh. Understanding these definitions is essential for determining the rulings of purity, prayer, and fasting for women. The text provides precise conditions and time limits that distinguish normal menstruation from postpartum bleeding and irregular uterine bleeding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three blood types
List the three types: hayd, nifas, and istihadah. Note that some later scholars add a fourth (wasted blood) for pre-puberty bleeding.
The wasted blood (dam dha'i) does not carry istihadah rulings and does not corrupt the menstrual habit.
2
Examine conditions for hayd
Hayd requires: blood from the womb (not a vein or wound), maturity (at least 9 years), no illness, no pregnancy, and before menopause.
The condition 'no illness' distinguishes hayd from nifas (postpartum blood, where the woman is considered ill).
3
Note time limits for hayd and nifas
Hayd minimum 3 days (including nights), average 5, maximum 10. Nifas maximum 40 days, no minimum.
For hayd, bleeding need not be continuous; presence at beginning and end suffices.
4
Define istihadah
Istihadah is any bleeding less than 3 days (if within menstrual period) or exceeding 10 days in hayd or 40 in nifas. It is blood from a vein, not the womb.
A woman in istihadah performs wudu for each prayer and prays; she is not exempt from worship.
5
Understand the minimum purity interval (tuhr)
Between two hayd periods, there must be at least 15 days of purity. There is no maximum, except for a mustahada (who has irregular bleeding) whose habit is used.
This ensures that consecutive bleeding episodes are identified as separate menstrual cycles.

يخرج من الفرج حيض ونفاس واستحاضة، فالحيض: دم ينفضه رحم بالغة لا داء بها يدفعه بقوة ولا حبل و لم تبلغ سن الإياس، وأقل الحيض ثلاثة أيام، وأوسطه خمسة، وأكثره عشرة. بلياليها يخرج: اعلم أن الدماء المختصة بالنساء ثلاثة حيض ونفاس واستحاضة، وقد جعلها بعض المتأخرين أربعة أقسام: هذه الثلاثة والضائع، قالوا: والدم الضائع ما تراه قبل وقت البلوغ، وإنما سموه الضائع بمعنيين: أحدهما: أنه لا يترتب عليها أحكام الاستحاضة من الوضوء والصلاة والصوم وغيرها والثاني: أن دم الاستحاضة يفسد دم الحيض بالشوب، وهذا الدم لا يفسد حتى أن المراهقة إذا رأت قبل تمام تسع سنين خمسة أيام، وعقبها بعد تمام التسع ثمانية أيام، وطهرت طهراً صحيحاً، كانت الثمانية عادة لها بالإجماع، ولو كان دم استحاضة لفسد بها الثمانية. [الكفاية ١٤٢/١] فالحيض إلخ احترز بقوله: "رحم" عن الرعاف والدماء الخارجة . من الجراحات، ودم المستحاضة؛ فإنها دم عرق لا دم رحم، ويقوله: "لا داء بها عن دم النفاس؛ فإن النفساء في حكم المريضة حتى اعتبر تبرعاتها. وبقوله: "بالغة" عن دم تراه الصغيرة قبل أن تبلغ تسع سنين؛ فإنه ليس بمعتبر في الشرع، وفيه نوع إشكال، فإن ما تراه الصغيرة استحاضة، وليس بدم رحم ظاهرا، فخرج بقوله: "ينفضه رحم إلخ"، فلا حاجة إلى ذكره، وأيضا يتكرر إخراج الاستحاضة؛ لأن قوله: "لا داء بها" يخرجه كما يخرجه الأول، فتعريفه بلا استدراك، ولا تكرر دم من الرحم لا لولادة. من الثلث رحم: هو محل تربية ولد من نطفة بالغة أي بالغة تسع سنين، هو ما عليه الفتوى، وقيل: يتأتى حيضها فيما بين الخمس إلى التسع، وأما بنت خمس فلا تحيض بالإجماع مراقي الفلاح وحاشية الطحطاوي: ١٣٨] لا داء بها: أطلقه وهو مقيد بداء تقتضي خروج دم ،بسببه، فإن مرضت مرضا وسلمت رحمها، فالدم الخارج من رحمها حيض ألبتة، وعلى إطلاقه يمتنع كونه حيضا، فإن بها داء. منه ولا حبل الأجل إنسداد فم الرحم] قيد به؛ لأن عادة الله تعالى جرت بأن ينسد فم رحم الحامل، فلا يخرج شيء حتى يخرج الولد أو أكثره الإياس : قال في "المراقي": هو خمس وخمسون سنة على المفتى به. [ص: ۱۳۹] وفي "العناية": الإياس يحصل بانقطاع الدم مرة، لا تصلح لنصب العادة عند ستين سنة، وعند أكثرهم عند خمس وخمسين، والفتوى في زماننا عند الخمسين. ثلاثة: فإن قلت: لا يصح الحمل؛ لأن الحيض ليست من جنس الأيام، قلنا: هذا على تقدير مضاف أي زمن أقل الحيض. أيام: اعلم أنه لا يشترط أن يستغرق نزول الدم ثلاثة أو عشرة؛ لأن ذلك نادر، فرؤيته كل يوم ولو شيئا قليلا تكفي كما في "السراج"، بل المعتبر وجوده في أول المدة وآخرها ولو تخلل بينهما طهر، ويجعل الكل حيضاً. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٣٩] والنفاس: هو الدم الخارج عقب الولادة، وأكثره أربعون يوماً، ولا حد لأقله. والاستحاضة دم نقص عن ثلاثة أيام أو زاد على عشرة في الحيض، وعلى أربعين في النفاس، وأقل الطهر الفاصل بين الحيضتين خمسة عشر يوماً، ولا حد لأكثره إلا أو بين الحيض والنفاس لمن بلغت مستحاضة.
From the private part exit hayd, nifas, and istihadah. Hayd: blood that the womb of a mature woman expels with force, there being no illness, no pregnancy, and she has not reached the age of menopause. The minimum of hayd is three days, its average is five, and its maximum is ten, including their nights. Know that the bloods specific to women are three: hayd, nifas, and istihadah. Some later scholars made them four: these three and the wasted blood. They said: wasted blood is what a girl sees before the time of puberty. They named it wasted for two meanings: first, that the rulings of istihadah (ablution, prayer, fasting, etc.) do not apply to it; second, that istihadah blood corrupts hayd blood by mixing, but this blood does not corrupt, such that if a girl nearing puberty sees five days before completing nine years and then after completing nine sees eight days and has a valid purity, the eight days become her habit by consensus. If it were istihadah blood, it would have corrupted the eight. [Al-Kifayah 1/142] So 'hayd' etc. He guarded by saying 'womb' against nosebleed and blood exiting from wounds, and the blood of a mustahada, for it is blood of a vein not womb-blood. And by saying 'no illness' against nifas blood, for the postpartum woman is in the ruling of a sick person such that her charitable gifts are considered. And by saying 'mature' against blood a little girl sees before reaching nine years, for it is not considered in the Shari'a. There is some difficulty, for what a little girl sees is istihadah and is not womb-blood apparently. So it exits by his saying 'the womb expels it', so there is no need to mention it. Also the exclusion of istihadah is repeated, because his saying 'no illness' excludes it as does the first. So his definition is without correction and no repetition of blood from the womb not due to childbirth. 'Womb': it is the place of raising a child from a drop. 'Mature' meaning reaching nine years; that is the fatwa. It was said: her menstruation occurs between five and nine. As for a daughter of five, she does not menstruate by consensus. [Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 138] 'No illness': it is unrestricted but restricted to an illness that necessitates the exit of blood due to it. If she is ill and her womb is healthy, the blood exiting from her womb is hayd absolutely. On its unrestricted meaning, it is prevented from being hayd, for she has an illness. 'And no pregnancy' i.e. closure of the mouth of the womb. He restricted by it because Allah's custom is that the mouth of the pregnant woman's womb closes, so nothing exits until the child or most of it exits. 'Menopause': Al-Maraqi said: it is fifty-five years on the relied-upon opinion. [p. 139] In Al-Inayah: menopause occurs by the cessation of blood once; it is not suitable for setting a habit at sixty years. According to most, it is at fifty-five, and the fatwa in our time is at fifty. 'Three': if you say, the count is not valid because hayd is not of the genre of days, we say: this is on the basis of an implied word i.e. a period of minimum hayd. 'Days': know that it is not required that the descent of blood cover the whole three or ten days, because that is rare. Seeing it every day, even a little, suffices as in Al-Siraj. Rather, consideration is given to its presence at the beginning and end of the period, even if there is purity in between, and all is made hayd. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 139] Nifas: the blood that exits after childbirth. Its maximum is forty days, and there is no minimum limit. Istihadah: blood that is less than three days or exceeds ten in hayd, and forty in nifas. The minimum of purity separating two hayd periods is fifteen days, and there is no maximum, except between hayd and nifas for a woman who reaches puberty as a mustahada.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling statement categorizing the three types of blood specific to women: hayd (menstruation), nifas (postpartum bleeding), and istihadah (irregular uterine bleeding). The author begins by stating the general principle: from the private part emerge these three types. Then he defines each. Hayd is defined with several conditions: it must be blood expelled from the womb of a mature woman (at least nine years old, which is the age of puberty for girls in the Hanafi school), with force, and without the presence of illness, pregnancy, or menopause. The minimum duration of hayd is three days (including nights), the average is five, and the maximum is ten. The commentary then expands on each phrase: the word 'womb' excludes blood from other sources like nosebleeds or wounds; 'no illness' excludes postpartum bleeding (nifas) because the postpartum woman is considered ill for legal purposes (e.g., her charitable bequests are limited); 'mature' excludes blood seen before the age of nine, which is not legally considered hayd but rather istihadah or 'wasted blood'. The concept of 'wasted blood' (dam dha'i) is introduced by some later scholars: this blood does not trigger the rules of istihadah (like wudu) and does not corrupt the habit of hayd by mixing. The passage then discusses the age of puberty and menopause. The relied-upon view for menopause is fifty-five years, but the fatwa in our time is at fifty. An important point is that the bleeding need not be continuous within the three days; if blood appears at the beginning and end, even with purity in between, the entire period counts as hayd. Finally, nifas is defined as blood following childbirth with a maximum of forty days (no minimum), and istihadah is any bleeding that falls short of the minimum or exceeds the maximum of hayd or nifas. The purity between two menstruations must be at least fifteen days. This passage is foundational for understanding the rulings of female impurity in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
حيض (hayd): Blood that the womb of a mature woman expels with force, without illness or pregnancy, and before menopause, lasting between three and ten days.
نفاس (nifas): Blood that exits after childbirth; maximum forty days, no minimum.
استحاضة (istihadah): Irregular uterine bleeding that is less than three days (if it occurs in the menstrual period) or exceeds ten days in hayd or forty in nifas.
دم ضائع (dam dha'i): Blood seen by a girl before the age of puberty (nine years); it does not carry the rulings of istihadah and does not corrupt the habit.
إياس (iyas): Menopause; the cessation of menstrual blood. In the Hanafi school, it is set at fifty-five years (or fifty in later fatwa).
طهر (tuhr): The state of purity between two menstrual periods; minimum duration is fifteen days.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum duration of tuhr (state of purity) between two hayd periods according to the Hanafi school?
A) 10 days
B) 15 days
C) 40 days
D) 3 days

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines hayd as blood from the womb of a mature woman lasting 3-10 days, nifas as postpartum blood up to 40 days, and istihadah as any other uterine bleeding; the minimum pure interval between hayd periods is 15 days.

The Eight Prohibitions During Hayd and Nifas
Listing and explaining the eight prohibitions with exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the eight prohibitions during hayd and nifas, identify the exceptions for recitation, touching the Mushaf, and entering the mosque, and apply the ruling that intention and necessity create exceptions.

Core Idea
Eight acts are haram during hayd and nifas, but necessity, covering, and dhikr intention create well-defined exceptions.

This passage from Nur al-Idah lists five of the eight prohibitions explicitly, with the full list comprising eight. The commentary clarifies key exceptions and addresses a potential objection about fasting. Understanding these rules ensures that a menstruating or postpartum woman can maintain her devotion within the bounds of the Shari'a.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the core prohibitions
Identify the five acts explicitly listed: prayer (salat), fasting (sawm), reciting a verse with tilawah intention, touching the Mushaf except with a covering, and entering a mosque. Note that the text states eight; other prohibitions include tawaf, sexual intercourse, and i'tikaf.
The five are the most commonly encountered.
2
Understand the general hukm
Each act is haram (forbidden) during hayd and nifas. The prohibition applies regardless of wudu because the hadath is ongoing. Exceptions are made for necessity and specific intentions.
The hukm is based on the permanent impurity that prevents validity of these acts.
3
Analyze the exception for recitation
Reciting a verse is forbidden only when the intention is tilawah (recitation for reward). If the intention is dhikr (e.g., saying Bismillah) or teaching/learning, it is permitted by agreement.
The determining factor is the niyyah.
4
Analyze the exception for touching the Mushaf
Touching the Mushaf is forbidden except with a covering (ghilaf) or in necessity (e.g., to save it from fire or water). The prohibition extends even if the text is in Persian.
Scholars may handle the Mushaf with a sleeve due to necessity.
5
Analyze the exception for entering a mosque
Entering a mosque is forbidden, including the Ka'bah. Exceptions: Eid and funeral prayer grounds are excluded; necessity (e.g., the house door opens into the mosque) permits it. The prohibition is lifted when there is a genuine need.
Passing through the mosque for a valid reason is allowed.

ما يحرم بالحيض والنفاس] ويحرم بالحيض والنفاس ثمانية أشياء: الصلاة والصوم وقراءة آية من القرآن، ومسها إلا بغلاف ودخول مسجد . متجاف عن القرآن عقب الولادة: ينبغي أن يزاد في التعريف فيقال: "عقب الولادة من الفرج؛ فإنها لو ولدت من قبل سُرتها فانشقت بأن كان ببطنها جرح وخرج الولد منها، تكون صاحبة جرح سائل لا نفساء. [حاشية الشلبي على تبيين الحقائق: ١٨٦/١] لمن بلغت إلخ أي بأن ابتدأت مع البلوغ مستحاضة فيقدر حيضها بعشرة، وطهرها بخمسة عشر يوماً، ونفاسها بأربعين والصوم: لا يقال: كان ينبغي أن يجوز الصوم مع الحيض كما يجوز مع الجنابة؛ لأنا نقول: الكف عن المفطرات الثلاثة في الجنابة موجود، فيجوز الصوم، وفي الحيض الكف عنها لأجل الصوم لا يوجد؛ لأن الكف عن الجماع لأجل الحيض لا لأجل الصوم، فلهذا لا يجوز صومها. [حاشية الشلبي: ١٦١/١] وقراءة إلخ: هذا إذا قرأه على قصد التلاوة، أما إذا قرأه على قصد الذكر والثناء نحو: بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم أو الحمد لله رب العالمين، أو علم القرآن حرفا حرفا، فلا بأس به بالاتفاق؛ لأجل العذر ، ذكر في "المحيط". [تبيين الحقائق: ١٦٥/١] ومسها إلا بغلاف: ويستثنى منه موضع الضرورة؛ لخوف حرق المصحف، أو غرقه، ويحرم ولو كتبه بالفارسية إجماعا. فروع ويكره بالكم تحريماً، ويرخص لأهل كتب الشريعة أخذها بالكم وباليد؛ للضرورة إلا التفسير؛ فإنه يجب الوضوء لمسه والمستحب أن لا يأخذها إلا بوضوء، ويجوز تقليب أوراق المصحف بنحو قلم للقراءة، ولا يجوز لف شيء في كاغذ كتب فيه فقه أو اسم الله تعالى أو النبي ، ونهي عن محو اسم الله تعالى بالبزاق، ومثله النبي تعظيما، ويستر المصحف لوطء زوجته ،استحياء، ولا يرمي براية قلم ولا حشيش المسجد في محل ممتهن. [مراقي الفلاح: ١٤٣] ودخول مسجد: شمل الكعبة دون مصلى عيد وجنازة في الأصح، وقيد المنع في "الدرر" بأن لا يكون ثمة ضرورة، فإن كانت كأن يكون باب البيت إلى المسجد، فلا ، قال في "البحر": وينبغي أن يقيد بأن لا يمكن =
What is forbidden by hayd and nifas? Eight things are forbidden by hayd and nifas: prayer, fasting, reciting a verse of the Qur'an, touching it except with a covering, and entering a mosque. 'After childbirth': it should be added in the definition: 'after childbirth from the private part; for if she gives birth from above her navel such that there was a wound in her belly and the child came out from it, she is a person with a flowing wound, not a postpartum woman.' [Hashiyah al-Shalabi on Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 1/186] 'For a woman who reaches puberty as a mustahada' meaning she begins with puberty as a mustahada. Then her hayd is estimated as ten days, her purity as fifteen days, and her nifas as forty. 'Fasting': it should not be said that fasting should be permitted during hayd just as it is permitted during janaba; because we say: abstention from three invalidators during janaba exists, so fasting is valid. During hayd, abstention from them for the sake of fasting does not exist, because abstention from intercourse is due to hayd, not due to fasting, therefore her fasting is not valid. [Hashiyah al-Shalabi 1/161] 'And reciting' etc.: This is if he recites with the intention of recitation. But if he recites with the intention of remembrance and praise, like 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' or 'Alhamdu lillahi Rabb al-'Alamin', or teaching the Qur'an letter by letter, then there is no harm by agreement due to necessity. Mentioned in Al-Muhit. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 1/165] 'And touching it except with a covering': exceptions are made for necessity, such as fear of the mushaf burning or drowning. It is forbidden even if written in Persian by consensus. Branches: it is makruh tahriman with the sleeve, and it is permitted for scholars of the Shari'a to take it with the sleeve and hand due to necessity, except for the tafsir, for which wudu is required to touch it. It is recommended not to take it except with wudu. It is permissible to turn the pages of the mushaf with a pen, etc., for reading. It is not permissible to wrap something in paper that has fiqh or the name of Allah or the Prophet written on it. It is forbidden to wipe the name of Allah with saliva, and similarly the Prophet, as a respect. It is recommended to cover the mushaf when having intercourse with one's wife, out of modesty. One should not throw used pen wrapper or mosque grass in a disrespectful place. [Maraqi al-Falah: 143] 'Entering a mosque': includes the Ka'bah but excludes the Eid prayer place and funeral prayer place in the most correct view. The prohibition is restricted in Al-Durar to cases where there is no necessity. If there is necessity, like the door of the house being to the mosque, then it is not prohibited. Al-Bahr said: it should be restricted to where it is not possible...
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage enumerates the eight things forbidden during hayd and nifas: prayer, fasting, reciting even one verse of the Qur'an (with the intention of tilawah), touching the Qur'an except with a covering, and entering a mosque. The commentary then expands on each prohibition. First, a clarification about the definition of nifas: it must be blood that exits from the vagina after childbirth; if the child emerges from a wound in the abdomen, it is not nifas but rather a flowing wound. Second, for a woman who begins as a mustahada at puberty, her hayd is estimated as ten days, her purity as fifteen, and her nifas as forty. Regarding fasting, the text refutes a potential objection: why is fasting invalid during hayd while it is valid during janaba? The difference is that during janaba, abstention from eating, drinking, and intercourse for the sake of fasting is present, while during hayd, abstention from intercourse is due to hayd itself, not for the fast, so the fast is not valid. Regarding Qur'an recitation, it is forbidden only if the intention is tilawah; for the purpose of dhikr, praise, or teaching letter by letter, it is permitted by agreement due to necessity. Touching the Qur'an is forbidden except with a covering, but necessity allows it (e.g., to save it from fire or water). The commentary also includes branches: touching with the sleeve is makruh tahriman, and it is permitted for scholars to handle it for necessity. Entering the mosque is forbidden; this includes the Ka'bah but not the Eid or funeral prayer grounds. However, if there is a necessity (e.g., the house door opens into the mosque), then it is permitted. This passage provides a comprehensive list of prohibitions with important exceptions, especially for the Qur'an and the mosque.

Key Terms
مسها إلا بغلاف (massuha illa bighilaf): Touching the Qur'an except with a covering (ghilaf). This is forbidden for a menstruating woman, but she may touch it with a barrier (like a cloth) or in necessity.
دخول مسجد (dukhul masjid): Entering a mosque. Forbidden for a menstruating woman, but the Ka'bah is included; Eid and funeral prayer places are excluded. Necessity permits it.
قراءة آية (qira'ah ayah): Reciting a verse of the Qur'an with the intention of tilawah. Forbidden. But if the intention is dhikr or teaching, it is permitted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Prayer
B) Fasting
C) Reciting a verse with tilawah intention
D) Reading books of fiqh

Key Takeaway
The eight prohibitions during hayd and nifas are not absolute; intention (tilawah vs. dhikr) and necessity can lift the prohibition for recitation, touching the Mushaf, and entering the mosque.

Prohibitions During Hayd and Nifas and Ruling on Cessation
Defines nifas and istihadah, lists eight prohibitions, and rules on blood cessation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the eight prohibitions during hayd and nifas and apply the Hanafi ruling for the permissibility of intercourse after blood cessation.

Core Idea
Eight acts are absolutely prohibited during menstruation and postpartum bleeding; intercourse permissibility depends on whether bleeding stops at the maximum, at the habit, or before the habit.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi rulings on what becomes prohibited during a woman's menstrual and postpartum bleeding. You will learn the eight specific prohibitions and the detailed conditions under which intercourse becomes permissible after the bleeding ceases. Understanding these rulings is essential for applying the correct fiqh in daily life.

Guided Path
1
Identify the eight prohibited acts
List the acts from the text: prayer, fasting, reciting Quran even one verse, touching Quran without wrapper, entering mosque, tawaf, intercourse, and seeking pleasure between navel and knee. Each is haram during hayd and nifas.
Memorize these eight; they are foundational.
2
Understand the definitions
Distinguish nifas (postpartum bleeding, max 40 days, no min) from istihadah (irregular bleeding outside hayd limits). Know the minimum purity period (15 days) between cycles.
Definitions affect the application of prohibitions.
3
Analyze cessation scenarios
Three cases: (1) blood stops at maximum (10 days hayd, 40 days nifas) → intercourse halal immediately without ghusl; (2) stops at habit but before maximum → halal after ghusl or passage of a full prayer time; (3) stops before habit → must wait until habit passes, even with ghusl.
The ruling is nuanced; cessation alone does not always permit intercourse.
4
Apply to examples
Given a woman's habit and day of cessation, determine when intercourse becomes permissible. Use the three scenarios to decide.
Practice with varied habits to solidify.
