⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة
٥٣
ما يحرم بالحيض والنفاس
والنفاس: هو الدم الخارج عقب الولادة، وأكثره أربعون يوماً، ولا حد لأقله. والاستحاضة دم نقص عن ثلاثة أيام أو زاد على عشرة في الحيض، وعلى أربعين في النفاس، وأقل الطهر الفاصل بين الحيضتين خمسة عشر يوماً، ولا حد لأكثره إلا أو بين الحيض والنفاس
لمن بلغت مستحاضة.
ما يحرم بالحيض والنفاس]
ويحرم بالحيض والنفاس ثمانية أشياء: الصلاة والصوم وقراءة آية من القرآن،
ومسها إلا بغلاف ودخول مسجد .
متجاف عن القرآن
عقب الولادة: ينبغي أن يزاد في التعريف فيقال: "عقب الولادة من الفرج؛ فإنها لو ولدت من قبل سُرتها فانشقت بأن كان ببطنها جرح وخرج الولد منها، تكون صاحبة جرح سائل لا نفساء. [حاشية الشلبي على تبيين الحقائق: ١٨٦/١] لمن بلغت إلخ أي بأن ابتدأت مع البلوغ مستحاضة فيقدر حيضها بعشرة، وطهرها بخمسة عشر يوماً، ونفاسها بأربعين والصوم: لا يقال: كان ينبغي أن يجوز الصوم مع الحيض كما يجوز مع الجنابة؛ لأنا نقول: الكف عن المفطرات الثلاثة في الجنابة موجود، فيجوز الصوم، وفي الحيض الكف عنها لأجل الصوم لا يوجد؛ لأن الكف عن الجماع لأجل الحيض لا لأجل الصوم، فلهذا لا يجوز صومها. [حاشية الشلبي: ١٦١/١] وقراءة إلخ: هذا إذا قرأه على قصد التلاوة، أما إذا قرأه على قصد الذكر والثناء نحو: بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم أو الحمد لله رب العالمين، أو علم القرآن حرفا حرفا، فلا بأس به بالاتفاق؛ لأجل العذر ، ذكر في "المحيط". [تبيين الحقائق: ١٦٥/١] ومسها إلا بغلاف: ويستثنى منه موضع الضرورة؛ لخوف حرق المصحف، أو غرقه، ويحرم ولو كتبه بالفارسية إجماعا. فروع ويكره بالكم تحريماً، ويرخص لأهل كتب الشريعة أخذها بالكم وباليد؛ للضرورة إلا التفسير؛ فإنه يجب الوضوء لمسه والمستحب أن لا يأخذها إلا بوضوء، ويجوز تقليب أوراق المصحف بنحو قلم للقراءة، ولا يجوز لف شيء في كاغذ كتب فيه فقه أو اسم الله تعالى أو النبي ، ونهي عن محو اسم الله تعالى بالبزاق، ومثله النبي تعظيما، ويستر المصحف لوطء زوجته ،استحياء، ولا يرمي براية قلم ولا حشيش المسجد في محل ممتهن. [مراقي الفلاح: ١٤٣] ودخول مسجد: شمل الكعبة دون مصلى عيد وجنازة في الأصح، وقيد المنع في "الدرر" بأن لا يكون ثمة ضرورة، فإن كانت كأن يكون باب البيت إلى المسجد، فلا ، قال في "البحر": وينبغي أن يقيد بأن لا يمكن =

كتاب الطهارة
ما يحرم بالحيض والنفاس
والطواف، والجماع، والاستمتاع بما تحت السُّرَّة إلى تحت الركبة، وإذا انقطع الدم لأكثر الحيض والنفاس، حل الوطء بلا غسل، ولا يحل إن انقطع لدونه.........
تحويل الباب ولا السكنى في غيره، وإلا لم يتحقق الضرورة، ولو أجنب فيه تيمم وخرج من ساعته إن لم يقدر على استعمال الماء، وكذا لو دخله وهو جنب ناسيا ثم ذكر وإن خرج مسرعا من غير تيمم جاز، وإن لم يقدر
،
على الخروج تيمم ولبث فيه ولا يجوز لبثه بدونه إلا أنه لا يصلي ولا يقرأ [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٤٤] والطواف أي ويحرم بهما الطواف بالكعبة ولو نفلا وإن صح مراقي الفلاح: ١٤٥ وحاشية الطحطاوي] والجماع: أي ويحرم بالحيض والنفاس الجماع والاستمتاع إلخ. مراقي الفلاح (١٤٥] أفاد أن السرة وما فوقها يحل الاستمتاع به بوطء أو غيره ولو بلا حائل وكذا بما بين السرة والركبة بحائل بغير الوطء ولو تلطخ دما، والمحرم هو المباشرة والمس ولو بدون شهوة. [ حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٤٥] وإذا انقطع إلخ حاصله : إما أن ينقطع لتمام العشرة، أو دونها لتمام العادة، أو دونها، ففي الأول: يحل وطؤها بمجرد الانقطاع، وفي الثالث : لا يقربها وإن اغتسلت ما لم تمض عادتها وفي الثاني : إن اغتسلت أو مضى عليها وقت صلاة، يعني خرج وقت الصلاة حتى صارت دينا في ذمتها ،حل، وإلا لا، وعلى هذا التفصيل انقطاع النفاس، إن كان لها عادة فيها فانقطع دونها لا يقربها، حتى تمضي عادتها بالشرط أو لتمامها حلّ إذا خرج الوقت الذي طهرت فيه، أو لتمام الأربعين حل مطلقاً [فتح القدير: ١٥٠/١] . اعلم أن الانقطاع في مسألة المتن ليس بشرط، بل خرج مخرج العادة أو للمقابلة. مع. ما بعده، حتى لو لم ينقطع فالحكم كذلك. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٤٦] بلا غسل ويستحب له أن لا يقربها قبل الاغتسال؛ لأن الحائض بعد عشرة أيام كالتي صارت جنباً، والحكم فيها هكذا. [حاشية الشلبي على تبيين الحقائق: ١٦٧/١] ولا يحل إن انقطع إلخ أي لا يحل الوطء إن انقطع الحيض والنفاس عن المسلمة لدون الأكثر لتمام عادتها إلا بأحد ثلاثة أشياء فصلها بقوله: "أن تغتسل" إلخ، ومعنى قوله: "لتمام عادتها أي إن انقطع الدم على ما كانت عادتها لا أقل منها مثلا مسلمة كانت عادتها في الحيض خمسة أيام وفي النفاس ثلاثين يوما، فانقطع الدم بعد خمسة أيام في الحيض وبعد ثلاثين في النفاس، لا يحل له وطؤها إلا بأحد الأشياء المذكورة بعد.
وقيدنا بقولنا: "مسلمة ، احترازاً عن النصرانية، فإن وطئها يحل بنفس الانقطاع قبيل العشرة؛ لأنه لا ينتظر في حقها أمارة زائدة ولا يتغير بإسلامها بعده؛ لأنا حكمنا بخروجها من الحيض، واحترز بقوله: "لدونه" الأكثر عما انقطع للأكثر ، فحكمه ما بينه بقوله : "وإذا انقطع إلخ"، وبقوله: "التمام عادتها فإنه إذا انقطع لدون عادتها كما إذا انقطع الدم في الصورة المذكورة لأقل خمسة أيام في الحيض ومن ثلاثين يوماً في النفاس، وقد تجاوز دم الحيض ثلاثة أيام، لا يقربها وإن اغتسلت حتى تمضي ،عادتها، ولكنها تصلي وتصوم احتياطاً.
من
Book of Purification. 53. What is prohibited during menstruation and postpartum bleeding. And postpartum bleeding: it is the blood that emerges directly after childbirth, its maximum is forty days, and there is no limit for its minimum. And istihadah is blood that is less than three days or exceeds ten days in menstruation, and forty in postpartum bleeding. And the minimum purity separating two menstruations is fifteen days, and there is no limit for its maximum except that between menstruation and postpartum bleeding for a woman who began istihadah at puberty. What is prohibited during menstruation and postpartum bleeding: And eight things are prohibited during menstruation and postpartum bleeding: prayer, fasting, reciting even one verse of the Quran, and touching it except with a wrapper, and entering a mosque. Avoiding the Quran. 'Directly after childbirth': it is appropriate to add to the definition and say: 'directly after childbirth from the vagina; for if she gave birth from her navel area by splitting because of a wound in her belly and the child emerged, she is a woman with a flowing wound, not in postpartum bleeding.' [Hashiyat al-Shalabi on Tabayin al-Haqa'iq: 1/186] 'For one who began at puberty etc.' i.e., if she began at puberty as a mustahadah, then her menstrual period is estimated at ten days, and her purity at fifteen days, and her postpartum bleeding at forty. And fasting: it is not said that it should be permissible to fast during menstruation just as it is permissible during major impurity; for we say: refraining from the three nullifiers exists in major impurity, so fasting is permissible, but during menstruation, refraining from them for the sake of fasting does not exist, because refraining from intercourse is due to menstruation, not for the sake of fasting, therefore her fasting is not valid. [Hashiyat al-Shalabi: 1/161] And recitation etc.: this is if she recites with the intention of tilawah; if she recites with the intention of dhikr and praise, like 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' or 'Alhamdu lillahi Rabb al-'Alamin', or she teaches the Quran letter by letter, then there is no harm by consensus, due to necessity, mentioned in 'al-Muhit'. [Tabayin al-Haqa'iq: 1/165] And touching it except with a wrapper: an exception is made for cases of necessity, such as fear of burning the Quran or drowning, and it is prohibited even if written in Persian by consensus. Branches: It is prohibitively disliked to touch with the sleeve, and it is permitted for people of the religious sciences to take it with the sleeve and with the hand due to necessity, except for Tafsir; for it is obligatory to have wudu to touch it, and it is recommended not to take it except with wudu. It is permissible to turn pages of the Quran with something like a pen for reading. It is not permissible to wrap anything in paper in which fiqh or the name of Allah or the Prophet is written. And it is forbidden to erase the name of Allah with spittle, and similarly the Prophet out of reverence. The Quran should be covered when having intercourse with one's wife out of modesty. One should not throw a pen shaving or mosque grass in a contemptuous place. [Maraqi al-Falah: 143] And entering a mosque: includes the Kaaba but not the Eid or funeral prayer place according to the most correct view. The prohibition is restricted in 'al-Durar' to cases where there is no necessity. If there is necessity, like the door of the house facing the mosque, then it is not prohibited. al-Bahr said: it should be restricted to when it is not possible to relocate the door or live elsewhere, otherwise the necessity is not realized. If he becomes junub in it, he performs tayammum and exits immediately if unable to use water. Similarly, if he entered it while junub forgetfully then remembered; if he exits quickly without tayammum, it is permissible. If he cannot exit, he performs tayammum and stays, and it is not permissible to stay without it, except that he does not pray or recite. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 144] And tawaf: i.e., tawaf around the Kaaba is also prohibited by them, even if voluntary, as stated in Maraqi al-Falah: 145 and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi. And intercourse: i.e., intercourse and pleasure etc. are prohibited during menstruation and postpartum bleeding. Maraqi al-Falah (145:1] It indicates that the area above the navel is permissible to enjoy by intercourse or otherwise even without a barrier, and similarly what is between the navel and knee with a barrier without intercourse, even if stained with blood. The prohibition is for direct contact and touching, even without desire. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 145] And regardless of cessation etc. Its summary: either it stops at the completion of ten days, or before it at the completion of the habit, or before that. In the first: intercourse is permitted immediately upon cessation. In the third: he does not approach her even if she performs ghusl until her habit passes. In the second: if she performs ghusl or a prayer time passes over her, meaning the time of prayer exits so that it becomes a debt on her, then it is permissible, otherwise not. And this detailing applies to the cessation of postpartum bleeding. If she has a habit in it and it stops before it, he does not approach her until her habit passes with the condition, or at its completion it is permissible if the time in which she became pure exits, or at the completion of forty it is permissible absolutely. [Fath al-Qadir: 1/150] Know that cessation in the issue of the text is not a condition, rather it is mentioned as a customary expression or for comparison, so that even if it does not stop, the ruling is the same. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 146] Without ghusl: and it is recommended that he does not approach her before ghusl, because the menstruating woman after ten days is like one who became junub, and the ruling is the same. [Hashiyat al-Shalabi on Tabayin al-Haqa'iq: 1/167] And it is not permissible if it stops etc. i.e., intercourse is not permissible if menstruation or postpartum bleeding stops for less than the maximum at the completion of her habit, except by one of three things detailed in his statement: 'that she performs ghusl' etc. And the meaning of his statement 'at the completion of her habit' is that if the blood stops at what was her habit, not less than it; for example, a Muslim woman whose habit in menstruation was five days and in postpartum bleeding thirty days, and the blood stops after five days in menstruation and after thirty in postpartum bleeding, it is not permissible for him to have intercourse with her except by one of the things mentioned later. And we restricted with our statement 'Muslim woman' to exclude a Christian woman, for intercourse with her is permissible upon mere cessation before the tenth day, because we do not wait for an additional sign in her case, and it does not change by her Islam afterwards, because we rule that she has left menstruation. And he restricted with his statement 'less than the maximum' that which stops at the maximum, for its ruling is as he explained in 'and if it stops etc.', and with his statement 'at the completion of her habit' that if it stops before her habit, as if the blood stops in the mentioned scenario at less than five days in menstruation and thirty days in postpartum bleeding, and the menstrual blood has exceeded three days, he does not approach her even if she performs ghusl until her habit passes, but she prays and fasts as a precaution. from
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_statement from the Hanafi school covering two topics: the definitions of nifas and istihadah, and the eight things prohibited during hayd and nifas, along with the rules for when bleeding ceases. The author begins by defining nifas as blood that comes out directly after childbirth, with a maximum of forty days and no minimum. Istihadah is defined as bleeding that is either less than three days or exceeds ten days for hayd, or forty for nifas. The minimum purity between two menstrual cycles is fifteen days, with no maximum except the transition between hayd and nifas. The eight prohibitions are then listed: prayer, fasting, reciting any verse of the Quran, touching the Quran except with a wrapper, entering a mosque, tawaf, intercourse, and seeking pleasure from the area between the navel and knee. The commentary expands on each: for example, fasting is invalid during hayd because while a junub person refrains from nullifiers voluntarily, a menstruating woman refrains from intercourse due to the state, not for the sake of fasting. Recitation is prohibited only with the intention of tilawah; incidental dhikr is allowed. Touching the Quran is forbidden except with a wrapper, with exceptions for necessity. Entering a mosque is prohibited unless there is a legitimate excuse, like the house door opening into the mosque. Tawaf is prohibited even if voluntary. Intercourse and direct touching between navel and knee are prohibited; above navel is allowed. The cessation ruling is detailed: if blood stops at the maximum (10 days for hayd, 40 for nifas), intercourse is permissible immediately without ghusl. If it stops before the maximum but at the completion of the usual habit, it becomes permissible if she performs ghusl or a full prayer time passes. If it stops before the habit, she must wait until the habit passes, and intercourse remains prohibited even after ghusl until then. The text also notes that a non-Muslim woman (e.g., Christian) is treated differently; her hayd ends upon cessation even before ten days, as no further sign is expected. The passage concludes by emphasizing that cessation is not a condition; even if bleeding continues, the same rules apply if it reaches the relevant threshold.

Key Terms
النفاس (al-nifas): Blood that emerges directly after childbirth, with a maximum of forty days and no defined minimum.
الاستحاضة (al-istihadah): Irregular bleeding that is either less than three days or exceeds ten (for hayd) or forty (for nifas), considered a chronic excuse.
الطهر (al-tuhr): The period of purity between two menstrual cycles, with a minimum of fifteen days.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if a woman’s hayd blood stops after completing her usual number of days but before reaching 10 days, when does intercourse become permissible?
A) Immediately upon cessation
B) Only after she performs ghusl or a full prayer time passes
C) Not until the 10th day
D) Not until she completes an additional 3 days of purity

Key Takeaway
Eight acts are haram during hayd and nifas; intercourse after cessation depends on whether bleeding stops at the maximum, at the habit, or before the habit.

Prohibitions During Hayd and Nifas and the Ruling on Cessation at Maximum Duration
States the prohibitions and the cessation ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three prohibitions during hayd and nifas and apply the Hanafi ruling on when intercourse becomes permissible after bleeding stops.

Core Idea
Three acts are forbidden during hayd/nifas: tawaf, intercourse, and direct touching between navel and knee.

This passage from Nur al-Idah lays out the core prohibitions that apply to a woman during menstruation (hayd) and postnatal bleeding (nifas). It also clarifies the precise ruling on when sexual intercourse becomes permissible after the bleeding ceases, distinguishing between cessation at the maximum duration and earlier cessation. Understanding these rulings is essential for maintaining proper ritual purity and avoiding unlawful acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prohibitions
List the three things forbidden during hayd/nifas: tawaf of the Kaaba, sexual intercourse, and physical enjoyment (touching) between the navel and knee without a barrier.
The commentary adds that touching above the navel is permissible even without a barrier.
2
Understand the scope of the prohibition on touching
The prohibition is on direct skin contact between the navel and knee. Areas above the navel are permissible without a barrier. Between the navel and knee, touching is allowed only with a barrier (excluding intercourse).
This distinction comes from the commentary of Maraqi al-Falah.
3
Distinguish the ruling on cessation at maximum vs. less than maximum
If the bleeding stops at the maximum duration (10 days for hayd, 40 days for nifas), intercourse becomes permissible without the need for ghusl. If it stops before the maximum, it remains forbidden.
The text explicitly says 'without ghusl' meaning that at the maximum, the woman is considered pure even without a bath.
4
Note the condition of ghusl
At maximum cessation, ghusl is not required for permissibility of intercourse, though it is still recommended for prayer and other acts of worship.
This is a unique Hanafi ruling; other schools may require ghusl.

كتاب الطهارة
ما يحرم بالحيض والنفاس
والطواف، والجماع، والاستمتاع بما تحت السُّرَّة إلى تحت الركبة، وإذا انقطع الدم لأكثر الحيض والنفاس، حل الوطء بلا غسل، ولا يحل إن انقطع لدونه.........
تحويل الباب ولا السكنى في غيره، وإلا لم يتحقق الضرورة، ولو أجنب فيه تيمم وخرج من ساعته إن لم يقدر على استعمال الماء، وكذا لو دخله وهو جنب ناسيا ثم ذكر وإن خرج مسرعا من غير تيمم جاز، وإن لم يقدر
على الخروج تيمم ولبث فيه ولا يجوز لبثه بدونه إلا أنه لا يصلي ولا يقرأ [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٤٤] والطواف أي ويحرم بهما الطواف بالكعبة ولو نفلا وإن صح مراقي الفلاح: ١٤٥ وحاشية الطحطاوي] والجماع: أي ويحرم بالحيض والنفاس الجماع والاستمتاع إلخ. مراقي الفلاح (١٤٥] أفاد أن السرة وما فوقها يحل الاستمتاع به بوطء أو غيره ولو بلا حائل وكذا بما بين السرة والركبة بحائل بغير الوطء ولو تلطخ دما، والمحرم هو المباشرة والمس ولو بدون شهوة. [ حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٤٥]
Chapter on Purity. What is forbidden due to hayd and nifas: Tawaf, sexual intercourse, and enjoyment of what is between the navel and the knee. And if the blood stops at the maximum of hayd and nifas, intercourse becomes permissible without ghusl, and it is not permissible if it stops at less than that. ... Tawaf: meaning both forbid tawaf around the Kaaba even if supererogatory. Intercourse: meaning hayd and nifas forbid intercourse and enjoyment etc. Maraqi al-Falah (145) indicates that what is above the navel is permissible to enjoy by intercourse or otherwise even without a barrier, and likewise what is between the navel and knee with a barrier other than intercourse, even if smeared with blood. What is forbidden is direct contact and touching even without desire.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the section on what is forbidden during hayd and nifas. It begins by stating the ruling as a memorization anchor: three things are forbidden – tawaf of the Kaaba, sexual intercourse, and direct touching between the navel and knee. The commentary from Maraqi al-Falah clarifies that enjoyment of what is above the navel is permissible even without a barrier, and what is between the navel and knee is permissible with a barrier (excluding intercourse). The prohibition is on direct skin contact even if there is no sexual desire. The matn then states the basic ruling on cessation: if the bleeding stops at the maximum duration (10 days for hayd, 40 for nifas), intercourse becomes halal without the need for ghusl; but if it stops at less than the maximum, it remains forbidden. The intrusive text 'تحويل الباب' appears to be a misplaced note from another topic (possibly about the mosque or ritual impurity) and should be disregarded in this lesson.

Key Terms
حيض (hayd): Menstrual bleeding that occurs in a healthy woman, with a minimum of 3 days and maximum of 10 days.
نفاس (nifas): Postnatal bleeding after childbirth, with a maximum of 40 days; no minimum.
طواف (tawaf): Circumambulation of the Kaaba, which is forbidden for a woman in hayd or nifas, even if supererogatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is forbidden for a woman during hayd or nifas according to this passage?
A) Tawaf, intercourse, and touching above the navel without barrier
B) Tawaf, intercourse, and touching between navel and knee without barrier
C) Only intercourse
D) Tawaf and reciting Quran

Key Takeaway
Three acts are absolutely forbidden during hayd/nifas: tawaf, intercourse, and direct touching between navel and knee; intercourse becomes permissible only when bleeding stops at the maximum duration (10 days for hayd, 40 for nifas), and purification (ghusl) is not required at that point.

The Three Cases of Cessation of Menstrual Bleeding
Explains the three cases of cessation of menstruation and nifas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three cases of cessation of menstrual bleeding and apply the ruling for each case to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Three scenarios of cessation determine when intercourse is permissible immediately, with conditions, or after habit.

This lesson unpacks the matn's phrase 'and if it stops' by breaking it into three distinct cases based on when the bleeding stops relative to the maximum and the woman's habit. Understanding these cases is essential for correctly applying the rules of purification and permissible marital relations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three termination points
The text states that cessation can occur at the maximum (10 days hayd, 40 days nifas), at the completion of the woman's habit, or before the habit. Identify each termination point.
2
State the ruling for each case
For cessation at maximum: immediate halal. For cessation at habit: halal only if she performs ghusl/tayammum and prays, or a prayer time passes. For cessation before habit: no approach until habit ends, even after ghusl.
The third case applies even if she performs ghusl.
3
Apply to nifas
The same three-case structure applies to postpartum bleeding, with the maximum of 40 days.
4
Check the exception for non-Muslim women
The text restricts the ruling to Muslim women; for a Christian woman, immediate halal upon cessation before maximum, because no habit is considered.
This exception is found in the later elaboration.

وإذا انقطع إلخ حاصله : إما أن ينقطع لتمام العشرة، أو دونها لتمام العادة، أو دونها، ففي الأول: يحل وطؤها بمجرد الانقطاع، وفي الثالث : لا يقربها وإن اغتسلت ما لم تمض عادتها وفي الثاني : إن اغتسلت أو مضى عليها وقت صلاة، يعني خرج وقت الصلاة حتى صارت دينا في ذمتها ،حل، وإلا لا، وعلى هذا التفصيل انقطاع النفاس، إن كان لها عادة فيها فانقطع دونها لا يقربها، حتى تمضي عادتها بالشرط أو لتمامها حلّ إذا خرج الوقت الذي طهرت فيه، أو لتمام الأربعين حل مطلقاً [فتح القدير: ١٥٠/١] . اعلم أن الانقطاع في مسألة المتن ليس بشرط، بل خرج مخرج العادة أو للمقابلة. مع. ما بعده، حتى لو لم ينقطع فالحكم كذلك. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٤٦] بلا غسل ويستحب له أن لا يقربها قبل الاغتسال؛ لأن الحائض بعد عشرة أيام كالتي صارت جنباً، والحكم فيها هكذا. [حاشية الشلبي على تبيين الحقائق: ١٦٧/١] ولا يحل إن انقطع إلخ أي لا يحل الوطء إن انقطع الحيض والنفاس عن المسلمة لدون الأكثر لتمام عادتها إلا بأحد ثلاثة أشياء فصلها بقوله: "أن تغتسل" إلخ، ومعنى قوله: "لتمام عادتها أي إن انقطع الدم على ما كانت عادتها لا أقل منها مثلا مسلمة كانت عادتها في الحيض خمسة أيام وفي النفاس ثلاثين يوما، فانقطع الدم بعد خمسة أيام في الحيض وبعد ثلاثين في النفاس، لا يحل له وطؤها إلا بأحد الأشياء المذكورة بعد.
وقيدنا بقولنا: "مسلمة ، احترازاً عن النصرانية، فإن وطئها يحل بنفس الانقطاع قبيل العشرة؛ لأنه لا ينتظر في حقها أمارة زائدة ولا يتغير بإسلامها بعده؛ لأنا حكمنا بخروجها من الحيض، واحترز بقوله: "لدونه" الأكثر عما انقطع للأكثر ، فحكمه ما بينه بقوله : "وإذا انقطع إلخ"، وبقوله: "التمام عادتها فإنه إذا انقطع لدون عادتها كما إذا انقطع الدم في الصورة المذكورة لأقل خمسة أيام في الحيض ومن ثلاثين يوماً في النفاس، وقد تجاوز دم الحيض ثلاثة أيام، لا يقربها وإن اغتسلت حتى تمضي ،عادتها، ولكنها تصلي وتصوم احتياطاً.
من

كتاب الطهارة
٥٥
ما يحرم بالجناية والحدث
لتمام عادتها إلا أن تغتسل أو تتيمم وتصلي، أو تصير الصلاة دينا في ذمتها، وذلك بأن تجد
بعد الانقطاع من الوقت الذي انقطع الدم فيه زمنا يسع الغسل والتحريمة فما فوقهما،
لتمام عادتها
الجملة نعت لقوله: زمنا
و لم تغتسل، ولم تتيمّم حتى خرج الوقت وتقضي الحائض والنفساء الصوم دون الصلاة.
ما يحرم بالجنابة ]
وعليه الإجماع
ويحرم بالجنابة خمسة أشياء: الصلاة، وقراءة آية

من
ذلك لا يجزيها صوم
من
بأن
أو تتيمم لعذر من الأعذار المبيحة للتيمم. الوقت إلخ : أطلقه وهو مقيد بالوقت الذي هو من ا الأوقات الخمس؛ فإنه إذا انقطع في وقت الضحى، ولم تغتسل بعده ولم تتيمم لا يحل وطؤها حتى يخرج وقت الظهر؛ لتثبت صلاته في ذمتها بخروجه؛ لأن ما قبل الزوال وقت مهمل لا عبرة بخروجه وكذا إذا انقطع قبيل طلوع الشمس بأقل من الغسل والتحريمة لا يحل وطؤها حتى يخرج وقت الظهر. [ حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٤٧] زمنا يسع الغسل : فلا تجب الصلاة في ذمتها ما لم تدرك قدر ذلك من الوقت، ولهذا لو طهرت قبيل الصبح بأقل ذلك اليوم، ولا يجب عليها صلاة العشاء، فكأنها أصبحت وهي حائض، ويجب عليها الإمساك تشبها تبيين الحقائق: ۱۷۰/۱] حتى خرج الوقت فبمجرد خروج الوقت يحل وطؤها؛ لترتب صلاة ذلك الوقت في ذمتها، وهو حكم من أحكام الطهارات. [مراقي الفلاح: ١٤٧] وتقضي الخ: أي الحائض والنفساء تقضيان الصوم لزوما دون الصلاة فإن قيل إنها غير مخاطبة بالصوم حال حيضها؛ لحرمته، فكيف يجب عليها القضاء و لم يجب عليها الأداء؟ قلنا: أما قال مشايخنا وغيرهم من القضاء يجب بأمر جديد فلا إشكال على قولهم ، وأما على قول الجمهور من مشايخنا أن القضاء يجب بما يجب به الأداء، فانعقاد السبب يكفي لوجوب القضاء وإن لم تخاطب بالأداء. [البحر الرائق: ٣٩٩/١]
The gist of 'and if it stops etc.' is that it either stops at the completion of ten [days], or at the completion of her habit, or less than that. In the first, intercourse becomes permissible immediately upon cessation. In the third, he should not approach her even if she has performed ghusl until her habit passes. In the second, if she performs ghusl or a prayer time passes over her, meaning the prayer time exits so that prayer becomes a debt upon her, it becomes permissible; otherwise not. And upon this detail is the cessation of nifas: if she has a habit and it stops before it, he should not approach her until her habit passes with the condition, or at its completion it becomes permissible if the time in which she became pure exits, or at the completion of forty [days] it becomes permissible unconditionally. Know that cessation in the matn's question is not a condition, but rather came out in the way of habit or for comparison, with what follows, such that even if it did not stop, the ruling is likewise. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi 146] 'without ghusl' and it is recommended that he not approach her before ghusl, because the menstruating woman after ten days is like one who became junub, and the ruling for her is thus. [Hashiyah al-Shalabi 167/1] And 'it is not permissible if it stops etc.' means that intercourse is not permissible if hayd or nifas stops for a Muslim woman at less than the maximum for completion of her habit except with one of three things detailed by his statement 'that she performs ghusl' etc. And the meaning of 'for completion of her habit' is that the blood stops according to what her habit was, not less than it. For example, a Muslim woman whose habit in hayd is five days and in nifas thirty days; if the blood stops after five days in hayd and after thirty in nifas, intercourse is not permissible except with one of the mentioned things. And we restricted by our statement 'Muslim' to exclude a Christian woman, for intercourse with her becomes permissible by the mere cessation before the maximum [of ten days] because no additional indication is expected in her case, and it does not change by her subsequent Islam, for we rule that she has exited hayd. And he restricted by his statement 'less than the maximum' that which stops at the maximum, whose ruling is indicated by his statement 'and if it stops etc.', and by his statement 'the completion of her habit' that if it stops at less than her habit, as in the mentioned example of less than five days in hayd and less than thirty in nifas, and the bleeding has exceeded three days, he should not approach her even if she performs ghusl until her habit passes, but she prays and fasts as a precaution. For completion of her habit unless she performs ghusl or tayammum and prays, or prayer becomes a debt upon her, and that is by her finding after cessation, from the time in which the blood stopped, a period sufficient for ghusl and the opening takbir and beyond, for completion of her habit. The phrase is an adjective for 'a period'. And she did not perform ghusl or tayammum until the time exited. And the menstruating woman and the woman in nifas make up the fast [only] not the prayer. What is forbidden due to janabah. And there is consensus upon it. And due to janabah five things are forbidden: prayer, reciting a verse ... that does not suffice her fast ... or tayammum for a valid excuse from the excuses that permit tayammum. The time etc.: he released it and it is restricted to the time that is among the five times; if it stops at the time of Duha and she did not perform ghusl or tayammum after it, intercourse is not permissible until the time of Zuhr exits, to establish her prayer in her liability by its exit, because the time before zawal is neglected, its exit is of no consequence. Similarly if it stops before sunrise with less than [time for] ghusl and takbir, intercourse is not permissible until the time of Zuhr exits. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi 147] A period sufficient for ghusl: prayer does not become incumbent upon her unless she reached that amount of time, and hence if she becomes pure before Fajr with less than that day, the Isha prayer is not obligatory upon her, as if she started the day as menstruating, and she must refrain as a likeness. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 170/1] Until the time exits, then immediately upon exit intercourse becomes permissible, because the prayer of that time is established as a debt upon her, and this is a ruling from the rulings of purifications. [Maraqi al-Falah 147] And 'she makes up' etc.: meaning the menstruating woman and the woman in nifas necessarily make up the fast but not the prayer. If it is said that she was not addressed to fast during her hayd due to its prohibition, so how is she required to make up while she was not required to perform? We say: as our scholars and others said that making up is required by a new command, so there is no difficulty on their view. And on the view of the majority of our scholars that making up is required by the same requirement as performance, the occurrence of the cause suffices for the requirement of making up even if she was not addressed to perform. [Bahr al-Ra'iq 399/1]
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This is an expansion of the ruling on cessation of bleeding. The author of the commentary explains the matn's statement 'and if it stops etc.' by breaking it into three scenarios: (1) bleeding stops at the maximum (10 days hayd, 40 days nifas) – intercourse is permissible immediately; (2) bleeding stops at the woman's usual habit (e.g., 5 days) – intercourse is permissible only if she performs ghusl or tayammum and prays, or if a full prayer time passes without her doing so, making the prayer a debt on her; (3) bleeding stops before her habit – intercourse remains forbidden until her habit ends, even if she performs ghusl. The same three cases apply to nifas. Importantly, cessation of bleeding is not a condition itself; the ruling applies even if bleeding continues but the maximum or habit period ends. The commentary then discusses the detail of 'without ghusl' in the matn, noting that it is recommended not to approach her before ghusl because after ten days she is like a junub person. Next, it defines 'for completion of her habit' with an example, and it restricts the ruling to Muslim women – for a Christian woman, intercourse becomes permissible upon cessation before the maximum because her hayd has no additional signs. The commentary continues on page 56 elaborating the condition of 'passing of prayer time': the time must be one of the five obligatory prayer times, and she must have time enough to perform ghusl and the opening takbir. If she fails to do so before the time exits, the prayer becomes a debt, and intercourse becomes permissible. If she becomes pure very close to Fajr and there isn't enough time for ghusl, the night prayer (Isha) is not considered a debt. Finally, the passage addresses the rule that menstruating and postpartum women must make up missed fasts but not prayers, and provides a scholastic defense: the requirement of making up fasts is based on a new command (or the same cause), so the lack of original obligation does not preclude make-up.

Key Terms
عادة (adah): The usual duration of menstruation for a particular woman, used to determine permissibility of intercourse before maximum.
نفاس (nifas): Postpartum bleeding that has the same three-case structure as hayd, with maximum of 40 days.
غسل (ghusl): Ritual bath required to become pure from major impurity (janabah) and to permit intercourse after cessation.
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with earth as a substitute for ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which case is intercourse permissible immediately upon cessation without any further condition?
A) When bleeding stops at the woman's habit
B) When bleeding stops at the maximum of hayd or nifas
C) When bleeding stops at less than the habit
D) When bleeding stops at any time and she performs ghusl

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of intercourse after cessation depends on whether bleeding stops at the maximum, at the habit, or before the habit, each with distinct rules.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
Conditions for Permissibility of Intercourse and the Rule of Making Up Missed Fasts
Details the conditions for permissible intercourse after cessation at habit and the rule of qada

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the conditions that permit intercourse after cessation at the habit, and explain why menstruating women must make up fasts but not prayers.

Core Idea
A prayer time becoming a debt is one condition; make-up of fast is required by a new command, not the original obligation.

This lesson elaborates on the conditions that must be met for intercourse to be permissible when bleeding stops at the woman's habit, including the precise definition of 'passing of prayer time'. It also addresses the well-known rule that menstruating women make up missed fasts but not prayers, providing the scholastic justification.

Guided Path
1
List the three conditions from the matn
The text says intercourse is not permissible after cessation at the habit except with one of three things: ghusl/tayammum and prayer, or the passing of a prayer time making prayer a debt.
2
Define when prayer becomes a debt
A full prayer time must pass while she has enough time to perform ghusl and the opening takbir. If she fails to do so, the prayer becomes a debt.
The time must be one of the five obligatory prayer times; Duha (pre-noon) is negligible.
3
Understand the exceptions to the prayer time condition
If she becomes pure just before Fajr with less than enough time for ghusl, the Isha prayer does not become a debt because she had no opportunity.
Similarly, if she becomes pure in the Duha time, its exit does not count.
4
Explain the qada rule for fasts and prayers
Menstruating and postpartum women must make up fasts but not prayers. The text provides a scholastic defense: either by a new command (amr jadid) or by the same cause (sabab), though the original address was absent.

What is forbidden due to janabah. And there is consensus upon it. And due to janabah five things are forbidden: prayer, reciting a verse ... that does not suffice her fast ... or tayammum for a valid excuse from the excuses that permit tayammum. The time etc.: he released it and it is restricted to the time that is among the five times; if it stops at the time of Duha and she did not perform ghusl or tayammum after it, intercourse is not permissible until the time of Zuhr exits, to establish her prayer in her liability by its exit, because the time before zawal is neglected, its exit is of no consequence. Similarly if it stops before sunrise with less than [time for] ghusl and takbir, intercourse is not permissible until the time of Zuhr exits. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi 147] A period sufficient for ghusl: prayer does not become incumbent upon her unless she reached that amount of time, and hence if she becomes pure before Fajr with less than that day, the Isha prayer is not obligatory upon her, as if she started the day as menstruating, and she must refrain as a likeness. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 170/1] Until the time exits, then immediately upon exit intercourse becomes permissible, because the prayer of that time is established as a debt upon her, and this is a ruling from the rulings of purifications. [Maraqi al-Falah 147] And 'she makes up' etc.: meaning the menstruating woman and the woman in nifas necessarily make up the fast but not the prayer. If it is said that she was not addressed to fast during her hayd due to its prohibition, so how is she required to make up while she was not required to perform? We say: as our scholars and others said that making up is required by a new command, so there is no difficulty on their view. And on the view of the majority of our scholars that making up is required by the same requirement as performance, the occurrence of the cause suffices for the requirement of making up even if she was not addressed to perform. [Bahr al-Ra'iq 399/1]
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This is an expansion of the ruling on cessation of bleeding. The author of the commentary explains the matn's statement 'and if it stops etc.' by breaking it into three scenarios: (1) bleeding stops at the maximum (10 days hayd, 40 days nifas) – intercourse is permissible immediately; (2) bleeding stops at the woman's usual habit (e.g., 5 days) – intercourse is permissible only if she performs ghusl or tayammum and prays, or if a full prayer time passes without her doing so, making the prayer a debt on her; (3) bleeding stops before her habit – intercourse remains forbidden until her habit ends, even if she performs ghusl. The same three cases apply to nifas. Importantly, cessation of bleeding is not a condition itself; the ruling applies even if bleeding continues but the maximum or habit period ends. The commentary then discusses the detail of 'without ghusl' in the matn, noting that it is recommended not to approach her before ghusl because after ten days she is like a junub person. Next, it defines 'for completion of her habit' with an example, and it restricts the ruling to Muslim women – for a Christian woman, intercourse becomes permissible upon cessation before the maximum because her hayd has no additional signs. The commentary continues on page 56 elaborating the condition of 'passing of prayer time': the time must be one of the five obligatory prayer times, and she must have time enough to perform ghusl and the opening takbir. If she fails to do so before the time exits, the prayer becomes a debt, and intercourse becomes permissible. If she becomes pure very close to Fajr and there isn't enough time for ghusl, the night prayer (Isha) is not considered a debt. Finally, the passage addresses the rule that menstruating and postpartum women must make up missed fasts but not prayers, and provides a scholastic defense: the requirement of making up fasts is based on a new command (or the same cause), so the lack of original obligation does not preclude make-up.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed worship after its time. For menstruating women, make-up of fast is required, but not prayer.
غسل (ghusl): Ritual bath required to become pure; one of the conditions for permissibility of intercourse after cessation at habit.
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with earth as a substitute for ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
وقت صلاة (waqt salat): The period of an obligatory prayer. The passing of such a time, with opportunity for ghusl, makes the prayer a debt and permits intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What condition must be met for the 'passing of a prayer time' to make intercourse permissible?
A) Any time of day must pass
B) One of the five obligatory prayer times must pass while she had time to perform ghusl and the opening takbir
C) She must pray at least one rakah
D) She must fast that day

Key Takeaway
Intercourse after cessation at habit requires either ghusl with prayer or the passing of an obligatory prayer time, and menstruating women must make up fasts but not prayers due to a new command or the same cause.

Prohibitions for a Junub: The Dispute on Reciting Less Than a Verse
Intra-Hanafi dispute on reciting less than a verse in janabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi views on reciting less than a verse in janabah and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school is split: does a junub's recitation of less than a complete Quranic verse remain prohibited? The relied-upon view says yes.

This passage addresses the prohibitions for a person in janabah, focusing on the debated issue of reciting part of a Quranic verse (ma duna al-ayah). While the five prohibitions are listed briefly, the main content is the ikhtilaf among Hanafi scholars. Understanding the arguments and the preferred ruling is essential for correct practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling in dispute
What specific action is being contested? It is the recitation of less than a full verse of the Quran by a person in janabah. Does the prohibition of Quran recitation cover less than a verse?
2
State the two positions within the Hanafi school
One group (al-Karkhi, author of al-Hidayah, Qadi Khan, etc.) holds absolute prohibition. Another group (al-Khulasa, Fakhr al-Islam) permits it. Determine which scholars support each view.
Use the names cited in the passage.
3
Examine the dalil for each position
The prohibitionists rely on general ahadith forbidding Quran recitation for a junub without specifying quantity. The permissibility view uses analogy (qiyas) that only full recitation is prohibited.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the permissibility argument
The text states that reasoning (ta'lil) in the face of a clear text is rejected. The general ahadith are straightforward; they do not differentiate between full verse and part.
This is a key usul principle: 'al-amm yufidu al-wujub' or here 'al-amm yufidu al-tahrim'.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi ruling
The author of Bahr al-Ra'iq prefers prohibition. This is the operative view for fatwa.
Always check the later Hanafi master's tarjih.

And among them are those who permitted less than a verse, authenticated by the author of al-Khulasa, and adopted by Fakhr al-Islam in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir, and attributed by al-Zahidi to the majority. And the opinion that should be preferred is prohibition, because the ahadith did not differentiate, and reasoning in the face of a text is rejected. [Bahr al-Ra'iq 409/1]
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage begins by stating the five prohibitions for a person in janabah (ritual impurity due to sexual intercourse or wet dream): prayer, reciting Quran (even a verse or less, with ikhtilaf), and other things that are not fully listed here due to OCR corruption. The text then repeatedly digresses into the previous lesson's discussion about cessation of hayd and nifas, likely due to the marginal commentary or page misalignment. The core fiqh point in this section is the dispute about reciting less than a verse of the Quran. The Hanafi position divides into two views: one group (including al-Karkhi, the author of al-Hidayah, Qadi Khan) holds that it is completely prohibited to recite any part of the Quran, even less than a verse, while in janabah. Another group (including the author of al-Khulasa, Fakhr al-Islam) permits reciting less than a verse. The relied-upon view (al-mu'tamad) is the prohibition, because the prophetic ahadith that forbid recitation for a junub do not distinguish between a full verse and less, and analogy ('illa) cannot override a textual proof. This is a classic example of the Hanafi principle that a general text remains general unless specified.

Key Terms
جنابة (janabah): State of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl, caused by sexual intercourse or orgasm.
ما دون الآية (ma duna al-ayah): Less than a full verse of the Quran, e.g., a few words or letters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Recommended

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi prohibits reciting any part of the Quran while in janabah, because the general ahadith forbid recitation without distinguishing between a full verse and less.

Qada of Fasts, Not Prayers, for Delayed Ghusl after Menses
Ruling and commentary on qada of fast but not prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qada for a woman whose menses ends and who delays ghusl, and identify the condition that determines when prayer becomes a debt in her liability.

Core Idea
A woman delaying ghusl after menses owes qada of fasts, not prayers; prayer becomes a debt only if she had time to purify.

This passage from Nur al-Idah and its commentaries clarifies a common scenario: a menstruating or postpartum woman becomes pure but delays ghusl or tayammum until after the prayer time exits. The ruling distinguishes between fasting and prayer obligations, and hinges on whether she had sufficient time to perform purification and the opening takbir within the prayer time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The passage states: 'The menstruating woman and the postpartum woman make up the fast but not the prayer.' Note this as the primary legal conclusion.
2
Determine the condition for prayer becoming a debt
Look for the condition that makes the prayer a 'debt in her liability' (dayn fi al-dhimmah). The text says this occurs if after cessation of blood she has enough time to perform ghusl and the opening takbir (and more) before the time exits, but she does not purify.
The minimum time is the duration needed for ghusl and takbirat al-ihram.
3
Understand the implication of insufficient time
If she does not have that minimal time (e.g., her menses ends just before dawn with less time than required for ghusl and takbir), the prayer does not become obligatory, and she does not need to make it up. She still must make up the fast of that day.
The fast of the day is wajib even if she was not required to pray that day.
4
Examine the rationale for qada of fast but not prayer
The passage provides two explanations: (1) Some Hanafi scholars say qada of fast is by a new command (amr jadid), so there is no conflict. (2) The majority hold that the cause (turuq al-sabab) suffices for qada even if performance was not addressed during hayd. For prayer, the absence of sufficient time means no liability arises.
The ikhtilaf is on rationale, not on the ruling itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

To complete her normal menstrual period, unless she performs ghusl or tayammum and prays, or the prayer becomes a debt in her liability. That is when she finds after the cessation (of blood) a time sufficient for ghusl and the opening takbir and what is beyond them, to complete her normal period. For if it (the blood) stops at the time of duha (forenoon), and she does not perform ghusl or tayammum afterwards, intercourse with her is not permissible until the time of zuhr exits, because her prayer becomes established in her liability by its exit; because the time before midday is a neglected time, its exit is not considered. As for the view of the majority of our scholars that qada is obligatory by what obligates performance, the occurrence of the cause suffices for the obligation of qada even if she was not addressed with performance. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 1/399] Fasting: It should not be said that it would be appropriate for fasting to be permissible during menstruation just as it is permissible during janaba. We say: Refraining from the three nullifiers exists in janaba, so fasting is permissible. In menstruation, refraining from them for the sake of fasting does not exist because refraining from intercourse in it is due to menstruation, not due to fasting, so her fasting is not permissible. النفساء (al-nafsā’): A woman experiencing postpartum bleeding (nifās).
القضاء (al-qaḍā’): The compensatory performance of an act of worship after its prescribed time has elapsed.
دين في الذمة (dayn fī al-dhimmah): A liability or debt in one's obligation; here referring to the prayer becoming owed upon the woman after the time exits.

Prohibitions for Janaba and Minor Impurity
Listing of prohibitions with elaboration on ikhtilaf and definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five prohibitions for a junub and the three for a muḥdith, explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on reciting less than a verse, and apply the Hanafi position on touching the mus-haf and its cover.

Core Idea
A junub is prohibited from five acts; a muḥdith from three; reciting less than a verse is also prohibited according to the relied-upon view.

This passage from Nur al-Idah and its commentary in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq lays out the core prohibitions that apply to a person in major or minor impurity. While the list is straightforward, the text also delves into a nuanced difference of opinion within the Hanafi school on whether a junub may recite less than a full verse. Understanding both the basic rulings and the reasoning behind the preferred view will sharpen your fiqh instincts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of impurity
Separate the prohibitions for junub (major impurity) from muḥdith (minor impurity). Note that the junub has five prohibitions, the muḥdith has three.
The junub's list includes reciting Quran, touching Quran, and entering mosque—items not prohibited for muḥdith.
2
Analyze the ikhtilaf on reciting less than a verse
Examine the two positions: al-Karkhi (majority) prohibits absolutely; others permit if less than a verse. Understand the key argument: hadiths did not differentiate, so qiyas against text is rejected.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute; the relied-upon view is prohibition.
3
Interpret 'touching a verse' (mass ayat)
The author uses 'touching a verse' to include any surface with Quranic writing, such as a tablet or coin, not just the mus-haf.
Other scholars limited to the mus-haf; this broader view is preferred.
4
Define the cover (ghilaf) for mus-haf
Identify the two meanings: attached cover (like leather binding) and separate cover (pouch). The preferred view includes both, but the attached cover is considered part of the mus-haf.
Touching the mus-haf without any cover is prohibited.
5
Clarify 'entering a mosque'
It is prohibited for a junub to enter a mosque, whether for staying or passing through. Places like Eid prayer grounds, schools, and ribat are excluded.
The prohibition is specific to mosques, not all prayer areas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما يحرم بالجنابة ] وعليه الإجماع ويحرم بالجنابة خمسة أشياء: الصلاة، وقراءة آية من القرآن، ومسها إلا بغلاف ودخول مسجد، والطواف. ويحرم على المحدث ثلاثة أشياء الصلاة والطواف، ومس المصحف إلا بغلاف. آية اختلفوا في ما دون الآية، فمنهم من أطلق المنع ، وهو قول الكرخي، وصححه صاحب" الهداية" في "التجنيس"، وقاضي خان في شرح الجامع الصغير ، والولوالجي في "فتاواه" وقواه في "الكافي"، ونسبه صاحب البدائع" إلى عامة المشايخ، ومنهم من أباح ما دون الآية، وصححه صاحب "الخلاصة"، ومشى عليه فخر الإسلام في "شرح الجامع الصغير، ونسبه الزاهدي إلى الأكثر، والذي ينبغي ترجيحه: القول بالمنع؛ لأن الأحاديث لم تفصل، والتعليل في مقابلة النص مردود. [البحر الرائق: ٤٠٩/١] ومسها تعبير المصنف بمس آية أولى من تعبير غيره بمس المصحف؛ لشمول كلامه ما إذا مس لوحا مكتوبا عليه آية وكذا الدرهم والحائط، وتقييده بالسورة في "الهداية" اتفاقي، بل المراد الآية، لكن لا يجوز مس كله المكتوب وغيره، بخلاف غيره، فإنه لا يمنع إلا مس المكتوب. [البحر الرائق: ٤١٢/١] بغلاف وفي تفسير الغلاف اختلاف فقيل: الجلد المشرز، وفي غاية البيان: مصحف مشرز أجزاؤه مشدود بعضها إلى بعض من الشيرازة، وليست بعربية، وفي "الكافي" والغلاف: "الجلد الذي عليه" في الأصح، وقيل: هو المنفصل كالخريطة ،ونحوها والمتصل بالمصحف منه حتى يدخل في بيعه بلا ذكر، وصحح هذا القول في "الهداية" وكثير من الكتب البحر الرائق بتصرف : ٤١٢/١٢] ودخول مسجد أي يحرم بالجنابة دخول مسجد، قيد بالمسجد، فخرج غيره كمصلى العيد والجنائز والمدرسة والرباط، فلا يمنع الجنب من دخولها، وأطلق الدخول فشمل ما إذا كان الدخول للمكث أو للمرور.
What is prohibited by janaba: There is consensus upon it. And five things are prohibited by janaba: prayer, reciting a verse of the Quran, touching it except with a cover, entering a mosque, and tawaf. And three things are prohibited for the one with minor impurity: prayer, tawaf, and touching the mus-haf except with a cover. Regarding 'a verse': they differed concerning less than a verse. Some of them absolutely prohibited it, which is the statement of al-Karkhi, and the author of al-Hidayah in al-Tajnīs, Qadi Khan in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Walwaliji in his Fatawa, and it was strengthened in al-Kafi, and the author of al-Bada'i' attributed it to the generality of the scholars. And some of them permitted less than a verse, which was corrected by the author of al-Khulasa, and Fakhr al-Islam acted upon it in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir, and al-Zahidi attributed it to the majority. And what should be preferred is the prohibition, because the hadiths did not differentiate, and reasoning against the text is rejected. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 1/409] And 'touching it': the author's expression of 'touching a verse' is better than the expression of others of 'touching the mus-haf' because his words include if one touches a tablet on which a verse is written, and likewise a dirham and a wall. His restriction to 'surah' in al-Hidayah is coincidental; rather what is intended is verse, but it is not permissible to touch all of it, written and other, unlike other than it, for it does not prevent except the touching of what is written. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 1/412] 'With a cover': and there is difference in interpretation of the cover. It is said: the stitched leather. In Ghayat al-Bayan: a mus-haf with its parts stitched and bound together, from al-shirazah, which is not Arabic. In al-Kafi: and the cover is 'the leather that is upon it' in the most correct view. And it is said: it is the separate one like the pouch and the like, and the attached one from the mus-haf so that it enters into its sale without mention. This statement was corrected in al-Hidayah and many books. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq with adaptation: 1/412] 'And entering a mosque' means entering a mosque is prohibited by janaba. It is restricted to mosque, so other than it like the Eid prayer place, funeral prayer place, school, and ribat are excluded, so the junub is not prevented from entering them. And he made 'entry' absolute, so it includes whether the entry is for staying or passing through.
Source pages p. 56

Key Terms
الجنب (al-junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
المحدث (al-muḥdith): A person in a state of minor impurity requiring wudu.
الغلاف (al-ghilāf): The cover or binding of the mus-haf; includes attached leather or separate pouch.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Five
B) Three
C) Four
D) Six

Key Takeaway
A junub is prohibited from five acts (salah, recitation, touching Quran, mosque entry, tawaf) and a muḥdith from three; reciting less than a verse is prohibited as per the relied-upon view.

Rulings for Istihadah and the Ma'dhur
Explanation of istihadah and the wudu obligations for those with chronic excuses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for istihadah (irregular bleeding) and explain the wudu obligation for a ma'dhur (one with a chronic excuse).

Core Idea
Istihadah does not invalidate worship; the ma'dhur must perform wudu for each prayer time.

This lesson clarifies the rulings for istihadah—irregular uterine bleeding that is not menstrual—and for individuals with chronic excuses (ma'dhur) such as urinary incontinence or chronic diarrhea. The Hanafi school provides clear guidance that these conditions do not prevent acts of worship, but they impose a specific wudu obligation for each prayer time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of chronic excuses
Recognize that istihadah is one type of chronic excuse, and others include sals al-bawl (urinary incontinence) and istitlaq al-batn (chronic diarrhea).
These conditions are called 'udhr (excuse) in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Understand the definition of istihadah
Istihadah is blood from a ruptured vein, not from the womb, and it has no characteristic odor. This distinguishes it from menstrual blood (hayd).
The source cites Maraqui al-Falah: 'it is blood from a vein, not from the womb, and its sign is that it has no odor.'
3
Determine the obligation of wudu
The mustahadah (woman with istihadah) and other ma'dhur must perform wudu for each fard prayer time. This wudu suffices for that entire prayer time even if the excuse continues.
The text explicitly states: 'And the mustahadah and one with an excuse perform wudu.'
4
Note that istinja is not required for each prayer
The commentary clarifies that istinja (washing the private parts) is not required for each prayer time, only wudu.
This is a key practical difference from normal purity requirements.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[مراقي الفلاح: ١٤٨] وتتوضأ : شروع في طهارة ذوي الأعذار المستحاضة أفاد أنه لا يجب عليها الاستنجاء لوقت كل صلاة] دم نقص عن أقل الحيض، أو زاد على أكثره، أو أكثر النفاس أو زاد على عادتها في أقلهما، أو يجاوز أكثرهما، والحبلى والتي لم تبلغ تسع سنين مراقي الفلاح: ١٤٨] كسلس بول: قيل: السلس: بفتح اللام نفس الخارج، وبكسرها من به هذا المرض وصاحبه هو الذي لا ينقطع تقاطر بوله لضعف في مثانته، أو لغلبة البرودة. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٤٩] واستطلاق بطن أي جريان ما فيه من إطلاق اسم المحل على الحال فيه كسال الوادي. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٤٩]
And the blood of istihadah (irregular uterine bleeding) is like a continuous nosebleed; it does not prevent prayer, nor fasting, nor intercourse. [Heading: Rulings of the one with an excuse (ma'dhur)] And the mustahadah (woman with istihadah) and one with an excuse such as urinary incontinence (sals al-bawl) and chronic diarrhea (istitlaq al-batn) perform wudu. And the blood of istihadah: it is blood from a (ruptured) vein, not from the womb, and its sign is that it has no odor. [Maraqi al-Falah: 148] 'And they perform wudu': beginning of the purity (rulings) of those with excuses. The mustahadah: it indicates that estinja (washing the private part) is not required for each prayer time. [Blood that is] less than the minimum of hayd, or exceeds its maximum, or the maximum of nifas, or exceeds her habit in the minimum of them, or surpasses their maximum, and the pregnant woman and one who has not reached nine years (of age). [Maraqi al-Falah: 148] 'Like sals al-bawl': it is said: sals with a fatha on the lam is the thing that exits itself, and with a kasra on the lam is the one who has this illness. And its possessor is one whose urine does not stop dripping due to weakness in his bladder or due to overwhelming cold. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 149] 'And istitlaq al-batn' means the flowing of what is in it, by a metonymy of place for the thing in it, like the flow of a valley. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 149]
Source pages p. 57

Key Terms
الاستحاضة (al-istiḥāḍah): Irregular uterine bleeding that is not menstrual or postpartum; it is caused by a ruptured vein and has no characteristic smell.
المعذور (al-ma‘dhūr): One who has a chronic excuse such as urinary incontinence or chronic diarrhea; they are excused from some purity requirements but must perform wudu for each prayer time.
سلس البول (sals al-bawl): Urinary incontinence, the continuous dripping of urine due to bladder weakness or cold.
استطلاق البطن (istitlāq al-baṭn): Chronic diarrhea, the involuntary flow of stools.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the obligation of a mustahadah (woman with irregular bleeding) regarding wudu?
A) She must perform ghusl before each prayer.
B) She must perform wudu for each fard prayer time.
C) She must perform wudu and istinja before each prayer.
D) She is excused from wudu because the blood is continuous.

Key Takeaway
The mustahadah and others with chronic excuses must perform wudu for each fard prayer time, and this wudu remains valid for that prayer time despite the ongoing excuse.

Taharah — Purification

Who is a Ma'dhur? Definition and Condition
Defines the ma'dhur and sets the condition for the status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of a ma'dhur and identify the condition that must be met for someone to be considered a ma'dhur in Hanafi law.

Core Idea
A ma'dhur is someone whose chronic excuse covers an entire prayer time without a break sufficient for wudu and prayer.

In Hanafi fiqh, a person who suffers from a continuous excuse such as istihadah, urine incontinence, or chronic diarrhea is granted a special ruling to facilitate worship. This lesson explains who qualifies as a ma'dhur and what condition must be fulfilled for this status to apply.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of excuses
The text mentions istihadah, sals al-bawl (urine incontinence), and istitlaq al-batn (chronic diarrhea). These are chronic conditions that prevent normal purity.
Excuses must be continuous or recurrent.
2
Understand the condition for being a ma'dhur
The passage states: 'ولا يصير معذورا حتى يستوعبه العذر وقتا كاملا' – a person does not become excused until the excuse covers a complete prayer time without a break sufficient for wudu and prayer.
The time is a full fard prayer time (e.g., Zuhr time).
3
Distinguish actual vs constructive coverage
Coverage can be actual (excuse exists throughout) or constructive (excuse breaks for a short time insufficient for purification). Both establish the status.
If the excuse stops for a period long enough to perform wudu and prayer, the person is no longer a ma'dhur.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الاستيعاب
لوقت كل فرض الا لكل فرض ولا نفل] قال في "البدائع": وإنما تبقى طهارة صاحب العذر في الوقت إذا لم يحدث حدثاً آخر، أما إذا أحدث حدثاً آخر فلا تبقى، كما إذا سال الدم من أحد منخريه فتوضأ، ثم سال من المنخر الآخر، فعليه الوضوء؛ لأن هذا حدث جديد لم يكن موجوداً وقت الطهارة، فأما إذا سال منهما جميعا فتوضأ ثم انقطع أحدهما، فهو على وضوئه ما بقي الوقت. [البحر الرائق: ٤٣٢/١] من الفرائض إلخ: لا يراد به الحصر بل يصلون النذور والواجبات أيضًا ما دام الوقت باقيا عندنا. [العناية: ١٥٩/١] بخروج الوقت: أي يبطل وضوؤهم بخروج الوقت فقط، وهو قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد، وقال زفر: يبطل بالدخول فقط، وقال أبو يوسف يبطل بكل واحد منهما، وثمرة الخلاف تظهر في موضعين أحدهما: إذا توضؤوا بعد طلوع الشمس لهم أن يصلوا به الظهر عندهما، وعند أبي يوسف وزفر ليس لهم ذلك والثاني: إذا توضؤوا قبل طلوع الشمس انتقض طهارتهم بطلوع الشمس عندهم وعند زفر لا تنتقض [تبيين الحقائق: ۱۸۲/۱] ثم إنما يبطل بخروجه إذا توضؤوا على السيلان أو وجد السيلان بعد الوضوء، أما إذا كان على الانقطاع ودام إلى خروج الوقت، فلا يبطل بالخروج ما لم يحدث حدثا آخر أو يسيل. [البحر الرائق: ٤٣٤/١] ثم اعلم أن مشايخنا صر أضافوا انتقاض الطهارة إلى خروج الوقت أو دخوله ليسهل على المتعلمين وإلا فلا تأثير للخروج والدخول في الانتقاض حقيقة وإنما يظهر الحدث السابق عنده ولهذا لا يجوز لهم أن يمسحوا على الخفين بعد ما خرج الوقت، وكذا لا يجوز لهم البناء إذا خرج الوقت وهم في الصلاة؛ لأن جوازهما عرف نصا الحدث الطارئ لا في الحدث السابق، وبخروج الوقت يظهر الحدث السابق. [تبيين الحقائق: ۱۸۳/۱] فقط أي لا بدخوله خلافا لزفر له ولا بكل منهما ، خلافا لأبي يوسف حه ولا يصير: أي من ابتلي بناقض الوضوء والصلاة أطلقها وهي مقيدة بالمفروضة؛ لئلا يرد عليه الوقت المهمل، كما بين الطلوع والزوال؛ فإنه وقت لصلاة غير مفروضة، وهي العيد والضحى، فلو استوعبه لا يصير معذوراً، وكذا لو استوعبه الانقطاع لا يكون برء. وهذا: أي المذكور من الاستيعاب مطلقا سواء كان حقيقياً بأن وجد العذر في جميع الوقت، أو حكميا بأن ينقطع العذر انقطاعا قليلا لا الطهارة والصلاة شرط؛ لكونه معذورا ابتداء. يسع
Book of Purification - Rulings of the Excused Person. From the Quran, and touching it except with a cover, and entering a mosque, and circumambulation. Three things are forbidden for the one in minor impurity: prayer, circumambulation, and touching the Mushaf except with a cover. And the blood of istihadah is like a continuous nosebleed; it does not prevent prayer, nor fasting, nor intercourse. Rulings of the excused person: The mustahadah (woman with chronic bleeding) and one who has an excuse like urine incontinence and chronic diarrhea - meaning its continuous flow - perform wudu for each obligatory prayer, whether the prayer is obligatory or supererogatory. And they pray with their wudu as many obligatory and supererogatory prayers as they wish. And the wudu of the excused persons is nullified only by the exit of the time. And a person does not become excused until the excuse covers a complete time period in which there is no break sufficient for wudu and prayer. This is the condition for its establishment. [Commentary on the condition] For each obligatory time - not for each prayer nor supererogatory. Al-Bada'i states: The purity of the one with an excuse remains within the time only if he does not commit another nullifier. But if he commits another nullifier, it does not remain, as when blood flows from one nostril and he performs wudu, then blood flows from the other nostril, he must perform wudu because this is a new nullifier that did not exist at the time of purity. But if it flowed from both and he performed wudu, then one stopped, he remains in his wudu as long as the time remains. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 1/432] 'From the obligatory prayers etc.' - it does not mean restriction, but they pray vows and obligatory duties as well as long as the time remains according to us. [Al-Inayah 1/159] 'By exit of time' - meaning their wudu is nullified only by exit of time. This is the statement of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Zufar said: It is nullified only by entry. Abu Yusuf said: It is nullified by each of them. The fruit of the difference appears in two places: One: If they perform wudu after sunrise, they can pray Zuhr with it according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), but according to Abu Yusuf and Zufar they cannot. Second: If they perform wudu before sunrise, their purity is nullified by sunrise according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), but according to Zufar it is not nullified. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 1/182] Then it is nullified by its exit only if they performed wudu while the flow was happening, or the flow occurred after wudu. But if they performed wudu during a pause and the pause lasted until exit of time, it is not nullified by exit unless another nullifier occurs or flow resumes. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 1/434] Then know that our scholars attributed nullification of purity to exit or entry of time only to make it easy for students; otherwise, exit and entry have no real effect on nullification; rather the previous nullifying event manifests at that time. For this reason, they are not allowed to wipe over khuffs after the time exits, nor are they allowed to build (on previous prayer) if the time exits while they are in prayer, because permissibility of these is established for a new occurring nullifier, not for the previous nullifier. By exit of time, the previous nullifier manifests. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 1/183] 'Only' - i.e., not by entry, contrary to Zufar. And not by each of them, contrary to Abu Yusuf. 'And a person does not become excused' - i.e., one afflicted with a nullifier of wudu and prayer. He used the absolute term 'prayer' but it is restricted to obligatory prayer, to avoid objection from the idle time (like between sunrise and zawal) which is a time for non-obligatory prayer, i.e., Eid and Duha. So if the excuse covers that time, he does not become excused. Likewise, if a break covers it, it is not recovery. And 'this' - i.e., the mentioned condition of coverage - is absolute, whether actual (the excuse exists throughout the time) or constructive (the excuse breaks for a short time insufficient for purification and prayer). This is a condition for being considered excused initially.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah states the rulings for a person with a chronic excuse (ma'dhur) that prevents complete purity, such as istihadah (chronic non-menstrual bleeding), urine incontinence (sals al-bawl), or chronic diarrhea (istitlaq al-batn). The author first distinguishes istihadah from menstruation: its blood is from a vein, not the uterus, and has no odor. It does not prevent prayer, fasting, or intercourse. The core ruling: such a person must perform fresh wudu for each obligatory prayer time (not for each prayer). With that wudu, they can pray any number of obligatory or supererogatory prayers during that time. The wudu is nullified only when the time exits (according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). The condition for being considered excused is that the excuse must be continuous throughout a complete prayer time (like Zuhr time) with no break long enough to perform wudu and prayer (about 5-10 minutes estimated). If the excuse stops for that long, the person is no longer 'excused' and must perform wudu normally. The passage also details an intra-Hanafi dispute: Zufar holds that wudu is nullified upon entry of the time, Abu Yusuf that it is nullified at both entry and exit. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is shown in two cases: if the person performs wudu after sunrise, they can pray Zuhr with it according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but not according to Abu Yusuf and Zufar. If they wudu before sunrise, their wudu is broken at sunrise according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but not according to Zufar. The passage clarifies that the attribution to time is metaphorical; the real cause is the previous hadath manifesting at that moment.

Key Terms
المعذور (al-ma'dhur): A person with a chronic excuse that prevents normal purification, such as constant bleeding, urine incontinence, or diarrhea.
الاستحاضة (al-istihadah): Chronic non-menstrual bleeding from a vein (not the uterus); it has no odor and does not prevent prayer, fasting, or intercourse.
سلس البول (sals al-bawl): Urinary incontinence – continuous dripping of urine due to weakness in the bladder or excessive coldness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum duration that a chronic excuse must cover for a person to be considered a ma'dhur in Hanafi law?
A) The time of one fard prayer
B) The time of one nafl prayer
C) One hour
D) A full day

Key Takeaway
A person becomes a ma'dhur only when their chronic excuse covers an entire fard prayer time without a break sufficient for purification and prayer.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
7 min
The Ruling: Wudu for Each Fard Time
States the ruling of wudu per fard time and the scope of prayers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a ma'dhur must perform wudu for each fard prayer time and explain what prayers they can perform with that wudu.

Core Idea
The ma'dhur's wudu is valid for the entire time period, allowing them to pray any number of fard and nafl prayers without repeating wudu.

Once a person qualifies as a ma'dhur, a special ruling applies: they must perform a fresh wudu for each fard prayer time. With that wudu, they can pray any number of obligatory and supererogatory prayers during that time. This lesson explains the obligation and its scope.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligation
The text says 'تتوضأ المستحاضة ومن به عذر ... لوقت كل فرض' – the ma'dhur performs wudu for each fard time. This is wajib.
It is not required to repeat wudu for each prayer; one wudu suffices for the whole time.
2
Understand what prayers are allowed
The text states 'ويصلون به ما شاؤوا من الفرائض والنوافل' – they can pray any number of fard and nafl prayers with that wudu, including make-up prayers and vows.
As long as no new nullifier occurs.
3
Recognize the consequence of a new nullifier
If a new hadath (e.g., blood from the other nostril) occurs, the wudu is broken and must be repeated within the same time.
The text gives an example from Al-Bada'i: blood from one nostril then the other requires a new wudu.

المصحف
من القرآن أطلق حرمة ،القرآن فشمل ما إذا قصد قراءة القرآن أو لم يقصد، وفي "العيون" لأبي الليث: ولو أنه قرأ الفاتحة على سبيل الدعاء، أو شيئا من الآيات التي فيها معنى الدعاء ولم يرد به القراءة، فلا بأس به، واختاره الحلواني وذكر في غاية البيان أنه المختار ، لكن قال الهندواني: لا أفتي بهذا وإن روي عن أبي حنيفة. [البحر الرائق: ٤١٠/١] ومسها تعبير المصنف بمس آية أولى من تعبير غيره بمس المصحف؛ لشمول كلامه ما إذا مس لوحا مكتوبا عليه آية وكذا الدرهم والحائط، وتقييده بالسورة في "الهداية" اتفاقي، بل المراد الآية، لكن لا يجوز مس كله المكتوب وغيره، بخلاف غيره، فإنه لا يمنع إلا مس المكتوب. [البحر الرائق: ٤١٢/١] بغلاف وفي تفسير الغلاف اختلاف فقيل: الجلد المشرز، وفي غاية البيان: مصحف مشرز أجزاؤه مشدود بعضها إلى بعض من الشيرازة، وليست بعربية، وفي "الكافي" والغلاف: "الجلد الذي عليه" في الأصح، وقيل: هو المنفصل كالخريطة ،ونحوها والمتصل بالمصحف منه حتى يدخل في بيعه بلا ذكر، وصحح هذا القول في "الهداية" وكثير من الكتب البحر الرائق بتصرف : ٤١٢/١٢] ودخول مسجد أي يحرم بالجنابة دخول مسجد، قيد بالمسجد، فخرج غيره كمصلى العيد والجنائز والمدرسة والرباط، فلا يمنع الجنب من دخولها، وأطلق الدخول فشمل ما إذا كان الدخول للمكث أو للمرور. ودم الاستحاضة: هو دم عرق انفجر ليس من الرحم وعلامته أنه لا رائحة له. [مراقي الفلاح: ١٤٨] وتتوضاً : شروع في طهارة ذوي الأعذار المستحاضة أفاد أنه لا يجب عليها الاستنجاء لوقت كل صلاة] دم نقص عن أقل الحيض، أو زاد على أكثره، أو أكثر النفاس أو زاد على عادتها في أقلهما، أو يجاوز أكثرهما، والحبلى والتي لم تبلغ تسع سنين مراقي الفلاح: ١٤٨] كسلس بول: قيل: السلس: بفتح اللام نفس الخارج، وبكسرها من به هذا المرض وصاحبه هو الذي لا ينقطع تقاطر بوله لضعف في مثانته، أو لغلبة البرودة. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٤٩] واستطلاق بطن أي جريان ما فيه من إطلاق اسم المحل على الحال فيه كسال الوادي. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٤٩]
