الاستيعاب
لوقت كل فرض الا لكل فرض ولا نفل] قال في "البدائع": وإنما تبقى طهارة صاحب العذر في الوقت إذا لم يحدث حدثاً آخر، أما إذا أحدث حدثاً آخر فلا تبقى، كما إذا سال الدم من أحد منخريه فتوضأ، ثم سال من المنخر الآخر، فعليه الوضوء؛ لأن هذا حدث جديد لم يكن موجوداً وقت الطهارة، فأما إذا سال منهما جميعا فتوضأ ثم انقطع أحدهما، فهو على وضوئه ما بقي الوقت. [البحر الرائق: ٤٣٢/١] من الفرائض إلخ: لا يراد به الحصر بل يصلون النذور والواجبات أيضًا ما دام الوقت باقيا عندنا. [العناية: ١٥٩/١] بخروج الوقت: أي يبطل وضوؤهم بخروج الوقت فقط، وهو قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد، وقال زفر: يبطل بالدخول فقط، وقال أبو يوسف يبطل بكل واحد منهما، وثمرة الخلاف تظهر في موضعين أحدهما: إذا توضؤوا بعد طلوع الشمس لهم أن يصلوا به الظهر عندهما، وعند أبي يوسف وزفر ليس لهم ذلك والثاني: إذا توضؤوا قبل طلوع الشمس انتقض طهارتهم بطلوع الشمس عندهم وعند زفر لا تنتقض [تبيين الحقائق: ۱۸۲/۱] ثم إنما يبطل بخروجه إذا توضؤوا على السيلان أو وجد السيلان بعد الوضوء، أما إذا كان على الانقطاع ودام إلى خروج الوقت، فلا يبطل بالخروج ما لم يحدث حدثا آخر أو يسيل. [البحر الرائق: ٤٣٤/١] ثم اعلم أن مشايخنا صر أضافوا انتقاض الطهارة إلى خروج الوقت أو دخوله ليسهل على المتعلمين وإلا فلا تأثير للخروج والدخول في الانتقاض حقيقة وإنما يظهر الحدث السابق عنده ولهذا لا يجوز لهم أن يمسحوا على الخفين بعد ما خرج الوقت، وكذا لا يجوز لهم البناء إذا خرج الوقت وهم في الصلاة؛ لأن جوازهما عرف نصا الحدث الطارئ لا في الحدث السابق، وبخروج الوقت يظهر الحدث السابق. [تبيين الحقائق: ۱۸۳/۱] فقط أي لا بدخوله خلافا لزفر له ولا بكل منهما ، خلافا لأبي يوسف حه ولا يصير: أي من ابتلي بناقض الوضوء والصلاة أطلقها وهي مقيدة بالمفروضة؛ لئلا يرد عليه الوقت المهمل، كما بين الطلوع والزوال؛ فإنه وقت لصلاة غير مفروضة، وهي العيد والضحى، فلو استوعبه لا يصير معذوراً، وكذا لو استوعبه الانقطاع لا يكون برء. وهذا: أي المذكور من الاستيعاب مطلقا سواء كان حقيقياً بأن وجد العذر في جميع الوقت، أو حكميا بأن ينقطع العذر انقطاعا قليلا لا الطهارة والصلاة شرط؛ لكونه معذورا ابتداء. يسع
Book of Purification - Rulings of the Excused Person. From the Quran, and touching it except with a cover, and entering a mosque, and circumambulation. Three things are forbidden for the one in minor impurity: prayer, circumambulation, and touching the Mushaf except with a cover. And the blood of istihadah is like a continuous nosebleed; it does not prevent prayer, nor fasting, nor intercourse. Rulings of the excused person: The mustahadah (woman with chronic bleeding) and one who has an excuse like urine incontinence and chronic diarrhea - meaning its continuous flow - perform wudu for each obligatory prayer, whether the prayer is obligatory or supererogatory. And they pray with their wudu as many obligatory and supererogatory prayers as they wish. And the wudu of the excused persons is nullified only by the exit of the time. And a person does not become excused until the excuse covers a complete time period in which there is no break sufficient for wudu and prayer. This is the condition for its establishment. [Commentary on the condition] For each obligatory time - not for each prayer nor supererogatory. Al-Bada'i states: The purity of the one with an excuse remains within the time only if he does not commit another nullifier. But if he commits another nullifier, it does not remain, as when blood flows from one nostril and he performs wudu, then blood flows from the other nostril, he must perform wudu because this is a new nullifier that did not exist at the time of purity. But if it flowed from both and he performed wudu, then one stopped, he remains in his wudu as long as the time remains. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 1/432] 'From the obligatory prayers etc.' - it does not mean restriction, but they pray vows and obligatory duties as well as long as the time remains according to us. [Al-Inayah 1/159] 'By exit of time' - meaning their wudu is nullified only by exit of time. This is the statement of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Zufar said: It is nullified only by entry. Abu Yusuf said: It is nullified by each of them. The fruit of the difference appears in two places: One: If they perform wudu after sunrise, they can pray Zuhr with it according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), but according to Abu Yusuf and Zufar they cannot. Second: If they perform wudu before sunrise, their purity is nullified by sunrise according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), but according to Zufar it is not nullified. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 1/182] Then it is nullified by its exit only if they performed wudu while the flow was happening, or the flow occurred after wudu. But if they performed wudu during a pause and the pause lasted until exit of time, it is not nullified by exit unless another nullifier occurs or flow resumes. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 1/434] Then know that our scholars attributed nullification of purity to exit or entry of time only to make it easy for students; otherwise, exit and entry have no real effect on nullification; rather the previous nullifying event manifests at that time. For this reason, they are not allowed to wipe over khuffs after the time exits, nor are they allowed to build (on previous prayer) if the time exits while they are in prayer, because permissibility of these is established for a new occurring nullifier, not for the previous nullifier. By exit of time, the previous nullifier manifests. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 1/183] 'Only' - i.e., not by entry, contrary to Zufar. And not by each of them, contrary to Abu Yusuf. 'And a person does not become excused' - i.e., one afflicted with a nullifier of wudu and prayer. He used the absolute term 'prayer' but it is restricted to obligatory prayer, to avoid objection from the idle time (like between sunrise and zawal) which is a time for non-obligatory prayer, i.e., Eid and Duha. So if the excuse covers that time, he does not become excused. Likewise, if a break covers it, it is not recovery. And 'this' - i.e., the mentioned condition of coverage - is absolute, whether actual (the excuse exists throughout the time) or constructive (the excuse breaks for a short time insufficient for purification and prayer). This is a condition for being considered excused initially.

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many wudu does a ma'dhur need to perform during the Zuhr time if he wants to pray fard Zuhr and two nafl prayers?
A) One wudu at the start of Zuhr time suffices.
B) Two wudu: one for fard and one for nafl.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Nullification of Ma'dhur's Wudu: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Details the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding nullification of the ma'dhur's wudu.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three Hanafi positions on when the ma'dhur's wudu is nullified and apply the relied-upon position to practical scenarios.

Core Idea
The wudu of a ma'dhur is nullified only by the exit of the prayer time according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad; other Hanafi imams differ on entry and exit.

One of the most discussed aspects of the ma'dhur's ruling is the exact moment when their wudu is considered nullified. The Hanafi school has three positions: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say only at exit of time, Zufar says only at entry, and Abu Yusuf says both. The relied-upon view is exit only. This lesson dissects the dispute and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the three positions
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: nullified by exit of time. Zufar: nullified by entry. Abu Yusuf: nullified by both.
These are clearly outlined in the text.
2
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
The text gives two cases: (1) wudu after sunrise for Zuhr – according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), Zuhr can be prayed; according to others, not. (2) wudu before sunrise – nullified at sunrise according to majority but not according to Zufar.
Note the time of sunrise is the boundary between Fajr and the start of the voluntary time, not a fard time boundary. However, the example illustrates entry vs exit.
3
Recognize the metaphorical attribution
The text clarifies that attributing nullification to entry/exit is a pedagogical simplification. The real cause is the manifestation of the previous hadath at that boundary.
This explains why the ma'dhur cannot wipe over khuffs after the time exits.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

من القرآن أطلق حرمة ،القرآن فشمل ما إذا قصد قراءة القرآن أو لم يقصد، وفي "العيون" لأبي الليث: ولو أنه قرأ الفاتحة على سبيل الدعاء، أو شيئا من الآيات التي فيها معنى الدعاء ولم يرد به القراءة، فلا بأس به، واختاره الحلواني وذكر في غاية البيان أنه المختار ، لكن قال الهندواني: لا أفتي بهذا وإن روي عن أبي حنيفة. [البحر الرائق: ٤١٠/١] ومسها تعبير المصنف بمس آية أولى من تعبير غيره بمس المصحف؛ لشمول كلامه ما إذا مس لوحا مكتوبا عليه آية وكذا الدرهم والحائط، وتقييده بالسورة في "الهداية" اتفاقي، بل المراد الآية، لكن لا يجوز مس كله المكتوب وغيره، بخلاف غيره، فإنه لا يمنع إلا مس المكتوب. [البحر الرائق: ٤١٢/١] بغلاف وفي تفسير الغلاف اختلاف فقيل: الجلد المشرز، وفي غاية البيان: مصحف مشرز أجزاؤه مشدود بعضها إلى بعض من الشيرازة، وليست بعربية، وفي "الكافي" والغلاف: "الجلد الذي عليه" في الأصح، وقيل: هو المنفصل كالخريطة ،ونحوها والمتصل بالمصحف منه حتى يدخل في بيعه بلا ذكر، وصحح هذا القول في "الهداية" وكثير من الكتب البحر الرائق بتصرف : ٤١٢/١٢] ودخول مسجد أي يحرم بالجنابة دخول مسجد، قيد بالمسجد، فخرج غيره كمصلى العيد والجنائز والمدرسة والرباط، فلا يمنع الجنب من دخولها، وأطلق الدخول فشمل ما إذا كان الدخول للمكث أو للمرور. ودم الاستحاضة: هو دم عرق انفجر ليس من الرحم وعلامته أنه لا رائحة له. [مراقي الفلاح: ١٤٨] وتتوضاً : شروع في طهارة ذوي الأعذار المستحاضة أفاد أنه لا يجب عليها الاستنجاء لوقت كل صلاة] دم نقص عن أقل الحيض، أو زاد على أكثره، أو أكثر النفاس أو زاد على عادتها في أقلهما، أو يجاوز أكثرهما، والحبلى والتي لم تبلغ تسع سنين مراقي الفلاح: ١٤٨] كسلس بول: قيل: السلس: بفتح اللام نفس الخارج، وبكسرها من به هذا المرض وصاحبه هو الذي لا ينقطع تقاطر بوله لضعف في مثانته، أو لغلبة البرودة. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٤٩] واستطلاق بطن أي جريان ما فيه من إطلاق اسم المحل على الحال فيه كسال الوادي. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٤٩]
هي
ذات
أحكام المعذور
كتاب الطهارة لوقت كل فرض، ويصلون به ما شاؤوا من الفرائض والنوافل، ويبطل وضوء بوضوئهم
والواجبات أيضا
المعذورين بخروج الوقت فقط، ولا يصير معذورا حتى يستوعبه العذر وقتا كاملا ليس فيه انقطاع بقدر الوضوء والصلاة، وهذا شرط ثبوته .
أي لعذره
الاستيعاب
لوقت كل فرض الا لكل فرض ولا نفل] قال في "البدائع": وإنما تبقى طهارة صاحب العذر في الوقت إذا لم يحدث حدثاً آخر، أما إذا أحدث حدثاً آخر فلا تبقى، كما إذا سال الدم من أحد منخريه فتوضأ، ثم سال من المنخر الآخر، فعليه الوضوء؛ لأن هذا حدث جديد لم يكن موجوداً وقت الطهارة، فأما إذا سال منهما جميعا فتوضأ ثم انقطع أحدهما، فهو على وضوئه ما بقي الوقت. [البحر الرائق: ٤٣٢/١] من الفرائض إلخ: لا يراد به الحصر بل يصلون النذور والواجبات أيضًا ما دام الوقت باقيا عندنا. [العناية: ١٥٩/١] بخروج الوقت: أي يبطل وضوؤهم بخروج الوقت فقط، وهو قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد، وقال زفر: يبطل بالدخول فقط، وقال أبو يوسف يبطل بكل واحد منهما، وثمرة الخلاف تظهر في موضعين أحدهما: إذا توضؤوا بعد طلوع الشمس لهم أن يصلوا به الظهر عندهما، وعند أبي يوسف وزفر ليس لهم ذلك والثاني: إذا توضؤوا قبل طلوع الشمس انتقض طهارتهم بطلوع الشمس عندهم وعند زفر لا تنتقض [تبيين الحقائق: ۱۸۲/۱] ثم إنما يبطل بخروجه إذا توضؤوا على السيلان أو وجد السيلان بعد الوضوء، أما إذا كان على الانقطاع ودام إلى خروج الوقت، فلا يبطل بالخروج ما لم يحدث حدثا آخر أو يسيل. [البحر الرائق: ٤٣٤/١] ثم اعلم أن مشايخنا صر أضافوا انتقاض الطهارة إلى خروج الوقت أو دخوله ليسهل على المتعلمين وإلا فلا تأثير للخروج والدخول في الانتقاض حقيقة وإنما يظهر الحدث السابق عنده ولهذا لا يجوز لهم أن يمسحوا على الخفين بعد ما خرج الوقت، وكذا لا يجوز لهم البناء إذا خرج الوقت وهم في الصلاة؛ لأن جوازهما عرف نصا الحدث الطارئ لا في الحدث السابق، وبخروج الوقت يظهر الحدث السابق. [تبيين الحقائق: ۱۸۳/۱] فقط أي لا بدخوله خلافا لزفر له ولا بكل منهما ، خلافا لأبي يوسف حه ولا يصير: أي من ابتلي بناقض الوضوء والصلاة أطلقها وهي مقيدة بالمفروضة؛ لئلا يرد عليه الوقت المهمل، كما بين الطلوع والزوال؛ فإنه وقت لصلاة غير مفروضة، وهي العيد والضحى، فلو استوعبه لا يصير معذوراً، وكذا لو استوعبه الانقطاع لا يكون برء. وهذا: أي المذكور من الاستيعاب مطلقا سواء كان حقيقياً بأن وجد العذر في جميع الوقت، أو حكميا بأن ينقطع العذر انقطاعا قليلا لا الطهارة والصلاة شرط؛ لكونه معذورا ابتداء. يسع
Book of Purification - Rulings of the Excused Person. From the Quran, and touching it except with a cover, and entering a mosque, and circumambulation. Three things are forbidden for the one in minor impurity: prayer, circumambulation, and touching the Mushaf except with a cover. And the blood of istihadah is like a continuous nosebleed; it does not prevent prayer, nor fasting, nor intercourse. Rulings of the excused person: The mustahadah (woman with chronic bleeding) and one who has an excuse like urine incontinence and chronic diarrhea - meaning its continuous flow - perform wudu for each obligatory prayer, whether the prayer is obligatory or supererogatory. And they pray with their wudu as many obligatory and supererogatory prayers as they wish. And the wudu of the excused persons is nullified only by the exit of the time. And a person does not become excused until the excuse covers a complete time period in which there is no break sufficient for wudu and prayer. This is the condition for its establishment. [Commentary on the condition] For each obligatory time - not for each prayer nor supererogatory. Al-Bada'i states: The purity of the one with an excuse remains within the time only if he does not commit another nullifier. But if he commits another nullifier, it does not remain, as when blood flows from one nostril and he performs wudu, then blood flows from the other nostril, he must perform wudu because this is a new nullifier that did not exist at the time of purity. But if it flowed from both and he performed wudu, then one stopped, he remains in his wudu as long as the time remains. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 1/432] 'From the obligatory prayers etc.' - it does not mean restriction, but they pray vows and obligatory duties as well as long as the time remains according to us. [Al-Inayah 1/159] 'By exit of time' - meaning their wudu is nullified only by exit of time. This is the statement of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Zufar said: It is nullified only by entry. Abu Yusuf said: It is nullified by each of them. The fruit of the difference appears in two places: One: If they perform wudu after sunrise, they can pray Zuhr with it according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), but according to Abu Yusuf and Zufar they cannot. Second: If they perform wudu before sunrise, their purity is nullified by sunrise according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), but according to Zufar it is not nullified. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 1/182] Then it is nullified by its exit only if they performed wudu while the flow was happening, or the flow occurred after wudu. But if they performed wudu during a pause and the pause lasted until exit of time, it is not nullified by exit unless another nullifier occurs or flow resumes. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 1/434] Then know that our scholars attributed nullification of purity to exit or entry of time only to make it easy for students; otherwise, exit and entry have no real effect on nullification; rather the previous nullifying event manifests at that time. For this reason, they are not allowed to wipe over khuffs after the time exits, nor are they allowed to build (on previous prayer) if the time exits while they are in prayer, because permissibility of these is established for a new occurring nullifier, not for the previous nullifier. By exit of time, the previous nullifier manifests. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 1/183] 'Only' - i.e., not by entry, contrary to Zufar. And not by each of them, contrary to Abu Yusuf. 'And a person does not become excused' - i.e., one afflicted with a nullifier of wudu and prayer. He used the absolute term 'prayer' but it is restricted to obligatory prayer, to avoid objection from the idle time (like between sunrise and zawal) which is a time for non-obligatory prayer, i.e., Eid and Duha. So if the excuse covers that time, he does not become excused. Likewise, if a break covers it, it is not recovery. And 'this' - i.e., the mentioned condition of coverage - is absolute, whether actual (the excuse exists throughout the time) or constructive (the excuse breaks for a short time insufficient for purification and prayer). This is a condition for being considered excused initially.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah states the rulings for a person with a chronic excuse (ma'dhur) that prevents complete purity, such as istihadah (chronic non-menstrual bleeding), urine incontinence (sals al-bawl), or chronic diarrhea (istitlaq al-batn). The author first distinguishes istihadah from menstruation: its blood is from a vein, not the uterus, and has no odor. It does not prevent prayer, fasting, or intercourse. The core ruling: such a person must perform fresh wudu for each obligatory prayer time (not for each prayer). With that wudu, they can pray any number of obligatory or supererogatory prayers during that time. The wudu is nullified only when the time exits (according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). The condition for being considered excused is that the excuse must be continuous throughout a complete prayer time (like Zuhr time) with no break long enough to perform wudu and prayer (about 5-10 minutes estimated). If the excuse stops for that long, the person is no longer 'excused' and must perform wudu normally. The passage also details an intra-Hanafi dispute: Zufar holds that wudu is nullified upon entry of the time, Abu Yusuf that it is nullified at both entry and exit. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is shown in two cases: if the person performs wudu after sunrise, they can pray Zuhr with it according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but not according to Abu Yusuf and Zufar. If they wudu before sunrise, their wudu is broken at sunrise according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but not according to Zufar. The passage clarifies that the attribution to time is metaphorical; the real cause is the previous hadath manifesting at that moment.

Key Terms
المعذور (al-ma'dhur): A person with a chronic excuse that prevents normal purification, such as constant bleeding, urine incontinence, or diarrhea.
الاستحاضة (al-istihadah): Chronic non-menstrual bleeding from a vein (not the uterus); it has no odor and does not prevent prayer, fasting, or intercourse.
سلس البول (sals al-bawl): Urinary incontinence – continuous dripping of urine due to weakness in the bladder or excessive coldness.
ثمرة الخلاف (thamarah al-khilaf): The practical consequence or difference that results from a legal dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), when is the wudu of a ma'dhur nullified?
A) Upon entry of the prayer time
B) Upon exit of the prayer time
C) At both entry and exit
D) After completing each prayer

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi position is that the ma'dhur's wudu is nullified only by the exit of the prayer time, not by entry; this is the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Rulings of the Excused Person (Ma'dhur): When Does Wudu Break?
Conditions and intra-Hanafi dispute on wudu of the excused

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the conditions for being a ma'dhur in the Hanafi school and apply the intra-Hanafi dispute on wudu nullification to determine validity at different prayer times.

Core Idea
A ma'dhur's wudu breaks only at time exit (Abu Hanifa & Muhammad) not at entry.

This lesson explores the concept of the excused person (ma'dhur) in Hanafi fiqh—someone with a continuous impurity like chronic nosebleeds. We will examine the conditions to be considered excused, and more importantly, an intra-Hanafi dispute on when such a person's wudu becomes invalid. Understanding this dispute will help you apply the correct ruling in practical scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of ma'dhur
Identify who qualifies as ma'dhur and the condition of encompassing (istiy'ab) a complete prayer time.
The excuse must exist continuously or with minimal interruption.
2
Learn the general ruling on wudu of ma'dhur
The wudu remains valid for the entire prayer time and they can pray any prayers.
Wudu is invalidated if a new event occurs.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Contrast the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad (exit only), Zufar (entry only), and Abu Yusuf (both).
Note the thamarat al-khilaf (practical difference).
4
Understand the rationale behind attributing nullification to time boundaries
Scholars used time boundaries for ease; in reality, the previous event becomes manifest at those moments.
This affects rulings like wiping over khuffs after time exit.
5
Apply the ruling to specific scenarios
Given a case (e.g., wudu after sunrise for Zuhr), determine validity based on each imam's view.
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

أي لعذره
الاستيعاب
لوقت كل فرض الا لكل فرض ولا نفل] قال في "البدائع": وإنما تبقى طهارة صاحب العذر في الوقت إذا لم يحدث حدثاً آخر، أما إذا أحدث حدثاً آخر فلا تبقى، كما إذا سال الدم من أحد منخريه فتوضأ، ثم سال من المنخر الآخر، فعليه الوضوء؛ لأن هذا حدث جديد لم يكن موجوداً وقت الطهارة، فأما إذا سال منهما جميعا فتوضأ ثم انقطع أحدهما، فهو على وضوئه ما بقي الوقت. [البحر الرائق: ٤٣٢/١] من الفرائض إلخ: لا يراد به الحصر بل يصلون النذور والواجبات أيضًا ما دام الوقت باقيا عندنا. [العناية: ١٥٩/١] بخروج الوقت: أي يبطل وضوؤهم بخروج الوقت فقط، وهو قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد، وقال زفر: يبطل بالدخول فقط، وقال أبو يوسف يبطل بكل واحد منهما، وثمرة الخلاف تظهر في موضعين أحدهما: إذا توضؤوا بعد طلوع الشمس لهم أن يصلوا به الظهر عندهما، وعند أبي يوسف وزفر ليس لهم ذلك والثاني: إذا توضؤوا قبل طلوع الشمس انتقض طهارتهم بطلوع الشمس عندهم وعند زفر لا تنتقض [تبيين الحقائق: ۱۸۲/۱] ثم إنما يبطل بخروجه إذا توضؤوا على السيلان أو وجد السيلان بعد الوضوء، أما إذا كان على الانقطاع ودام إلى خروج الوقت، فلا يبطل بالخروج ما لم يحدث حدثا آخر أو يسيل. [البحر الرائق: ٤٣٤/١] ثم اعلم أن مشايخنا صر أضافوا انتقاض الطهارة إلى خروج الوقت أو دخوله ليسهل على المتعلمين وإلا فلا تأثير للخروج والدخول في الانتقاض حقيقة وإنما يظهر الحدث السابق عنده ولهذا لا يجوز لهم أن يمسحوا على الخفين بعد ما خرج الوقت، وكذا لا يجوز لهم البناء إذا خرج الوقت وهم في الصلاة؛ لأن جوازهما عرف نصا الحدث الطارئ لا في الحدث السابق، وبخروج الوقت يظهر الحدث السابق. [تبيين الحقائق: ۱۸۳/۱] فقط أي لا بدخوله خلافا لزفر له ولا بكل منهما ، خلافا لأبي يوسف حه ولا يصير: أي من ابتلي بناقض الوضوء والصلاة أطلقها وهي مقيدة بالمفروضة؛ لئلا يرد عليه الوقت المهمل، كما بين الطلوع والزوال؛ فإنه وقت لصلاة غير مفروضة، وهي العيد والضحى، فلو استوعبه لا يصير معذوراً، وكذا لو استوعبه الانقطاع لا يكون برء. وهذا: أي المذكور من الاستيعاب مطلقا سواء كان حقيقياً بأن وجد العذر في جميع الوقت، أو حكميا بأن ينقطع العذر انقطاعا قليلا لا الطهارة والصلاة شرط؛ لكونه معذورا ابتداء. يسع

مبتدأ
و شرط دوامه أي حكم المعذورين يبقى إذا لم يمض عليهم وقت صلاة إلا والحدث الذي بهم يوجد فيه ولو قليلا، حتى لو انقطع وقتاً كاملاً . خرجوا عن كونهم معذورين ذلك الاستيعاب الحقيقي والحكمي.
Rulings of the Excused One: The book of purification: for the time of every obligatory prayer, and they pray with it whatever they wish of obligatory and supererogatory prayers, and their ablution is invalidated only by the exit of the time. And they also pray vows and obligatory acts. The excused persons: their ablution is invalidated only by the exit of the time. And one does not become excused until the excuse encompasses a complete time period in which there is no interruption sufficient for ablution and prayer. This is a condition for its establishment. [Commentary:] 'For his excuse.' 'The encompassment of the time of every obligatory prayer' is not for every obligatory prayer nor supererogatory. He said in al-Bada'i: The purity of the person with an excuse remains during the time if he does not cause another event; if he does cause another event, it does not remain, as if blood flows from one nostril and he performs ablution, then it flows from the other nostril – he must perform ablution because this is a new event that was not present at the time of ablution. But if it flows from both and he performed ablution, then one stopped, he is upon his ablution as long as the time remains. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 1/432] 'From the obligatory prayers etc.' is not intended for limitation, but they pray vows and obligatory acts as well as long as the time remains according to us. [al-Inayah 1/159] 'By the exit of the time': i.e., their ablution is invalidated only by the exit of the time, and this is the saying of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Zufar said: it is invalidated only by the entry. Abu Yusuf said: it is invalidated by each one. The fruit of the dispute appears in two places: one, if they perform ablution after sunrise, they may pray Zuhr with it according to the two, but according to Abu Yusuf and Zufar they may not. The second: if they perform ablution before sunrise, their purity is nullified by sunrise according to them, but according to Zufar it is not nullified. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 1/182] Then it is invalidated by its exit only if they performed ablution while flowing or flow occurred after ablution. But if it was intermittent and lasted until the exit of the time, it is not invalidated by exit unless another event occurs or it flows. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 1/434] Then know that our scholars attached the nullification of purity to the exit or entry of the time to make it easy for students; otherwise, exit or entry has no real effect on nullification. Rather, the previous event becomes manifest at that time. For this reason, they are not allowed to wipe over the khuffs after the time exits, nor are they allowed to build upon their prayer if the time exits while they are praying, because permissibility is defined by a new event, not the previous event, and by the exit of the time the previous event becomes manifest. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 1/183] 'Only' i.e., not by entry, contrary to Zufar, and not by either, contrary to Abu Yusuf. 'And one does not become excused' i.e., one afflicted by a nullifier of ablution and prayer – [the prayer] is left general but is restricted to obligatory prayer, lest there be a problem with the idle time, as between sunrise and noon, for it is time for non-obligatory prayer, i.e., Eid and Duha. So if it encompasses it, he does not become excused. Similarly, if the interruption encompasses it, it is not recovery. 'And this' i.e., the mentioned encompassment is absolute, whether real (the excuse exists in all of the time) or legal (the excuse is interrupted by a small interruption that does not suffice for ablution and prayer) – it is a condition for being considered excused initially. It is sufficient. And the condition for its continuance is its existence in every subsequent time even once. And the condition for its cessation and the person exiting from being excused is a complete time free from it. ['Wa siliyya'?] And the condition for its continuance: the ruling of the excused remains if no prayer time passes except that the event exists in it, even a little, until if it stops for a complete time, they exit from being excused – that full encompassment, real and legal.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah, with commentary from multiple sources, explains the rulings of a person with a chronic excuse (ma'dhur) such as continuous bleeding. The key points:

1. An excused person's wudu remains valid for the entire time of a fard prayer, and they can pray any prayers (fard, sunnah, nadhr) with that wudu. The wudu is invalidated only by the exit of that time.

2. To be considered excused (a condition for initial establishment), the excuse must encompass a complete prayer time without an interruption equal to the time needed for wudu and the fard prayer. This can be real (continuous) or legal (interruption shorter than wudu+prayer).

3. For continuance of the ruling, the excuse must exist in every subsequent prayer time at least once. If a complete prayer time passes without the excuse, the person is no longer excused.

4. Intra-Hanafi dispute: According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the wudu invalidates only at the exit of the time. Zufar says only at the entry. Abu Yusuf says at both entry and exit. The practical difference: if one makes wudu after sunrise, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad allow praying Zuhr with that wudu, while Abu Yusuf and Zufar do not. If one makes wudu before sunrise, Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf say the wudu nullifies at sunrise; Zufar says it remains.

5. The nullification by exit applies only if the flow was present after wudu. If the excuse was intermittent and stopped before exit, the wudu remains valid until a new event or flow.

6. Our scholars attributed nullification to time boundaries for pedagogical ease; in reality, the previous event becomes manifest at those times. Thus, after time exit, one cannot wipe over khuffs or continue a prayer interrupted by the time exit, because those rulings are based on the absence of a new event, not the manifestation of a previous one.

7. The prayer referred to in the condition is the obligatory prayer, not supererogatory, so time between sunrise and noon (for Duha/Eid) does not count.

Key Terms
المعذور (al-ma'dhur): A person with a continuous excuse (e.g., chronic nosebleed, urinary incontinence) that prevents them from maintaining purity.
الاستيعاب (al-istiy'ab): The condition that the excuse must be present throughout a complete prayer time (real or legal) for the person to be considered excused.
ثمرة الخلاف (thamarat al-khilaf): The practical consequence of a legal disagreement among schools or within the madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, when does the wudu of a ma'dhur become invalid?
A) At the entry of the prayer time
B) At the exit of the prayer time
C) At both entry and exit
D) Only if a new event occurs

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that a ma'dhur's wudu expires only at the exit of the prayer time, not at entry or both.

Conditions for Continuity and Cessation of the Excused Person's Status
Defines the conditions for continuity and cessation of the excuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for continuity and cessation of the ma'dhur's excuse and apply them to determine when the excuse is maintained or lost.

Core Idea
The excuse continues only if the impurity occurs in every prayer time; it ceases after one complete time free of it.

This lesson examines the precise legal definition of a 'ma'dhur' (excused person) according to the Hanafi school. The text from Nur al-Idah clarifies when the excuse remains valid and when it ends. Understanding these conditions is crucial for determining the rulings of wudu and salah for those with chronic impurities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
The passage states two conditions: one for continuance (the impurity exists in every prayer time, even once) and one for cessation (a complete prayer time free of the impurity).
The phrase 'even if once' is critical: only presence, not quantity, matters.
2
Define a 'complete prayer time'
In Hanafi fiqh, a 'prayer time' refers to the full duration from its start to its end. A complete time without impurity means the entire time is free.
This is the standard Hanafi definition; other schools may use different time units.
3
Apply the conditions to a case
Consider a ma'dhur with chronic nosebleeds. If he has a nosebleed during Fajr and Zuhr, but not during Asr, he loses the excuse after Asr time passes completely without an occurrence.
The loss is immediate after the complete time elapses, not retroactive.
4
Distinguish between real and legal encompassing
The passage ends with 'real and legal encompassing'. This means the condition applies both to actual impurity and to impurity that is legally deemed present (e.g., if the person could not check).
This ensures the ruling is practical, not overly strict.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحكام المعذور. وشرط دوامه وجوده في كل وقت بعد ذلك ولو مرة، وشرط انقطاعه وخروج صاحبه عن كونه معذورا خلوّ وقت كامل عنه. وشرط دوامه أي حكم المعذورين يبقى إذا لم يمض عليهم وقت صلاة إلا والحدث الذي بهم يوجد فيه ولو قليلا، حتى لو انقطع وقتاً كاملاً خرجوا عن كونهم معذورين ذلك الاستيعاب الحقيقي والحكمي.
Rulings of the excused person. And the condition of its continuance is its existence in every time after that, even if once. And the condition of its cessation and the person exiting from being excused is a complete time free of it. And the condition of its continuance, i.e., the ruling of excused persons remains as long as no prayer time passes upon them except that the impurity that they have is found in it, even if little. So if it ceases for a complete time, they exit from being excused, that is the real and legal encompassing.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage explains the rules for a person who suffers from a chronic impurity (like continuous nosebleed or urine drip). The author, from the Hanafi school, states that for the excuse status to continue, the impurity must occur within every prayer time after the initial onset, even if only once. Conversely, the excuse ceases if there is a complete prayer time entirely free of the impurity. The commentary clarifies that the condition for continuance is that no prayer time passes without the impurity being present, even if briefly. If there is a complete time without it, the person is no longer considered excused. The term 'real and legal encompassing' refers to both actual and legal continuity.

Key Terms
المعذور (al-ma'dhur): A person who suffers from a continuous impurity (like urine drip or blood) that prevents valid wudu and salah without excuse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The excuse of a ma'dhur is conditional: it persists only as long as the impurity occurs in every prayer time, and it ends after one complete prayer time free of impurity.

The Hanafi Split on Heavy vs. Light Impurities
Intra-Hanafi dispute on criterion for heavy/light impurity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi criteria for classifying impurities as heavy or light and apply them to determine the ruling on dung of edible animals.

Core Idea
Is it heavy or light? Depends on whether texts conflict or ijtihad is allowed.

This passage from the chapter on impurities introduces a critical intra-Hanafi dispute: what exactly makes an impurity 'heavy' (ghalizah) or 'light' (khafifah)? The answer determines how meticulously one must purify, especially in everyday matters like animal dung. Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn offer distinct criteria—one based on textual contradiction, the other on the permissibility of ijtihad. Understanding this difference not only clarifies a key fiqh rule but also demonstrates how Hanafi jurists derive rulings from conflicting evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify that the dispute is over the definitional criterion for heavy vs. light impurity, not over the existence of the categories themselves.
Both sides agree on the categories; they disagree on the test.
2
Explain Abu Hanifa's criterion
Heavy impurity: proven by a nass (text) that is uncontradicted. Light impurity: two nass texts conflict on its impurity and purity, and the impurity ruling is preferred due to a preponderating factor (marjih).
Example: urine of edible animals—one hadith says avoid urine, another (story of 'Uraynis) suggests purity.
3
Explain the Sahibayn's criterion
Heavy impurity: no ijtihad is permissible on its purity (i.e., the ruling is definitive). Light impurity: ijtihad is permissible on its purity, so scholars may differ.
Ijtihad here means scholarly reasoning based on evidence, not arbitrary opinion.
4
Identify the thamarah (practical difference)
The difference appears on dung (rawth) of edible animals like cows and sheep. For Abu Hanifa, it is heavy (must be washed); for the Sahibayn, it is light (sprinkling water suffices).
The text notes that Malik considers dung pure due to common occurrence (balwa), which is a cross-madhhab perspective.
5
Apply the criteria to a new case
Given a new type of impurity, determine its category by checking whether there is uncontradicted text (Abu Hanifa) or whether ijtihad on its purity is plausible (Sahibayn).
This step requires familiarity with the relevant hadith literature and scholarly consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الأنجاس والطهارة عنها. تنقسم النجاسة إلى قسمين: غليظة وخفيفة، فالغليظة كالخمر، والدم المسفوح، ولحم الميتة، وإهابها، وبول ما لا يؤكل، ونجو الكلب، ورجيع السباع ولعابها. الأنجاس جمع نجس بفتحتين، وهو في الأصل مصدر، ثم استعمل اسماً لكل مستقذر، ويطلق على الحقيقي والحكمي، فكان ينبغي أن يقول: "باب الأنجاس الحقيقية" تعييناً للمراد، لكن لما تقدم ذكر الحكمي كان قرينة دالة على أن المراد الحقيقي، ويختص الحدث بالحكمي، والخبث بالحقيقي. [الشلبي على تبيين الحقائق: ۱۹۱/۱، مراقي الفلاح] غليظة: اعلم أنهم اختلفوا فيما يثبت به الغليظة والخفيفة، فعند أبي حنيفة الغليظة ما ثبتت نجاسته بنص لم يعارضه نص آخر يخالفه كالدم ونحوه مما لم يوجد فيه تعارض نصين والخفيفة ما تعارض النصان في نجاسته وطهارته، وكان الأخذ بالنجاسة أولى؛ لوجود المرجح، مثل بول ما يؤكل لحمه؛ فإن قوله عليه السلام: "استنزهوا من البول" يدل على نجاسته وخبر العرنيين يدل على طهارته فخف حكمه للتعارض، وعند أبي يوسف ومحمد: ما ساغ الاجتهاد في طهارته فهو مخفف؛ لأن الاجتهاد حجة في وجوب العمل به، وثمرة الخلاف تظهر في الروث والخَي والبعر ونحوها فعند أبي حنيفة مغلظة؛ لأن ما روي عنه عليه السلام من أنه ألقى الروثة، وقال: "إنها ركس" لم يعارضه نص آخر ولا اعتبار عنده بالبلوى في موضع النص كما في بول الآدمي، فإن البلوى فيه أعم، وعندهما مخففة؛ لاختلاف العلماء فيه؛ فإن مالكا يرى طهارتها؛ لعموم البلوى؛ لامتلاء الطرق بها، بخلاف بول الحمار وغيره مما لا يؤكل لحمه؛ لأن الأرض تنشفه. [الحاشية: كالخمر: هي الني? ماء العنب إذا غلى واشتد وقذف بالزبد. مراقي الفلاح قيد بالخمر؛ لأن بقية الأشربة المحرمة كالطلاء والسكر ونقيع الزبيب فيها ثلاث روايات في رواية مغلظة وفي أخرى: مخففة، وفي أخرى: طاهرة، ذكرها في "البدائع"، بخلاف الخمر، فإنه مغلظ باتفاق الروايات؛ لأن حرمتها قطعية، وحرمة غير الخمر ليست قطعية، وينبغي ترجيح التغليظ. [البحر الرائق: ٤٥١/١] والدم أي السائل من أي حيوان إلى محل يلحقه حكم التطهير [قهستاني) والمراد أن يكون من شأنه السيلان فلو جمد المسفوح ولو على اللحم، فهو نجس، أطلقه وهو مقيد بدم غير الشهيد، فإنه طاهر ولو مسفوحا مادام عليه، فلو حمله المصلي جازت صلاته [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٥٣] إلا إذا أصابه منه؛ لأنه زال عن المكان الذي حكم بطهارته (رد المحتار) ولحم الميتة: أراد بها الميتة ذات الدم؛ لئلا یرد عليه لحم السمك والجراد، وما لا نفس له سائلة. وبول إلخ أطلقه فشمل بول الصغير الذي لم يطعم، وشمل بول الهرة والفأرة، وفيه اختلاف، ويستثنى منه بول الخفاش؛ فإنه طاهر. [البحر الرائق: ٤٥٧/١] ونجو الكلب بالجيم هو ما يخرج من البطن من ريح أو غائط. (أقرب الموارد)
Chapter of impurities and purification from them. Impurities divide into two types: heavy and light. Heavy is like wine, flowing blood, meat of carrion, its skin, urine of what is not eaten, dog's stool, and predators' dung and saliva. [Then commentary: 'Anjas is plural of najis, originally a source, then used as a noun for everything filthy, and applies to real and legal. So it should have said 'Chapter of real impurities' to specify the intended, but since the legal was mentioned earlier, it is an indicator that the real is intended. Legal is specific to hadath (ritual impurity), and khabath to real impurity.' [Shalabi on Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 1:191, Maraqi al-Falah] 'Heavy': Know that they differed on what establishes heavy and light. According to Abu Hanifa, heavy is what is proven impure by a text not contradicted by another text opposing it, like blood and the like where there is no contradiction of two texts. Light is where two texts contradict on its impurity and purity, and taking impurity is preferable due to a preponderating factor, like urine of what is eaten; for his saying peace be upon him: 'Avoid urine' indicates its impurity, and the report of the Araniyyeen indicates its purity, so its rule is light due to contradiction. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: whatever ijtihad is permissible on its purity is light, because ijtihad is a proof for the necessity of acting upon it. The fruit of the difference appears in dung, etc. According to Abu Hanifa they are heavy, because what was narrated from him peace be upon him that he threw away the dung and said 'It is riks' (impure) was not opposed by another text, and he does not consider common occurrence in the place of a text, as in human urine where common occurrence is more general. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) they are light due to scholars' disagreement; for Malik sees its purity due to common occurrence because roads are filled with it, unlike donkey urine and other non-edible animals because the earth dries it. [Margin: Like wine: it is? grape juice when it boils, becomes strong, and throws foam. Maraqi al-Falah restricted to wine because other prohibited drinks like tila', sukr, and raisin infusion have three narrations: in one heavy, in another light, in another pure, mentioned in al-Bada'i', unlike wine, it is heavy by agreement of narrations because its prohibition is definitive, and the prohibition of other than wine is not definitive, and preponderance of heavy is preferred. [Bahr al-Ra'iq 1:451] And blood: i.e., flowing from any animal to a place where the ruling of purification applies? And the intended is that it is of a nature to flow; if it coagulates even if on meat, it is impure. He made it absolute and it is restricted to blood other than the martyr's for it is pure even if flowing as long as it is on him; if the praying person carries it, his prayer is valid [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 153] except if some of it gets on him because it left the place ruled pure (Radd al-Muhtar). And meat of carrion: he means carrion with blood, so as not to object fish and locust meat and what has no flowing blood. And urine etc. he made it absolute so it includes urine of a child who has not eaten food, and includes cat and mouse urine, and there is difference, and bat urine is excepted for it is pure. [Bahr al-Ra'iq 1:457] And dog's stool (najw) with jim: it is what comes out of the belly from wind or feces. (Aqrab al-Mawarid)
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on impurities and their purification. It first divides impurities into two categories: heavy (ghalizah) and light (khafifah). Examples of heavy impurities include wine, flowing blood, carrion meat and skin, urine of animals not eaten, dog stool, and predator waste and saliva. The commentary explains the linguistic meaning of 'anjas' and why the chapter title does not specify 'real' impurities—the context of the previous chapter on legal impurity (hadath) indicates that real impurities are meant. The passage then delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute about the criterion for heavy vs. light. According to Abu Hanifa, a heavy impurity is one whose impurity is established by a text (nass) that is not contradicted by another text. A light impurity is one where there are conflicting texts on its impurity and purity, and the ruling of impurity is given preference due to a preponderating factor (marjih). For example, the urine of an animal whose meat is eaten: a hadith commands avoidance of urine, indicating impurity, but another hadith (the story of the 'Uraynis) suggests purity. Due to this contradiction, the ruling is light. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani), the criterion is whether ijtihad is permissible on its purity—if so, it is light. The practical difference (thamarah) appears in the ruling on dung (rawth) of animals. For Abu Hanifa, it is heavy because a hadith about the Prophet throwing away dung and calling it 'riks' is not contradicted, and he does not consider general need (balwa) as a factor overriding a text. For the Sahibayn, dung is light due to scholars' disagreement and common occurrence. The commentary then adds detailed notes on specific items: wine is heavy by consensus, other intoxicating drinks have three narrations; flowing blood is impure except that of a martyr; carrion refers to animals with blood; urine includes that of small children and cats, but bat urine is pure; dog's stool is defined as anything from the belly (wind or feces). The passage emphasizes the importance of definitive proof (qat'iyyah) for heavy impurity.

Key Terms
النجاسة الغليظة (al-najasah al-ghalizah): Heavy impurity: either proven by an uncontradicted text (Abu Hanifa) or not subject to ijtihad on purity (Sahibayn).
النجاسة الخفيفة (al-najasah al-khafifah): Light impurity: either involves contradictory texts (Abu Hanifa) or is subject to ijtihad on purity (Sahibayn).
الروث (al-rawth): Dung of animals whose meat is eaten (e.g., cow, sheep). In this passage, it is an example of the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Ijtihad is permissible on its purity, meaning scholars can disagree about it.
D) It comes from an animal whose meat is eaten.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two distinct criteria for heavy vs. light impurity: textual contradiction (Abu Hanifa) vs. ijtihad allowance (Sahibayn), with practical consequences on purification methods.

Classification of Najasah and Excused Amounts
Defines heavy and light najasah and their excused amounts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify impurities as heavy or light according to Hanafi fiqh and apply the excused amounts (dirham for heavy, quarter for light) to determine the validity of prayer.

Core Idea
Heavy impurities are excused up to a dirham; light impurities up to a quarter of the garment or body. Above that, prayer is invalid.

A drop of urine on your sleeve—must you remove it before prayer? The Lawgiver has set clear thresholds that make purification easier. In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi classification of impurities (najasah) into heavy (mughallazah) and light (mukhaffafah) and the exact amounts that are excused. By mastering these rules, you will know when prayer remains valid without removing the impurity and when removal becomes obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the impurity source
Determine what the impurity is: human excrement, animal urine/dung, etc. The source dictates whether it is heavy or light.
Human waste is always heavy. Animal wastes vary.
2
Classify as heavy or light
Using the rules from the text, decide if the impurity is heavy (e.g., human excrement, chicken dung) or light (e.g., horse urine, urine of animals whose meat is eaten). Note intra-Hanafi differences.
Check the ikhtilaf on horse dung and urine.
3
Determine the excused threshold
For heavy impurities: if solid, measure by weight (dirham = 20 qirats); if liquid, by area (hollow of the palm). For light impurities: less than a quarter of the affected garment or body part is excused.
The quarter can be measured from the affected part, the whole garment, or the minimum garment—fatwa is on the affected part.
4
Apply to prayer validity
If the impurity is below the threshold, prayer is valid; at the threshold, it is makruh tahrimi; above, it invalidates prayer unless removed.
Consider time and congregation factors for makruh.

[حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٥٦]
وعفي: [أي عفا الشارع عن ذلك مراده من العفو صحة الصلاة بدون إزالته لا عدم الكراهة؛ لما في "السراج الوهاج" وغيره: إن كانت النجاسة قدر الدرهم تكره الصلاة معها إجماعاً، وإن كانت أقل وقد دخل في الصلاة، نظر، إن كان في الوقت سعة، فالأفضل إزالتها واستقبال الصلاة، وإن كانت تفوته الجماعة، فإن كان يجد الماء ويجد جماعة آخرين في موضع آخر فكذلك أيضًا؛ ليكون مؤدياً للصلاة الجائزة بيقين، وإن كان في آخر الوقت أو لا يدرك الجماعة في موضع آخر يمضي على صلاته ولا يقطعها، والظاهر أن الكراهة تحريمية؛ لتجويز هم رفض الصلاة لأجلها، ولا ترفض لأجل المكروه تنزيهاً. [البحر الرائق: ٤٥٤/١] قدر الدرهم وفيه تفصيل، فإن النجاسة المغلظة إن كانت متجسدة، فيعتبر قدر الدرهم وزناً، وهو عشرون قيراطا، وإن كانت مائعة، فالمعتبر مساحة، وهو قدر مقعر الكف داخل مفاصل الأصابع كما وفقه الهندواني، وهو الصحيح. وما دون ربع الثوب أي عفي ما كان من النجاسات أقل من ربع الثوب المصاب إذا كانت النجاسة مخففة. واعلم أنهم اختلفوا في كيفية اعتبار الربع على ثلاثة أقوال : فقيل : رُبع طرف أصابته النجاسة كالذيل والكم والدخريص إن كان المصاب ثوباً، وربع العضو المصاب كاليد والرجل إن كان بدنا، وصححه صاحب "التحفة" و"المحيط" و"المجتبى" و"السراج"، وفي "الحقائق : وعليه الفتوى، وقيل: ربع جميع الثوب والبدن، وصححه صاحب "المبسوط"، وقيل: ربع أدنى ثوب تجوز فيه الصلاة كالمئزر . قال الأقطع وهذا أصح ما روي فيه من غيره،
Book of Purification. 7. Impurities and purification from them. And the excrement of chicken, duck, and goose, and that which invalidates wudu when it exits from the human body. As for light impurities: horse urine, and similarly the urine of animals whose meat is eaten, and the excrement of birds not eaten. And [the lawgiver] excused the amount of a dirham from heavy impurity, and less than a quarter of the garment or body from light impurity. Commentary: Al-Iwazz (goose): with kasra and shadda on zaa: it is a duck-like bird. 'And that which invalidates wudu' etc.: meaning that which invalidates wudu when it exits – from heavy impurity, but wind is excluded because it is pure according to the correct view. The intended meaning is the real invalidator, excluding sleep and laughter during prayer, because they are not described with purity or impurity, being meanings. As for what does not invalidate, like vomit not filling the mouth, and blood that does not flow, it is pure according to the correct view. It is said that it contaminates liquids but not solids. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi with addition: 155] 'Horse urine': it is included in what precedes, but because there is a difference of opinion regarding eating its meat, it was stated explicitly, lest one might think it is included in the urine of animals whose meat is not eaten according to Imam Abu Hanifa, thus being heavy; but it is not so, for it is light according to the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). It is pure according to Muhammad, as is the urine of animals whose meat is eaten. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq with modification: 1/464] 'Urine of animals whose meat is eaten etc.' from domestic and wild cattle. It is restricted to their urine because the dung of horses, mules, donkeys, cow dung, and sheep dung are heavy impurities according to Imam Abu Hanifa, due to the lack of contradiction between the two texts; according to the two disciples they are light due to contradiction, which is more apparent due to general need. Muhammad later declared them pure. [Maraqi al-Falah: 156] Al-Tahtawi said: We do not take it, as in al-Qahistani. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 156] 'And excused': i.e., the Lawgiver excused that. What is meant by excusal is the validity of prayer without removing it, not the absence of dislike; because in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and others: If the impurity is the size of a dirham, prayer with it is disliked by consensus. If it is less, and he enters prayer, then: if there is ample time, it is better to remove it and repeat the prayer; if he will miss the congregation, and he finds water and another congregation elsewhere, then likewise, so that he performs a prayer that is definitely permissible; if it is at the end of time or he cannot catch the congregation elsewhere, he continues his prayer and does not cut it. It appears that the dislike is prohibitively disliked, because they permitted leaving the prayer for it, and one does not leave for a minor dislike. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 1/454] 'Amount of a dirham' – there is detail: If the heavy impurity is solid, then the amount of a dirham is considered by weight, which is twenty qirats; if it is liquid, then area is considered, which is the hollow of the palm inside the finger joints as verified by al-Hinduwani, and that is correct. 'And less than a quarter of the garment' i.e., impurities less than a quarter of the garment affected are excused if the impurity is light. Know that they differed on how to consider the quarter into three opinions: It is said: a quarter of the part affected, like the hem, sleeve, or opening, if the garment is affected, and a quarter of the body part affected, like the hand or foot, if it is the body. This was verified by the author of al-Tuhfa, al-Muhit, al-Mujtaba, and al-Siraj. In al-Haqa'iq: and the fatwa is upon it. It is said: a quarter of the entire garment and body, verified by the author of al-Mabsut. It is said: a quarter of the minimum garment in which prayer is permitted, like the izaar. Al-Aqta' said: this is the most correct of what has been narrated about it from others.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from Nur al-Idah on the classification of impurities (najasah) and the amounts that are excused during prayer. The author begins by listing heavy impurities: human excrement, and excrement of chicken, duck, and goose. Then light impurities: horse urine, urine of animals whose meat is eaten, and excrement of birds not eaten. The excused amount for heavy impurity is the weight or area of a dirham (approximately twenty qirats or the hollow of the palm). For light impurity, less than a quarter of the garment or body part affected is excused. The commentary clarifies exceptions, such as wind being pure, and discusses differences between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two disciples regarding horse urine and the dung of certain animals. The excused amount for heavy impurity is detailed: solid impurities are measured by weight, liquid by area. For light impurities, the quarter is considered based on the affected part, the entire garment, or the minimum garment for prayer, with the first view being preferred for fatwa.

Key Terms
النجاسة المغلظة (al-najasah al-mughallazah): Heavy impurity that invalidates wudu when it exits from the body, and includes human excrement and certain animal wastes.
قدر الدرهم (qadr al-dirham): The amount of heavy impurity that is excused: about twenty qirats in weight for solid, or the area of the hollow of the palm for liquid.
الربع (al-rub'): The quarter of a garment or body part that determines the excused amount for light najasah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the excused amount for heavy najasah when it is liquid?
A) The weight of a dirham (20 qirats)
B) The area of the hollow of the palm (inside finger joints)
C) One quarter of the garment
D) There is no excusal for liquid najasah

Key Takeaway
Heavy impurities up to a dirham and light impurities below a quarter of the affected area are excused; prayer is valid but removal is better when close to the threshold.

Rulings on Spray of Urine and Transfer of Impurity
Ruling on excused spray and impurity transfer conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the excused amount of urine spray and identify the conditions under which impurity transfers through wetness.

Core Idea
Spray of urine up to needle heads is excused; impurity only transfers when wetness can drip or a visible effect appears.

In this lesson, we examine two related rulings from Nur al-Idah: the excused spray of urine and the rules for impurity transfer via dampness. Understanding these conditions is essential for maintaining ritual purity in daily life, especially when dealing with accidental splashes or contact with impure surfaces.

Guided Path
1
Identify the excused amount
The passage states that urine spray the size of needle heads is excused, meaning washing is not required. This is due to necessity and applies even if it fills the garment.
The measure is based on the head of a common needle, not an awl.
2
Understand impurity transfer from a wet source
If a person sleeps or walks on a najis surface that is wet and the wetness transfers to the body or foot with visible effect, the body/foot becomes impure. Otherwise not.
The appearance of the effect is a condition for both sleeper and walker.
3
Apply the condition for wrapping
When a dry pure garment is wrapped in a wet impure garment, the pure garment becomes impure only if it is such that, when squeezed, it would drip. This is the view of al-Halwani.
The consideration is of the pure object (al-tahir al-muktasib) and its ability to drip.
4
Recognize wind-transported impurity
Wind carrying impurity particles (e.g., from urine or dung) does not make a garment impure unless a visible effect appears on the garment.
This distinguishes sensory contact from pure air-borne transfer.
5
Note the general rule for dry impure objects
A dry impure object (body, garment, or vessel) becomes pure by removal of the impurity, covering both heavy and light impurities.
This applies when the impurity is dry and can be simply removed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعفي رشاش بول كرؤوس الإبر، ولو ابتل فراش أو تراب نجسان من عرق نائم أو بلل قدم، وظهر أثر النجاسة في البدن ،والقدم تنجسا وإلا فلا، كما لا ينجس ثوب جاف طاهر لف في ثوب نجس رطب لا ينعصر الرطب لو عصر، ولا ينجس ثوب رطب بنشره على أرض نجسة يابسة، فتندت منه ولا بريح هبت على نجاسة، ببول أو سرقين مثلاً فأصابت الثوب إلا أن يظهر أثرها فيه، ويطهر متنجس
يابس
استثناء من كلا الصورتين النجاسة
ابتلت
= لكنه قاصر على الثوب، ولم يفد حكم البدن، فقد اختلف التصحيح كما ترى، لكن ترجح الأول بأن الفتوى عليه، وفق في "الفتح" بين الأخيرين بأن المراد اعتبار ربع الثوب هو عليه سواء كان ساترا لجميع البدن أو أدنى ما تجوز فيه الصلاة. وهو حسن جداً، ولم ينقل القول الأول أصلا. [البحر الرائق: ٤٦٣/١، رد المحتار بحذف] وعفي: أي البول المنتضح قدر رؤوس الإبر معفو عنه؛ للضرورة، وإن امتلأ الثوب أطلقه فشمل ما إذا أصابه ماء فكثر، فإنه لا يجب غسله أيضا، وشمل بوله وبول غيره وقيد برؤوس الإبر ؛ لأنه لو كان مثل رؤوس المسلة منع البحر الرائق بحذف وتصرف): ٤٦٦/١] رشاش : بالفتح ما ترشش من الدم والدمع ونحوهما. ولو ابتل إلخ أي إن نام أحد على فراش نجس أو تراب نجس وصار الفراش أو التراب مبتلاً . من عرقه، أو مشى أحد على الفراش النجس أو التراب النجس وصار الفراش أو التراب مبتلاً من بلل ،قدمه، وظهر أثر النجاسة في البدن أو القدم يحكم بنجاسة البدن والقدم، واعلم أن ظهور أثر النجاسة شرط لكلا المسألتين، أي مسألة النائم والماشي، وقيد النائم اتفاقي، فإن الحكم في المستيقظ كذلك. وإلا فلا أي وإن لم يظهر أثر النجاسة في البدن أو القدم فلا ينجس كل واحد منهما. كما لا ينجس إلخ: اعلم أنه إذا لف طاهر في نحس مبتل بماء واكتسب شيئاً، فلا يخلو إما أن يكون كل منهما بحيث لو انعصر قطر، وحينئذ ينجس الطاهر اتفاقاً، أو لا يكون واحد منهما كذلك، وحينئذ لا ينجس الطاهر اتفاقاً، أو يكون الذي بهذه الحالة الطاهر فقط، وهو أمر عقلي لا ،واقعي أو النجس فقط، والأصح عند الحلواني فيها أن العبرة بالطاهر المكتسب، فإن كان بحيث لو انعصر قطر تنجس، وإلا لا، ويشترط أن لا يكون الأثر ظاهراً في الطاهر، وأن لا يكون النجس متنجسا بعين نجاسة بل بمتنجس كما في "شرح المنية". [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٥٩ ] ويطهر متنجس إلخ : أطلق المتنجس فشمل ما إذا كان بدنا، أو ثوبا، أو آنية، والنجاسة فشملت كلا النوعين خفيفة وغليظة.
منه
And spray of urine like the heads of needles is excused. If a bed or soil that is impure becomes wet from the sweat of a sleeping person or the moisture of a foot, and the effect of the impurity appears on the body or foot, both become impure; otherwise not. Similarly, a dry pure garment wrapped in a wet impure garment that does not drip if squeezed does not become impure. A wet garment does not become impure by spreading it on dry impure ground, even if it becomes damp from it, nor from wind that blew over impurity, like urine or dung, and struck the garment, unless its effect appears on it. And a dry impure thing becomes pure... Exception from both cases: the impurity [؟] wet [؟] = but it is restricted to the garment, and does not give the ruling for the body, so the verification differs as you see, but the first is preferred because the fatwa is upon it. In al-Fath, he reconciled between the last two by saying that the quarter of the garment is what is intended, whether it covers the whole body or the minimum for prayer. That is very good, and the first opinion was not transmitted at all. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 1/463, Radd al-Muhtar with omission] 'And excused': i.e., spattered urine the size of needle heads is excused due to necessity. Even if it fills the garment, he generalized it to include if water increased on it, then washing it is not obligatory. It includes his urine and others' urine. It was restricted to needle heads because if it were like the heads of an awl, it would prevent. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq with omission and modification: 1/466] 'Rashash': with fatha, what spurts from blood, tears, and the like. 'And if it becomes wet' etc.: i.e., if one sleeps on an impure bed or impure soil and the bed or soil becomes wet from his sweat, or one walks on the impure bed or soil and the bed or soil becomes wet from the moisture of his foot, and the effect of the impurity appears on the body or foot, then the body or foot is judged as impure. Know that the appearance of the effect of impurity is a condition for both cases, i.e., the case of the sleeper and the walker. The restriction to the sleeper is incidental; the ruling for the awake person is the same. 'Otherwise not': i.e., if the effect does not appear, each does not become impure. 'Similarly, a dry pure garment does not become impure' etc.: Know that if a pure thing is wrapped in a wet impure thing and it acquires something, then either each is such that if squeezed it would drip, in which case the pure becomes impure by consensus; or neither is such, in which case it does not become impure by consensus; or only the pure is in that state, which is rationally possible but not actual, or only the impure is such. The correct view according to al-Halwani is that the consideration is of the pure that acquires; if it is such that if squeezed it would drip, it becomes impure; otherwise not. It is also required that no effect appears on the pure, and that the impure thing is not contaminated by the same impurity but by something else that is impure, as in Sharh al-Munya. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 159] 'And a dry impure thing becomes pure' etc.: He generalized the impure thing to include body, garment, and vessel, and the impurity to include both types, light and heavy.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage provides rulings on two related topics: spray of urine and the transfer of impurity through wetness. First, it states that urine spray in the amount of needle heads is excused due to necessity, even if it fills the garment; washing is not required. The commentary clarifies that this applies to all urine, not just one's own. Second, it discusses impurity transfer: if a person sleeps on a najis surface that becomes wet from sweat and the effect appears on the body, the body becomes impure; otherwise not. Similarly, walking with wet feet on a najis surface with visible effect causes impurity. The same principle applies to garments: a dry pure garment wrapped in a wet impure garment does not become impure unless moisture transfers when squeezed. A wet garment on dry impure ground does not become impure unless the effect appears. Wind carrying impurity particles does not cause impurity unless visible. The passage ends with a general rule that a dry impure object becomes pure by removal of the impurity, covering body, garment, and vessel, for both heavy and light impurities.

Key Terms
رشاش (rashash): Spray or spatter of urine, blood, tears, etc. that is excused when minimal.
الطاهر المكتسب (al-tahir al-muktasib): The pure object that acquires moisture from a wet impure object; its impurity depends on whether it would drip if squeezed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition does a dry pure garment become impure when wrapped in a wet impure garment?
A) Always, because it is in contact with impurity
B) Only if the pure garment, when squeezed, would drip
C) Only if the impure garment is wet enough to drip when squeezed
D) Never, because the garment is dry

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school excuses minimal spray of urine due to necessity, and impurity transfer requires wetness that can drip or a visible effect.

Ruling on Excused Urine Spray (Rashash al-Bawl)
Ruling statement on excused urine spray

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on urine spray of needle head size and identify the conditions for its excusal.

Core Idea
Urine spray up to the size of a needle head is excused on garments—it does not invalidate prayer.

This passage from Nur al-Idah presents the Hanafi ruling on small amounts of urine spray. A common practical issue is that after using the toilet, some splashes may land on one's clothes. This lesson clarifies when such impurity is overlooked and does not affect the validity of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text states that urine spray (rashash) of a specific size is excused (ma'fu 'anhu). This means the impurity is not required to be washed off for prayer to be valid.
The ruling is an exception to the general rule that najasah must be removed for prayer.
2
Determine the size threshold
The maximum excused size is the heads of sewing needles (ru'us al-ibar). This is a very small amount.
There is a dispute among Hanafis about the precise size; the fatwa is on the smallest measure.
3
Note the scope of the ruling
The ruling primarily applies to the garment (thawb). There is an internal Hanafi dispute whether it also applies to the body; the preferred view (mufta bihi) limits it to garments.
If the spray lands on the body, most authorities require washing even if it is small.
4
Understand the legal reason
The excuse is due to necessity (darurah) to avoid hardship in purification, as it is difficult to completely avoid such splashes.
The impurity remains najis but is overlooked for ease.
5
Distinguish between excused and pure
The urine is not rendered pure; it is still najis. The excusal only applies within the size limit and normally only to garments.
This is a common mistake; think of it as 'overlooked' not 'cleansed'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعفي رشاش بول كرؤوس الإبر استثناء من كلا الصورتين النجاسة ابتلت = لكنه قاصر على الثوب، ولم يفد حكم البدن، فقد اختلف التصحيح كما ترى، لكن ترجح الأول بأن الفتوى عليه، وفق في "الفتح" بين الأخيرين بأن المراد اعتبار ربع الثوب هو عليه سواء كان ساترا لجميع البدن أو أدنى ما تجوز فيه الصلاة. وهو حسن جداً، ولم ينقل القول الأول أصلا. [البحر الرائق: ٤٦٣/١، رد المحتار بحذف] وعفي: أي البول المنتضح قدر رؤوس الإبر معفو عنه؛ للضرورة، وإن امتلأ الثوب أطلقه فشمل ما إذا أصابه ماء فكثر، فإنه لا يجب غسله أيضا، وشمل بوله وبول غيره وقيد برؤوس الإبر ؛ لأنه لو كان مثل رؤوس المسلة منع البحر الرائق بحذف وتصرف): ٤٦٦/١] رشاش : بالفتح ما ترشش من الدم والدمع ونحوهما.
And the spray of urine the size of needle heads is excused. Exception from both images: If the impurity becomes wet? But it is limited to the garment, and does not convey the ruling of the body; the correction has differed as you see, but the first is preferred because the fatwa is upon it. He reconciled in al-Fath between the last two that what is meant is considering a quarter of the garment is upon him, whether it covers the whole body or the minimum in which prayer is permissible. This is very good, and the first opinion was not reported at all. Even if the garment becomes saturated, it includes if water touches it and increases, then washing it is not required. It includes his urine and that of others. It is limited to needle heads because if it were like the heads of a needle (large), it would prevent. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq abridged and modified: 1/466] 'Rashash' with fatha: what sprinkles from blood, tears, and the like.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on excusable amounts of urine spray. The text first states the general ruling: urine spray of the size of needle heads is excused. The commentary then notes a marginal discussion about the condition of the impurity becoming wet and whether it applies only to garments. The preferred opinion is that the fatwa is on the first view. The commentator from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains that the excuse is due to necessity. Even if the garment becomes saturated, no washing is required. The ruling applies to both one's own urine and others'. The limit is set to needle heads; if it were larger, it would not be excused. The word 'rashash' is defined linguistically as what sprinkles from blood, tears, etc.

Key Terms
رشاش (rashāsh): Sprinkles or spray of liquid, in this context urine spray.
رؤوس الإبر (ru'ūs al-ibar): Literal 'heads of needles' - a measure of size for excusable impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Condition for Impurity Transmission from Impure Surfaces
Ruling with condition for impurity transmission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for a person's body or foot becoming impure from contact with an impure surface, and apply it to determine impurity in specific scenarios.

Core Idea
Impurity transmits to the body only if its trace appears; dry contact or wetness without trace does not transfer najasah.

In this passage, the author of Nur al-Idah explains a key principle in Hanafi taharah: impurity does not automatically transfer upon contact. Instead, a specific condition must be met—the visible trace of the impurity must appear on the body. This lesson breaks down that condition and its application to both sleeping on an impure bed and walking on impure ground.

Guided Path
1
Identify the action and the surface
Consider the two actions: sleeping on an impure bed and walking on impure ground. The surface is the source of impurity.
2
Check for wetness
The surface must become wet from the person's sweat (sleeper) or foot moisture (walker). Dry contact is not discussed here.
3
Observe the trace (athar)
After wetting, look for the appearance of the impurity's trace (color, smell) on the body or foot. This is the critical condition.
4
Derive the ruling
If trace appears: body/foot becomes impure. If not: remains pure. The text explicitly states 'otherwise not'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ابتل فراش أو تراب نجسان من عرق نائم أو بلل قدم، وظهر أثر النجاسة في البدن ،والقدم تنجسا وإلا فلا، ولو ابتل إلخ أي إن نام أحد على فراش نجس أو تراب نجس وصار الفراش أو التراب مبتلاً . من عرقه، أو مشى أحد على الفراش النجس أو التراب النجس وصار الفراش أو التراب مبتلاً من بلل ،قدمه، وظهر أثر النجاسة في البدن أو القدم يحكم بنجاسة البدن والقدم، واعلم أن ظهور أثر النجاسة شرط لكلا المسألتين، أي مسألة النائم والماشي، وقيد النائم اتفاقي، فإن الحكم في المستيقظ كذلك. وإلا فلا أي وإن لم يظهر أثر النجاسة في البدن أو القدم فلا ينجس كل واحد منهما.
And if a bed or two impure earths become wet from the sweat of a sleeper or moisture of a foot, and the trace of impurity appears on the body and foot, they become impure; otherwise not. 'And if it becomes wet...' means that if someone sleeps on an impure bed or impure earth and the bed or earth becomes wet from his sweat, or someone walks on the impure bed or impure earth and the bed or earth becomes wet from the moisture of his foot, and the trace of impurity appears on the body or foot, then the body and foot are judged to be impure. Know that the appearance of the trace of impurity is a condition for both cases, i.e., the case of the sleeper and the walker. The qualification of sleeper is occasional; the ruling for the awake person is similar. 'Otherwise not' means that if the trace of impurity does not appear on the body or foot, neither becomes impure.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with explanation of the condition for impurity transmission. The matn states that if a person sleeps on an impure surface and his sweat makes it wet, or if he walks on impure ground and the moisture of his foot wets it, and the trace of the impurity becomes visible on his body or foot, then they become impure. The commentary emphasizes that the appearance of the trace is a necessary condition for both scenarios. The qualification of the sleeper is not restrictive; the same ruling applies to an awake person. If the trace does not appear, no impurity is transmitted.

Key Terms
أثر النجاسة (athar al-najāsah): The visible trace of the impurity, such as color, smell, or any evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does a person's foot become impure from walking on impure ground?
A) Always when the foot is wet.
B) Only if the foot becomes wet and the trace of impurity appears.
C) Only if the impurity is dry.
D) Never, because walking does not transfer impurity.

Key Takeaway
Impurity transfers to the body from an impure surface only when the trace of that impurity becomes visible on the body—this is the decisive condition in the Hanafi school.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Conditions for Impurity Transmission Between Cloths
Condition-based ruling on impurity transmission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a dry pure cloth becomes impure when wrapped in a wet impure cloth, and apply al-Halwani's criterion to determine impurity.

Core Idea
Impurity transfers only if the pure cloth would drip when wrung after contact.

This passage from Nur al-Idah explains a nuanced Hanafi ruling on how impurity transmits between cloths. It clarifies that mere contact with a wet impure cloth does not automatically render a pure cloth impure; instead, a specific condition of moisture transfer must be met. The commentary provides a detailed breakdown of four possible scenarios and resolves the ruling by focusing on the absorbent capacity of the pure cloth. Understanding this condition prevents both overly strict and overly lenient rulings in daily taharah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and default ruling
The act is wrapping a dry pure cloth in a wet impure cloth. The default ruling from the matn is that the pure cloth remains pure unless a specific condition is met.
The matn gives examples: even spreading a wet cloth on dry impure ground or wind blowing impurity does not render it impure unless a trace appears.
2
Understand the key condition 'yan'aṣiru'
The Arabic term 'yan'aṣiru' means 'it would drip if wrung'. This indicates sufficient moisture transfer. The passage uses this as the benchmark for impurity transmission.
This condition applies to both cloths: if either would drip when wrung, moisture transfer is possible.
3
Analyze the four scenarios
The commentary lists four possibilities: (1) both cloths would drip – pure becomes impure by agreement; (2) neither would drip – no impurity by agreement; (3) only the pure would drip – a theoretical case rarely occurring; (4) only the impure would drip – the disputed case.
Scenarios 1 and 2 are agreed upon; scenario 3 is unrealistic; scenario 4 is where ikhtilaf occurs.
4
Apply al-Halwani's criterion
Al-Halwani holds that the criterion is not the impure cloth's wetness but the pure cloth's absorbency: if the pure cloth would drip when wrung after contact, it becomes impure; otherwise it remains pure.
This is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position according to the sharh.
5
Note additional conditions
Two further conditions from the sharh: (a) the trace of impurity must not be apparent on the pure cloth (if visible, it is impure regardless); (b) the impure cloth must be mutanajjis (impure through a secondary impurity), not a source impurity like urine itself.
These conditions prevent false positives and align with other rulings on taharah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كما لا ينجس ثوب جاف طاهر لف في ثوب نجس رطب لا ينعصر الرطب لو عصر، ولا ينجس ثوب رطب بنشره على أرض نجسة يابسة، فتندت منه ولا بريح هبت على نجاسة، ببول أو سرقين مثلاً فأصابت الثوب إلا أن يظهر أثرها فيه، كما لا ينجس إلخ: اعلم أنه إذا لف طاهر في نحس مبتل بماء واكتسب شيئاً، فلا يخلو إما أن يكون كل منهما بحيث لو انعصر قطر، وحينئذ ينجس الطاهر اتفاقاً، أو لا يكون واحد منهما كذلك، وحينئذ لا ينجس الطاهر اتفاقاً، أو يكون الذي بهذه الحالة الطاهر فقط، وهو أمر عقلي لا ،واقعي أو النجس فقط، والأصح عند الحلواني فيها أن العبرة بالطاهر المكتسب، فإن كان بحيث لو انعصر قطر تنجس، وإلا لا، ويشترط أن لا يكون الأثر ظاهراً في الطاهر، وأن لا يكون النجس متنجسا بعين نجاسة بل بمتنجس كما في "شرح المنية". [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٥٩ ]
Just as a dry pure garment does not become impure when wrapped in a wet impure garment that does not drip if wrung, nor does a wet garment become impure by spreading it on dry impure ground even if it becomes damp from it, nor by a wind that blew over impurity, like urine or dung, and then hit the garment, unless its trace appears in it. 'Just as it does not become impure...' etc: Know that if a pure thing is wrapped in an impure thing moist with water and acquires something, it is either that both are such that if wrung they would drip, in which case the pure becomes impure by agreement; or neither is such, in which case it does not become impure by agreement; or only the pure is such, which is a rational non-actual case; or only the impure is such. The correct view according to al-Halwani is that consideration is given to the pure (absorbent) garment: if it is such that if wrung it would drip, then it becomes impure; otherwise not. And it is necessary that the trace not be apparent in the pure, and that the impure not be impure by a source of impurity but rather by something that became impure, as in Sharh al-Munya. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 159]
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on impurity transmission when a dry pure cloth is wrapped in a wet impure cloth. The matn states that the pure cloth does not become impure if the wet cloth does not drip when wrung. Similarly, a wet cloth spread on dry impure ground does not become impure, nor does a wind carrying impurity render a cloth impure unless the trace appears. The commentary provides a detailed analysis of the conditions. It distinguishes four scenarios: both cloths are capable of dripping (then agreement: pure becomes impure), neither is capable (no impurity), only the pure is capable (unrealistic), or only the impure is capable. The correct view, according to al-Halwani, is to consider the absorbent capacity of the pure cloth: if it would drip when wrung, it becomes impure; otherwise not. Additionally, the trace must not be visible on the pure cloth, and the impure cloth must be impure through a non-source impurity (mutanajjis).

Key Terms
ينعصر (yan'aṣiru): To be such that liquid can be squeezed out; used as a condition for impurity transmission.
متنجس (mutanajjis): Something that has become impure through contact with a source of impurity, not the source itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Halwani's view, when does a dry pure cloth become impure after being wrapped in a wet impure cloth?
A) Always, if the impure cloth is wet.
B) Only if the impure cloth would drip when wrung.
C) Only if the pure cloth would drip when wrung after contact.
D) Only if both cloths would drip when wrung.

Key Takeaway
A pure cloth becomes impure only if, after contact with a wet impure cloth, it would drip when wrung – based on al-Halwani's criterion.
